O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	You, my very dear children, I have completed this book which is the last of medical science, its fulfillment, and have finished it through its explanations and declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in a vision that I should complete this for you with this treatise, which is the beginning of the work of hands, namely "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And since the work of hands is forbidden in our region and strange to all, the knowledge has perished and been lost, and there is nothing left from its strength except for small descriptions in ancient books about what the hands have done.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this, error and vanity have arisen, and thoughts are closed, and knowledge is distant.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	It seems to me that I will revive this treatise by organizing it according to the order of exposition and explanation, and also by summarizing; and I will bring together the forms of cautery tools and other instruments used in the work, with adjustments to the declarations and preparations, as is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And for the reason that no good masters of hands are found in our time, the art of medicine has become distant.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And he who wishes to excel in the science of anatomy, as Galen says, must know the judgment of the members, their forms and conjunctions and separations, and have knowledge of bones and nerves and blood vessels and the number of veins, and understand the movement and rest of the veins, and from where they originate.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And Hippocrates says that the name is nothing, and the work is something; especially in the art of healing.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We tell you in the introduction of this book that he who is not knowledgeable about the things mentioned above, will certainly fall into error and mislead others; as I have often seen many who undertake this science without knowledge or experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For I saw a most strange sight, where the abscess of scrofula affected the neck of a woman, and it damaged the arteries in her neck; so much blood gushed out that the woman died in the woman's hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	And I saw another strange sight where a stone was removed from the bladder of an old man, and the stone was large; it took with it a piece of the bladder, and the man bled internally for three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I had already been called to treat him, and I saw the condition of the patient and the size of the stone; if it was not removed, he would surely die.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And I saw another wonder which took in hand the care of our lord who had a broken leg, and with the break, he suffered a wound; and the ignorant healers bound the break to the wound as if by strong thread, leaving no trace of healing on the wound, and left it thus until the leg was entirely swollen and painful and came to ruin.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	They called me to come to him, and I hurried to free the leg; and when I freed it, he was at peace and did not feel any pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But every way to correct the corruption was already confirmed in that limb, and it could not be healed; and the corruption continued to spread through the member until the whole limb was completely lost.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And I also see another wonder that increases an abscess, and then it inflames due to the wickedness of its lordship.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For the ulcer, when it is free from dark humor, one should not use iron to touch it unless it is in a part of the body that allows for the complete removal of what is corrupt.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And for this reason, dear child, it is necessary that you know that the art of healing is divided into two parts: that is to say, work where there is danger in many dispositions; and I will show in each case in this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	For this reason, it is necessary for you to guard yourself carefully, so that the ignorant do not speak ill of you; take up your arms in courage, and undertake your sick with lightness and firmness, and use the best means, so that through God's grace you may attain salvation and be safe; abandon diseases filled with despair, and put away from yourselves what makes you doubt, and be sure in yourself, so that you can pass from this world to the other one in glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Galen says in no way should one pay heed to evil diseases, unless they are called foolish by the masses.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have devised this treatise according to three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapter is about fire cautery and medicinal agues, and it is ordered from the head to the feet; and about the shapes of instruments, and the tools for cautery, and everything that is necessary for the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and the use of suction cups and wounds, and the extraction of arrows, and similar things; and this chapter is ordered with the shapes of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and twists, and similar conditions; it orders the use of the primary tools up to the foot, and the forms of instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Therefore, we must remember the work and it is necessary that I mention the qualities of aid and the harm of each condition.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the qualities of aid and their harms are the longest discourse and most subtle science, revealing secrets; on these topics, the greatest sages have spoken and agreed among themselves; and for me, their words are sufficient, as I fear lengthening this discussion.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that cautery helps universally for every complexion where it has matter, whether the complexities: that is to say, a hot complexion with matter, and a dry complexion without matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In both hot and dry complexes, matter exists, some devise that cautery is great help, and others say the opposite: that cautery is useless for ailments arising from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For the nature of fire is hot, and it should not be treated with heat for a hot illness by heat or dryness; and he who says the contrary states that cautery provides great help to hot and dry ailments that come into the body.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the body of man and its moisture to the color of fire, you perceive the body is fresh.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this statement.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	Because I have found it to be true through experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And in every case, no one should employ this method except he who has tried it and knows through long experience the chapter of cautery, the diversity of human complexes, the dispositions and causes of their illnesses, and the outcomes and the passage of time; for other complexes we have only fear, especially in cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all agreed and harmonized with the cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, child, that cautery enkindles fire from secret remedies, and is of greater benefit than medicinal burning cautery.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and brings no harm but to the member that is afflicted, and does not affect any other member by name.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	Medicine that burns travels from one member to another, bringing diseases of sorrow and hindering healing; and sometimes the fire, for its nobility and the goodness of its substance, does not cause harm if it is not excessive.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And thus, I have found by experience and the long service and study that I have devoted to this art, and it is in accord with the truth of things; and for this reason I excuse the length of my words, because I do not wish to deprive you of the secret contained within fire, nor its quality of work, how it heals diseases of the body, as the philosopher demonstrates; consider it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know this, my son, that there is agreement among them as to when the cautery should be made and the prayers invoked.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	I say that cautery is appropriate at all times, because the pain and suffering caused by the disease are removed with the help of cautery; especially when cautery is for necessary and urgent pains that cannot wait until a greater ill comes to the member.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And never think, dear child, as they do who are ignorant; for the disease that is healed by cautery does not relapse; and so it must be done; but it is not like what they care for, because cautery is only a medicine that alters the constitution and dries up the humors that cause pain, and acts faster than any other medicine for the sake of its value, and for the virtue of its work and authority.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And another thing that can happen is that the disease returns according to the constitution of the sick person and the place of the disease and its virtue; and superfluities accumulate in him through the acquisition of foods and similar things, unless cautery is administered where there are few superfluities and moisture, as in the cautery of deep wounds for pain and similar things, and such pain does not return; but it happens rarely.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And many people do not understand why cautery is called the last of medicine, but it is true; however, their intentions are false, and they consider cautery to be the last of medicine because when we administer treatment methods for any illness and they are ineffective, then we should resort to cautery, and it is effective.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Then it becomes clear that cautery is indeed the last resort in medicine, not at all according to the understanding of ignorant people.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The ancients said that gold cautery instruments are more effective than iron ones, and they only mentioned fire for its quality of gold and the nobility of its substance; they said that the heat from cautery does not cause putrefaction, but this is not certain, for I have tried it, and I have found that it is true in no man; and gold cautery is more effective than iron, as they say.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And still, when you heat the gold instrument, you are not sure if it is heated through by the color of the gold, and as soon as it cools down; and if you heat it too much, it will be damaged; thus there is enough hindrance.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this, we use fire cautery as we have equipped it with our tools for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Or, I have ordered this chapter at the end so that the way be lighter to find.
dou cautere olivaire	Oil cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	Fire cautery is useful for moisture and cold on the brain, and it heals two conditions caused by disease, known as "soda," and by many humors that descend to the limbs and ears, and due to numerous dreams and toothaches and throat pain, especially in all diseases arising from cold, such as paralysis and soda and apoplexy and similar illnesses.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cautery is such that the patient is cleansed by a solvent medicine, purifying the head III or IV, according to the virtue and age and habit of the patient's malady; and then the head of the patient is made to lie down.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And then make it sit crossed in your hands, and place your palms on his two legs; afterward, put the root of your palm onto the root of his thigh between his two joints; and there where your middle fingers meet, if it bleeds, heat up the cautery called "olive," which has this shape:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And mark it on the skin with ink, and repeatedly push and pull your hand, gently twisting; then lift your hand carefully, and check if you can see the bone emerge; and if not, repeat the cautery until you see the bone as I have told you. Afterward, take some string, put soft and melted butter inside, place it on the wound, and leave it for three days; then apply clean cotton until the burning sensation is gone; finally, dress the wound with "tetrafarmacy" until it heals completely.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And they say that the older the wound, the more it purifies itself; and for this reason, it needs help to heal.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And they say that one must not let the cautery burn off any part of the bone, and then remove what is burned from the bone, and it will be cured.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And another says that one must not apply the cautery too heavily, and pry so forcefully from the bone as wide as a woman's fist, so that the humors can come out; and one must keep the wound open for a long time; then one should clean it and dress it.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two methods of cautery do not seem good to me in every way, except for those who have no fear; and I think I should leave them, because the joint is weakened by continuous solutions of nature, as we witness in other members; and even when the patient's joint is weak by nature, the first appearance of cauterization seems more safe and flexible to me, and from this I act accordingly.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	from the ancient pain of the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When chronic pain in the head comes and lasts a long time, patients must use herbal remedies and pills known as "cough drops," and purgatives for the head and eyes and poultices; and if one tries the cauterization that we have mentioned above, it is of no avail.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Take care if the patient's shoulder is of strong nature and not too frozen; then cauterize it from below, just as we have said above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est I leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	After cauterizing each corner of the shoulder close to the bone, as we have said before, and cauterize the one called "vasselz" (likely referring to a specific muscle or tissue), which is where ventosas (suction cups) are placed; hold your hand lightly so as not to see the bone. The patient feels much greater pain from this cauterization than from others, and I will speak of it at that time. It is important that the cauterization of the corners be more delicate than that of the middle part of the shoulder, and this is its form.
dou cautere dou chief	For fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When in a part of the head sudden pain occurs, and the illness spreads to the oil (or possibly referring to inflammation), and the condition is purged with drugs made by skilled physicians, and all other treatments as I have mentioned in the division of illnesses, and none of these help: then perform cauterization according to two methods, that is, with hot ague medicine and fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The cauterization with hot ague medicine is when you press a warm compress on the affected area, remove the skin and clean the wound deeply, then place a poultice or cloth soaked in butter over it; leave this for 12 hours, then take it off, clean the wound thoroughly, and leave it uncovered for 2-3 days.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the treatment with medicine, as long as it is healed; and if you find yourself doing something from any burning medicines that I have written about or dosed to treat burning medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The fire cautery is done according to this manner.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the cautery instrument according to this form:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And it is called "closed" because the head is shaped like a clasp with a small amount of curvature, and in the middle there is a slight appearance; place it on the painful area, hold your hand, and gently turn it slightly until half of the thickness of the heart is burned; then remove your hand so that the artery does not burn, which is harmful, and allow an abundance of blood to flow.

de la cure de fistule par cautere	On the treatment of a fistula by cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula as we have discussed in the sections on diseases, and your treatments are ineffective, then it is necessary that you perform cauterization according to this method.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Instruct the patient to place his head in a healthy position, and hold his limbs' heads between your hands in such a way that they do not move or shift their positions; afterwards, apply moist cotton either in vinegar or in pear juice over the oil. After that, heat up the cauterizer until it is hot: shape it like a quill, so that its tip becomes the cauterizer; if you see fit, point it from one side to another, and if you prefer, make it similar to a tent; nevertheless, whatever shape it takes, it should be mobile for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	After pressing the fistula, open it and drain the pus and fluid; if it closes again, repeat the procedure and apply hot cautery; hold your hand over the cautery at the affected area above the oil, so your hand does not burn; place the cautery on the fat of the oil and corrupt (it).
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you begin the cautery close to the bone, that would be better.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If that does not work, repeat the cautery one more time, and if necessary, do it again after three days; then apply moist cotton in butter and cure the wound until it is healed, and if after forty days it is still not healed, apply a corrosive medicine to the exposed bone; and the remedy will depend on what comes in his chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a way of cautery for a fistula that no one among the ancients spoke of.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	Understand the fistula, and locate its source; then place a fine, sharp tool into the gap, thus taking on this shape:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	and it makes the quantity of a drop of blood; and hold your hand firmly with the tool, and do not move the patient in any way, so that the blood does not leave the wound; and one must put a soft cloth moistened with oil on the wound for healing or relief: the blood drops deeply into the fistula, and the healthy tissue is restored through wonderful health.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the ulcer is clean through the cautery we have described, that is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If that is not the case, it is necessary to administer heat or cold, and bring the ulcer back to the body according to what is appropriate for its own place.
des crevaices en levres	cracks in the lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Many times, cracks appear in the lips called "poil," especially on the lips of children.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these wounds as we have discussed in detail, and the cure does not benefit, then use a small surgical knife according to this form:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And insert the hospital (or dressing) into these wounds until it reaches the bottom; after that, treat the area with wax until it is healed.
de l’aposteme de la goule	from the abscess of the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When an abscess forms in the throat's root or tonsil, or on the palate, or at the roots of the teeth, it causes putrefaction and rot, becoming a fistula, and you treat it as we have discussed before, but it does not help: then you must apply cautery according to the size of the fistula. After opening or draining the fistula, hold your hand over it until the heat from the fire reaches the bottom, and do this once or twice, following the cure that we have described earlier, until it is healed; and if it heals in this way, it's good. If not, you must expose the area and remove the corrupt bone, as you will find described in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	no movement of the joints
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and treatment with medicines is ineffective, then place the patient's aching jaw in a healthy position; afterward, apply the hot cautery where the tooth's shape will appear, as you would place a cane on the tooth; and immerse the hot cautery deeply, holding your hand firmly so that the patient feels the heat reaching the root of the tooth; then release your hand and repeat the cauterization according to your desire; afterward, have the patient rinse his mouth with salty water and leave it for an hour, warming it thoroughly.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in this way, the tooth which was moving is now confirmed in place, and the gums softened are restrained, and the moisture corrupted is dried up.
de la dolor des dens	of the pain of teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When tooth pain comes from coldness or chill, and the remedies of medicine are ineffective, then cautery must be used according to these two methods: butter cautery and fire cautery.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Butter cautery is performed by pressing melted butter into a metal spoon (of iron or silver), then wrapping cotton around the tip and moistening it with butter. Apply this to the aching tooth with pressure until it becomes numb, and repeat this process several times until the numbing effect reaches the root of the tooth. If you find the butter too cold, you can place a hot iron on top while maintaining contact with the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	He uses fire cautery if it is such that you press a piece of iron or steel into the wound, and it is deep enough that the heat does not reach the patient's mouth; then, after heating the cautery, its shape will come forth, and place it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery cools; do this often, for the pain will be lessened on that day or the next.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it is necessary that the patient fill his mouth with good butter in the urgency of that cautery, and then suck out the heat; and this is the shape of the cautery.
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And perform cautery on the upper lip where you wish, and according to what you are able to do; and this is the shape of the instrument.
des scrophules	Of scrofula
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When scrofula is from cold moisture and does not obey digestion with medicines, then heat the cautery over it so that afterwards a form appears, and it has openings for the fumes to escape from the cautery of the other part; and apply hot cautery to the abscess once, as it is necessary, until it reaches the bottom of the abscess; and if the abscess is small, put cautery according to the quantity of the abscess, leaving it thus for three days; and then apply moist cotton or butter until the burn is healed; after that, cure the wound with oil and bandages until it is clean.
Li forme de la cainne:	The form of the bone.
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	When moisture conquers the channels of the body, especially when it arises from a cold complexion, then it is necessary that the patient be first relieved by solvent medicines; afterwards, he should have fire cautery at the root of the throat, and beware not to go up to the throat, and do not breathe with force but slightly.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	After that, he performs another cautery at the joint of the collarbone with the tip of the spine, and these cauteries that are called "clavicle" as we have shown before; and treat the limb as we have said before until it is healed.
de la toust	from the heat
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	When all and any disease of the pores are caused by cold moisture, and the patient has no fever or chills, and it is an old illness, then make two cauterizations on the afflicted area; and another cauterization between the two limbs; and this cauterization called 'clavile' is according to the shape as mentioned above.

Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais III a cop.	And for this reason, the cautery is lighter, because you do it three times.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	on the dislocation of the shoulder joint
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.

et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	and burn the heart as long as it feels hot, and the image of the burn would be four burns altogether; and for this reason, the burn is made with a burn instrument that has three prongs, so that the appearance of the burn is six burns; and the nerve according to the subtlety of a thread, and this is the shape of the burn with three prongs.
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce I nerf por coi il i a VIII cauteres.	And never should it be adjusted on this nerve, for which there are eight burns.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	After applying the burn, put a bandage with silk; then rest the patient, and do not move the limbs for a long time until they are well comforted.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if it is dislocated from above, this happens poorly, then apply cautery to the thick skin with a heated nail or many cauterizing pokes.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	Because the joint is closed, and the moisture is removed, and the patient is healed.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When coldness and much moisture come to the stomach while it is being stretched from its natural state, catarrh multiplies within it, and the usual remedies are ineffective, then the patient should be made to lie on his back, extending his legs and arms.

Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme; et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche; puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if you see yourself cauterized with a large cautery in the stomach according to this form; and whoever is afraid of this cautery, cauterize by poking and marking on the stomach in the amount that you see fit; then cauterize all over the cautery called "point.
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment we have previously discussed, as long as he is healthy.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez; et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil; et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient; et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi; et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere; et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez; et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais; et c’est li forme:	When the liver experiences pain from cold and moisture and excessive gas, as long as it is removed from its natural state due to excesses; and the patient is treated according to what we have mentioned in sections, but it does not help, then it is necessary that the patient be careful with his head; and a sign of this is three cauterizations according to this form and figure and quantity on the liver, removing the humors from the stomach or the intestines; and there should be enough space between each cauterization, approximately the thickness of two fingers; and the cautery should be long throughout the body, and do not press too hard with your hand over all the cauterized areas; and burn only slightly the middle part of the heart, and let the patient keep his legs straight; and if he cannot, let him lie down and stretch out his legs, easing his breath; and this is the form:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors; et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	And if you wish, cauterize these cauteries with a knife, if you are skilled and sharp in the art, and be careful not to burn all the heart, for you would scorch the whole body; and let it not come to boiling, for the veins are very delicate there, and only the wise can see.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile: s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort; et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	When there is an abscess in the liver, and you need to know if it is within the liver tissue or in the membrane: if it is in the tissue, the patient feels moderate pain; but if it is in the membrane, they feel intense pain.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste; et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	And when this cure involves the mirrors, it is necessary for the patient to rest their head; then apply a signet over the vein where the abscess is, and afterwards heat the cautery which resembles a rose, in this way:
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers; aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez; et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	And cauterize the cautery until the colors are burned, and come just to the syphag, as long as the pus is entirely hot; after the cure according to the treatment of the eschar as long as it is healed; and it is not appropriate for this cautery to be used by anyone other than those who have studied medicine extensively, and by whose hands these illnesses have been corrected in no way.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	Then he can boldly operate, but nevertheless, I still think it is better to leave it.
dou cautere de pleuresin	the cautery of tears
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	They say that one should perform cautery on the pleura with roots of the plant Aristolochia, in this way: take a long root of Aristolochia, as large as you can find it, and dry it; moisten it in oil, then apply it to the fire, and cauterize the cautery between the ribcage and collarbone, and smaller cauteries lower down on the part below the beard; cauterize between the fifth and sixth ribs, slightly leaning back; cauterize across the lower parts of the pelvis, and another one on the stomach, and between the shoulder blades, and along both sides of the lower pelvis, removing the cautery between the shoulder blades; do not press your hand, but hold it open as if smelling something.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	And they say that no ancient scholar or doctor use the fire cautery resembling a razor, and burn it, and place it between the ribs, until it reaches this abscess; and there is great pain, as we have said in the abscess of the liver.
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this case, the patients often die now, or there is an infection that cannot be healed.
de la mice	of the mouse
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent III manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you treat the disease of the mouse according to the divisions of treatment we have mentioned, and it does not benefit, then they (the healers) resort to three ways of cauterization, all of which are good.

And if you see fit, cauterize the entire cauterization with three edges.

de ydropisie	The term "ydropisie" appears to be a medieval
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	Cauterization is not effective against hydrops, except in the manner called "asclytes".
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur. de l’enfleure des piez	of the swelling of stones
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner. After that, make two cauteries on each leg, at the tip of the sharp blade; and let the cautery be deep, one on the inside of the knee joint and the other on the outside, along the leg; and leave the cauteries to heal on their own without dressing, so that the blood comes out; then follow up with the other treatments we have mentioned.
de la menoison	of the joint
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai I grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et IIII cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout I cautere clavile subtil, et II cauteres sus les hainches.	When the solution of the stomach comes from cold and moisture, so that the retentive and digestive virtues in the stomach and intestines are weakened, and cannot be cured by any means; and you see the patient suffering greatly and having great strength, then do a great cautery on the stomach according to what has been said above about cautery of the stomach, a circumferential cautery; and three cauterizations around the anus with very fine cautery, and two cauterizations on the hips.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et I cautere sus chaicun yle, et II petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see abundant moisture and the patient suffering, do a cautery on the wrist, and one cautery on each place, and three small cauterizations on the stomach to relieve the great pain, for the cure is beneficial when there is good aid.
de la cure des emorroydes	On the treatment of hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois; et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	When hemorrhoids are of long standing and consist of corrupt, cold, moist humors, they are treated as we have said in the previous divisions, but they do not benefit from cauterization. Make three incisions along the spine of the back, starting from below and moving upwards in a triangular pattern; one incision just below the anus (two incisions deep); and if you think the stomach is cold, the meat does not cook well, and swelling is visible on the face, then apply a strong cauterization to the stomach as previously mentioned, and another to the liver, and yet another to the heart, using cautery cloves; leave the cauterization open for a long time.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After treatment, reset the shoulder as long as it is healthy.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	from the fleshiness called "thelul
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou II, et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you deal with the fleshiness (thelul), if the cautery appears too sharp, cover it entirely with a hot compress; leave it until the heat reaches the vein, thereby causing the blood to flow; repeat this process once or twice, and if there is much flesh, cauterize each area as we have said. After the treatments, use beneficial remedies as long as they remain healthy; and if you cauterize with a large hot iron on the flesh, it will provide greater aid.
de plaie mal curee	from the poorly treated wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot endure cutting or opening, as we shall relate in its place, a disease arises that can only be healed by cautery.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	When a vein becomes fistulated, filled with pus and putrefied moisture, corrupting the surrounding areas, you must try every subtle remedy, and be sure to know at every step how effective it is.
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	After heating the cautery to a sharp point, insert it into the fistula according to the amount that the attempt has entered, and repeat the cauterization once, or twice, or three times, depending on the quantity required; be careful not to burn the surrounding nerves or major blood vessels.
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	It goes without saying that translating medieval medical texts can be complex and ambiguous due to the passage of time, linguistic shifts, and the specialized terminology used. de la maladie des reins	Of kidney disease
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra III cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When kidney pain accompanied by heavy urination and no ability to urinate, then it is necessary that you perform a fire cautery on the kidneys from both sides using the cautery knife that we have previously mentioned; and if we cauterize in the middle, there will be three cauteries in a row, and this will bring greater relief.
de la vessie	Of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et I a destre et I a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais I cautere defuers le dos, ou II se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is soft and weak from pain and moisture, preventing the patient from urinating, then perform a fire cautery on the outer part of the bladder where the hair begins to grow, both on the right and left side, making each cautery about as long as a finger; also perform a cautery on the back if necessary. The cautery knife should be shaped as previously described.
de la marris	Of the shoulder
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice III cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et II cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the wound is cold and moist, it does not allow anything to heal, and the flesh is corrupted and its healing is delayed; and when it comes, it causes great pain. Then it is necessary that he make three cauterizations around the wound, as we have said in the cauterization of the bladder, and two cauterizations on the back; and these cauterizations should be made with a clamp, as we have said.
de la hainche	de la hainche" translates to "of the hip
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a I cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When viscous moisture descends into the hip socket and for this reason it becomes stuck out of place, and the signs are that the thigh is longer than the other when measured together; and the nerves are found to be weakened, it is necessary that you cauterize the patient over the hip socket with a cauterization in the shape of a circle, and mark before the joint around the socket as it rotates, so that the socket stays within the circle; and the cauterization should be similar to that used for the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai III cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if this cautery is not present for you, perform three cauterizations with the great olive, and let the cauterization be just as effective as all the others; and treat until it is healed.
de la dolor de la hainche	of the pain of the back
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain arises in the back, and it is due to cold and moisture, and the patient is cured as we have stated in the previous section, but the cure is ineffective, and the illness is chronic: then you should purge the patient of thick, foul humors with bitter pills or other similar good pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	Afterward, he performs cautery; and the manner of cautery is according to two methods: that is to say, altogether burning medications, and fire cautery.
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	Fire cautery is performed in many ways, of which one is: You cauterize along the ribs, three cauteries in a triangular shape, with good depth and size, and there should be the thickness of two fingers between each cautery, making them olive-shaped. One never performs cautery directly in the middle on top of the chest, for that would result in four cauteries following this form.
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you see, cauterize with the cauterization of the circle that we have spoken of in the dislocation of the hip; but do it in such a way that the circle contains all the hip, and all the parts of the heart are burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	And this is the way it is done in sciatica, when the pain is confined to the hip and does not reach the thigh or leg.
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if the pain reaches the thigh and leg, make a second cauterization at the point where the patient feels the pain, and a third cauterization above the ankle, a little to the left; this can be done with a cutting cautery, and the thickness of the heart can be burned. If the patient feels that the pain radiates to the big toe or nearby, cauterize it at that point, three points or four with a cauterization called "point.
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if the pain is so intense in the knee and down to the thigh, he should perform cautery with a sharp or circular instrument, and be very careful in all his cauterizations that he does not leave them for too long, lest he burn the tendons and large arteries, and do the patient more harm and contraction.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	I myself have seen many who have performed cautery on the sole of the foot, leaving them for so long that the leg became completely swollen, and the feet as well, causing them to be pierced and corrupted entirely.
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	After an operation on the belly, he died.
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	And if the pain is in two parts together, apply cautery to one and the other, according to this manner.
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And the wise ones say about cautery for the spine, which is the way to do it: take a piece of iron, as thick as a new dime or slightly less, and make it notched on both sides with spaces the size of a small needle; place the notches over each other on the two parts, and they should be as even as possible, and use a good-quality piece of iron; this is its shape.
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois I cautere reont et lou laisse III jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And heat it until it is entirely red and emits steam, then place it on the spine of the ill patient, and turn to its healthy side; apply cautery once more and leave the wound for three days; then make a plaster with butter and keep the wound open for a long time; after treatment, as long as it is healed.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasim says that we should use this cautery little because of the fear of its regard, and we see few who use it; nevertheless, these are good cauteries, which he can endure, and place where he is strengthened.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi; et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	The burning medical cautery is such that you make an instrument with a descending edge along the margin of the door, and it should be made of iron or steel on a long wall, and in the center, there should be two openings, and they should be open from below and above, and join together in this form.
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche; aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	After placing the board of the hip on the sick patient lying on his side, and quickly covering your hand with the board of the hip, pour between the two circles of hot ash that is heated over the fire a little, and leave it for an hour, and let the patient suffer the heat and burn of it.
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu; et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit; et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait; et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it has a true burning sensation, just as from fire; and when the burns have passed, lift your hand with the instrument and raise the affected area gently, leaving it thus for three days, and apply butter until the blackness of the burn disappears; and let it remain in this state for three more days as the final aid after the treatment of wounds until it is healed.
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument; et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	And if the pain extends to the thigh or leg, use the instrument with gentle pressure as you did with the hand, increasing it gradually; this is the method of hot water, which I have written about in my treatise on rectifying medicine.
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	Take alkali and quicklime, equal amounts of each, crush them together, and place them in a new pot.
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir; et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main; et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	Where there is a small opening, make it larger so that the tip of a needle can enter; then place this pot into another well-sealed pot and add alkali and lime, stirring gently until two layers of powder form on top, as you hold it firmly in your hand. Leave it thus until the water and sediment at the bottom of the sealed pot settle, then take all that water and pour it over the lime and alkali as before.
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	And it will also be beneficial in many cases of medicine and other cautery treatments, as it acts like fire, and with other medicines such as fomentation, honey, anacardium, and lime with soap, all these ingredients mixed together.
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	And Galen tells us of a treatment by which one noble was cured of the pain in his back and sciatic nerve, and he said that no other remedy had been used, and that he was completely healed once this cure was performed, and he bathed as he teaches below.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie; et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	And he says to do this in the following way: you press and grind fresh and dry niter with a little fat, and apply it to the back and thigh and leg where the pain is, and wrap it; and leave it for three hours or until the patient no longer feels the burning.
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	And then make him enter into a bath as long as the body is slightly warmed, and let him enter into bed, and the pain will disappear completely and he will be healed.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And know that no one should use fire cautery with such medications unless it is after the evacuation of the body.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	And Dioscorides says that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with goat's hair, it helps a lot; and the cautery should be done in such a way.
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take lint and grease it with old oil, and apply it to the fossa between the big toe and the other toe called the falciform.
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	After taking a piece of dry goat horn, hold it in the fire until it becomes charcoal, and place it on the wound, leaving it until it is stained; repeat this process, and do not stop doing so until you think by sense that it reaches the chest, and that the pain ceases; and this way of cauterizing is called "goat horn cautery.
de la dolor dou dos	of the intense pain of the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, whether from stretching or impact or excessive evacuation, or due to some similar cold material expanding, none of these symptoms warrant cauterization, except for that which comes from the infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne V cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai III cauteres ou IIII au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary after that the patient be freed of foul pills or other similar substances, that one make them on the back, where the pain resides, three lines marked with a signet, and in each line V cauteries or more according to the virtue and quantity that the patient can endure; and the cauteries should be made according to the cautery called "point"; and if you see fit, make III cauteries or IV at the middle cautery following this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	This illness often afflicts small children, and the signs of its onset are that they have a tight and painful throat when they swallow, and weakness; you will find in the lower back a sharp pain that extends to the other spines.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this, and you observe it being cured, cauterize it with the fire cautery according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	The cautery should permeate each part of the wound equally.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you see that the cautery around the wound penetrates with two or three lines, and the points are close to each other.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	After the treatment, hold the limb until it is healthy according to what we have said, and be careful not to apply cautery to any numb areas that are affected by nerve damage.
de la dolor des jointes	from the pain of joints
