Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When the pain of joints is caused by moisture that spreads throughout each limb, and when the pain suddenly comes on, they call it "podagra" rightly so, and when it is due to a cold cause and cannot be cured by medicines, then cautery is used in this manner: make several cauteries around the joint of the foot, and let the cautery be olive-shaped according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if it is necessary to prick the sole of the foot, make a cautery in the shape of a 'dot'.
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if the pains come up to the knees and other joints, this happens often, so he applies fire to each knee three times or four times with olive oil; and if you need more, you can do so, but don't hold your hand too tight until the desired heat is reached.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend to the knee and back, he administers the fire we have mentioned in his chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	And if the pains are in the hands, you make two cuts around the bones; and if there is no pain left in the fingers, you apply fire to each joint and to each hair of the hand; and if the pains come up to the elbows or shoulders, you cauterize each part, and take good care of the patient and apply medicines.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you govern it well and drain the humors, it will be healed by God's help.
de la routure dou syfac	Of the dislocation of the shoulder
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When the dislocation occurs suddenly, the muscles contract and it is necessary, when you attempt to cure it, not to move the shoulder that day; and it should use things that relax the abdomen, so that the intestines descend from the abdominal cavity. After that, lay it on its back between your hands, and command the patient to keep his breath until the muscles are repaired, and align them properly, and sign below the dislocation on the bone of the forearm, and make a mark in the shape of half a circle above the body; then take the fire cautery according to this form.
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	as long as it is white and it sheds scales.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Then reset the bones to their proper place; and have the attendants lay their hands so that they do not return to their previous position; and open the patient's thighs well, and place pillows and assistants on his thighs, and another one on his buttocks, which holds his hands; then apply the cautery to the sign over your entire hand, holding it straight and firm until you reach the bone, and if you do not touch the bone on the first attempt, repeat the process again until you do; be careful that the bone does not move when applying the cautery; do not burn him; and ensure that the patient does not die or suffer any other harm.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And know that if you do not go close to the bone with cautery, your efforts are in vain.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And it is necessary that the cautery of children be subtle according to their size, and of large people as large according to their measure; after three days, treat the wound with butter until the scald is healed; afterwards, cure other wounds until they are clean, and let the patient lie on his back for forty days until the wound is well sealed; and it is necessary that his movements be restricted for a long time, so that the boils do not appear when he moves to his chamber.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	And after forty days, when he wishes to rise, a well-made bandage is applied to him for another forty days; and he should have good rest, working little and guarding against too much drinking and eating, and excessive noise; and by following this instruction, he will be completely healed.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And now I will describe the treatment for cutting in his chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of the rupture of the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	When ruptures occur in other stomachs and are known to not grow any further, hold the cautery near the wound according to its size, and burn it with a third of the heart's beat; after treatment as we have said; and no old ones said that one must cauterize at three angles with this form:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	but first mark the place with a sign of iron and make a line across the width above the fracture, and another beyond it, and hold your hand firm over all the cautery claw.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cautery is lighter and more gentle.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of ancient pain in any member
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain arises in any member, either from falling or injury, and this pain persists for a long time, and medical treatment is ineffective, then it should be cauterized with the cautery called "point," and the cautery should be applied according to the length of the member, its smallness, weakness, strength, and the location of the twist, as well as its pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If he is healthy after the first cautery, that is good; if not, begin another cautery on that part, for it often happens that it must move in the limb next to it, so you must perform cauteries until the patient is cured.
de meselerie	It seems like there might have been a slight error in the
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	These conditions are never helped by a single cautery; especially the illness that arises from the putrefaction of fluids and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	You must observe it being cauterized, take care if the illness is in its beginning, and if it is cured according to what we have said in the previous section, and do not delay or hesitate, and doubt that the corruption does not spread throughout the patient; then perform V cauteries on the head: I on the crown, II on each horn, and one behind at the nape; and leave your hand such that the cautery reaches the bone, and until the skin is removed so that the vapors of the thick humors can escape; and cauterize the mouse according to what is necessary.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et I cautere en som lou neis, et II cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et VI cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et I grant sus la crupie et I autre delez, et II sus les II espaules; et II sus les coutes, et II sus les tendrons dou pis, et I sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et I autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et I autre sus lou foie.	And if the disease is widespread, it becomes evident that you must cauterize these cauteries we have mentioned in the beginning, and cauterize in some places near the neck, and cauterize on the spine of the back, and six times on the spine of the hip, and one greatly on the knee, and another gently on the shoulder; and two on the elbows, and two on the tender parts of the pis (toe), and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the cavities of the hands; and beware of the nails that are on the last toe, so as not to burn them. Never make a cautery on the bone of the wrist, or another on the stomach bone, or one on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And know that the more you perform cautery, the greater the aid it provides and the more beneficial it becomes; and understand that the patient feels no pain from cautery as the healthy do, because the body is already corrupted.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it is necessary that the cautery be great and small according to the members and joints, as you will find in the ways of iron.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After treatment, wash the wound with wheat flour mixed with honey and other remedies until it is healed.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When swelling appears in any member and is cured by medicines, oils, and bandages, but there is no improvement, then make a cautery on the member according to its size and the extent of the problem; and this cautery should be somewhat penetrating towards the heart; then apply treatment with ointments until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And never should a cautery be performed on the hand, foot, or back, at the point where a nerve controls the member, and thus if the swelling is removed; nevertheless, no one should attempt this unless they are knowledgeable about the members and the paths of the moving nerves in the body.
de albaras	Of albars (or albaras)
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" is ignited, and the medical skill is useless, then cauterize it with a hot iron slightly, according to the quantity of the affected part, until the whiteness is removed, and its color changes; then cure it with flour of rice and lentils mixed with rose oil and plantain leaves, and collyry (eye drops) made from mullein and alder, each in a portion; mix them together, wrap them in a cloth, and apply to the affected area until it is healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The treatment of the chancre (a type of ulcer or sore) with cauterization:
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When a ulcer appears at the beginning, and you wish to stop it, cauterize it with the cautery that seems like a circle around the entire edge of the ulcer.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	Yet wise men say that one should also cauterize in the middle of the ulcer; however, I do not find this good, as I fear it may become ulcers and corrupted, and I have never seen it work well; and a more correct thing is that it should be cauterized around, in the cautery called "circle," as we have said about many cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling that cannot die
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	When anyone has a disease called "adubelati," and it does not yield to death or because of the excess it causes, or due to old age and the weakness of the patient when there is little blood, or for the time; and you see it hastening to die: then cauterize around with many small cautery burns in piercing; after which leave it thus.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	Because it will hasten to die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it piercing through all the cautery, make the cautery so hot that this is how it looks:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And place your hand in the middle of this illness called 'adubelati' as long as the cautery perceives the heart, and be such a cautery that the patient feels released in this way so that the course of putrefaction is eliminated.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	After the treatment, as long as it is completely healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	Heal the fire with iron.
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another type of illness is called 'corrodens', which is nothing other than a corruption of the member, as it destroys the members just as fire dries the wood.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	If you see this disease in a limb that can be treated with fire cautery, then heat the cautery instruments both small and large, according to what is suitable for the limb or the disease; after cauterizing from all sides until you have eliminated all the corruption, leave nothing of it, so that everything that is corrupted is removed.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	Then leave it for three days, and apply oil to the cauterized limbs that are suffering from burns until all the scalds from the fire are eliminated, and all the corruption.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the treatment of wounds that cause pain.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	And if after three days the wound does not heal, it is good; and if not, recommence the cautery on that which remains stuck in the corrupted joint.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	And this method is sometimes effectively treated with hot medicines instead of fire cautery; however, fire cautery is much more helpful, and I have already mentioned the treatment with cold medicines in the previous section: take as much as you need.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	from the vessels that come as pieces
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Many times it happens that a pain arises from a deficiency which we call "close" according to our intention, and it is a great fault which harms the foot.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the cautery for this disease is according to two manners.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	This is to know, the fire cautery, and the hot water cautery.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	The fire cautery is that you heat the cautery knife also like a pen, and it should be made of good iron to penetrate the nail from all sides, and have subtle edges; after that, place it hot on the nail, and turn your hand around the nail until it reaches the bottom of the nail; leave it thus for three days until it begins to rot; then make an ointment of wild mallows ground with silk, and leave the ointment on all night, and the nail will come off and be uprooted from its roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the dislocated joint with a hot compress until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	If they are converted by heat, and often occur in the hands and feet, it is necessary to apply hot cautery; and this is done thus: take a cane of iron or steel, or a penknife, and place the nail and the ulcer, that is, the warts, on it; then place the cane around it so that it embraces everything, and pour some hot water onto it, holding your hand firmly, and twist it so that the edge of the cane reaches the root of the nail, and allows the hot water to penetrate deeply to the root; let the patient bear the sting of the hot water for an hour; then leave it in that state, and it will come out at the roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	First, do one after another, until you have straightened all those that are in the body, then treat the bruises that cause pain.
li cure dou trembler	It treats the shaking.
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices IIII cauteres ou IV sus l’espinee dou dos, I cautere entre chescune espinee; et I cautere ou pez, et I sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When anyone shakes from cold or quartan fever or another, it is necessary that you make four cauterizations or five on the spine of the back, one cauterization between each spine; and one cauterization at the foot, and one on the stomach with an olive cauterization; if it stops shaking, and hastens the health from the cold illness.
des pustules puans	from pus-filled boils
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	Never is it apparent through external symptoms that the body is bathed in foul pus, which comes from deeply corrupted substances.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	if it is necessary to do a cauterization on each boil, one should use a delicate cauter from the wood of a myrtle tree, with which the point is taken in the fire, or a cautery from the root of an herb called aristologe, or a lenticular cautery.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	And never should cauterization be done at the beginning when they appear, according to this manner, lest it grow worse and break off the excesses from which it arises, and becomes healed; but it must be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	When the artery is cut.
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Many times, great consequences arise from the blood of an artery that is cut, whether it comes to the wound, or the incision of an abscess, or cautery of a member, and similar things; and this is a very painful thing to endure.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren I, ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And still, when this happens to anyone, if you quickly place your index finger on the wound of the vein and pull it out so much that the blood is stopped beneath your finger, and no more drips; then take several small and large olive oil cauteries and hold them over a flame until they are all red; then, according to the size of the wound and its location, place the cautery on the vein where you hold your finger, and keep it there until the blood stops.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement I autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if you feel a sudden pain when lifting your arm above the vein, and the cauterization is complete, quickly take another cautery from the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des IIII manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not cease to perform one after the other until the wound is healed; and be careful not to damage the nerve nearby, and let no further harm come to the patient; and know that when the flow from the artery has ceased, it cannot be properly healed, especially if the artery is large, unless by one of the four methods we have mentioned: either by cauterization, or by extraction when it has not been treated, or by tightly tying it with thread, or by applying medicines that have the power to stop blood; and do this carefully and gently.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Whoever alleviates the pain by applying tight cloths or placing hot things on it, or other similar things, will not benefit; it will only make it worse.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if it happens to someone who has no good medicine at hand, they should apply their finger to the vein wound as we have said, and press firmly until all pain is gone from the wound and the vein; they must not move it, but moisten it with cold water frequently until it becomes very cold, as long as the limb is frozen, swollen, and painful. And make inquiries about what he needs for cauterization and medicine.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	We begin the second book of surgical treatments.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter about every disease for which it is appropriate to use fire cautery or burning medicine, and about the herbs, causes, tools, and shapes of cauterization; I have placed this chapter on the most important body parts up to this point, and I will continue in this chapter along the same path so that those who wish to learn may do so more easily.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And so, before I begin, it is important for you to know that this chapter involves more risk and danger than the first one on cautery; therefore, greater caution is required.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I warn you not to undertake folly.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For many ways of people come for treatment.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	so often come those who are so certain of their illness that they die gently due to the hope they find in their treatment and the magnitude of their suffering; and from these one must have fear.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	And there are those who give you their attention and say: "Wait, I am sore"; and the disease is painful.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	You should not give your consent to those who come to you with this mannerism, but put more great caution in your honor than in your greed, and do not act rashly but prudently regarding those whom you are certain of and from whom you can gain and benefit; and use prognosis and indication in the treatment of your patients so that health is restored; and this will help you achieve good repute, glory, and a lasting memory.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Very dear son, our lords grant you good understanding and rectitude, and if you desire the holy inspiration from his hand, so be it.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	I have ordered this chapter for you, devising it according to the chapters of cautery that I have previously devised from the beginning up to the foot, so that you may find more easily what you will need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	chief filled with blood
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	You know that this disease often comes to children at birth, and when the grip is too strong around the child's head; and never does it come from a cause resolved because one cannot intervene.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this disease except in children, and it hastens the death of all that I have seen; and for this reason, I think it is better to leave the work in part, rather than to pursue it completely.
Et je vis I enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com II nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw a child whose joints were filled with water, and the head became swollen each day until it could not be supported; the moisture was so great that it led to death, and this moisture is collected beneath the bone next to the syphac, between the heart and the bone; the work should be such that the moisture is drained from between the heart and the bone, and the abscess is small, so that you make a wide cut through the head, as long as the moisture flows; and see the shape of the sponge:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai II fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is deeper, and the abscess larger, then make two cuts in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief III fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is under the bone, and you see the openings of the glands on each side of the head clearly, and there is a strong, sharp pain when you press it with your hand from inside, and it has not yet healed; then you must make three cuts in the head according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision, remove all the moisture thoroughly.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	After loosening the cracks of bandages and powders, he applies wine and oil, leaving it for up to five days; then he removes them, treating the wound with bandages and ointments, and ensures the head is equally stretched, and gives the patient dry meat from a pouch of moisture until the limb is comfortable and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another method of incision is that you observe or measure the size of the abscess and the arrangement of the fluid; for it never appears in front, nor behind, nor on the right, nor on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Measure then the abscess and the fullness of the fluid, and cut according to your ability; be careful not to block the artery; and come quickly with the flow of blood, so that the patient does not die from the slow drain of blood and moisture.
de reume	Of the root
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les II arteres.	When a person suffers from a disease called "cataract" either in one or both eyes, and the disease is old, and medical treatments are of no avail, then the final remedy is cautery by sealing the two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	Therefore, when you have sealed their eyes, make the patient turn their head; then rub the affected area with a rough cloth until the arteries open; afterward, pull the skin tightly from the patient's head using the entire cloth; then locate where the vein is pulsating, and ensure both sides of the ear are sealed; then mark the locations of the joints, and cut each one with a sharp scalpel from both sides, reaching down to the bone, ensuring it is wide across the forehead.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com II dois au traver.	And if you see, turn the spatule beneath the artery and cut through the clot on top, cutting as it should go through.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, it bleeds continuously from above.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery does not open when pressed, it is necessary to measure the quantity of space in three parts, then tie it with a thread and cut until it reaches the bone; and this should be done with blood, about six parts, or perhaps a little more or less, according to what the patient can endure and the filling of the artery; then inspect the wound: if there is no swelling on the bone where the clot has formed, and if the base of the clot does not prevent it from healing, then strain the wound and bandage it, and apply treatment until it becomes healthy.
de emigrainne	from migraine
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When an old migraine comes with a severe catarrh due to the moisture of tears and heat in the eyes and nose, and similar conditions that cause ancient foreskin and other things, it is treated by various medical cures, but none benefit if we do not drain the arteries of the eyes and cauterize them, as we have described.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the method for extracting them is that the patient pulls out the hairs from his temples, and listens to the artery that opens in the temple, as it opens well with its beating, and is quickly closed except for no man who is too weak; and if it is closed, he pulls the collar of some cloth, then rubs the place with a rough cloth, and raises the area with hot water until the artery appears clearly; then take the spatula with this shape:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	Then scrape the skin lightly until you reach the artery, then treat it with pinches and detach well the threads that hold each part; and if the artery is thin, turn it to the tip of the hook, then cut off that part according to the quantity of two joints.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	For if it is not cut, it does not heal without great pain.
Et trai dou sanc des VI c/, jusc’a III; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en II leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les II liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And treat the abscess with six cuts, down to three; and if the artery is large, it is necessary that you tie it with two threads of strong silk, so that putrefaction does not come before the healing of the wound, and causes complications; then cut off the excess between the two threads at the same time, and if you see fit, cauterize with a cuticle knife down to the bone while the joints are cut; and this is the moving work, if the patient does not have fever and has a hot complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For cauterization is aid to finish off moisture; hence it is of greater aid for moisture.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de II pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	Or for the extraction of arteries, it is necessary that one fills the space with cotton wool and places several well-made bands on top; and when they are loosened, one should be careful to apply dry medicines that produce heat, and use bands until the wound is healed; and as soon as you see the artery exposed, hasten to cover it by cauterization, or use vitriole (a caustic substance) and press with your hand so that the wound is cleaned; and if you don't have this at hand, place your finger over the wound until it freezes, and keep applying cold water as long as necessary, and pull with due care. The more mobile and lighter the artery is during extraction, the better it is to cauterize the vein from both sides to retain its heat for a longer time.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instruments are too tight, they retain less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les II coutelz I doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les II leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en II leus; et soient esloigniet entre les II chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it must have between the two blades a substantial amount of space, and then when you have marked the two joints with a sign, place the hot iron over them until it reaches the bone, and cut the vein in two joints; and they should be spaced apart between the two joints because this cautery is not entirely solid throughout. And this is the form of the cautery:
des larmes	tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears from the eyes descend into the veins that are on the top of the head, and no medicine helps, you see the face of the sick person turning red, and they feel movement as if from a fever, and the skin is dry and moist so that the hairs of the eyelids fall out, and the eyelids are scorched by the heat of the tears, then this treatment is necessary.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And they called this ancient treatment "contused cure". For the patient with this condition, you should pluck the hairs from their forehead, then make three cuts on the forehead evenly according to its length; one cut should go all the way across the forehead just below the hairline, and the other two should be along the sides of the forehead, passing through two joints. Avoid incising the arteries that are on either side of the papers (eyelids). Keep your hand away from the continuation of the jawbones, making each wound about three joints in width. Have a piece of sponge and cloth to wipe the blood, then use the curved spatula part as shown:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	From the incision that is made on the temple down to the second incision; peel away all the skin that lies between the two slits to the very satisfaction that is on the bone, then make another incision from the middle of this one down to the other second, and then extract this spatula.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	if you insert the instrument called "cultellaire" (a type of knife) into the first slit, it should be very sharp on one side and soft on the other. This is its shape:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	and place the sharp side of the instrument against the skin at an angle to the bone, and the soft side towards the bone, and cut until it reaches the middle slit.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cut all the veins that descend from the neck to the tips, ensuring the incision is continuous all the way to the heart; then make another deep cut until it reaches the other side. Then extract the blood evenly and press the wound to expel more blood. Place a piece of thin cotton in each cut and cover them with moistened cloths soaked in wine, oil, and ash, and ensure the abscesses do not form again. On the third day, loosen the bandages and apply a strong injection of warm water, then use basilicon ointment with rose oil, and other remedies to heal wounds until they are cured.
dou reume des eulz	dou reume des eulz" translates to "cut the tips" in
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	Whenever any catarrh comes habitually, and you see the eyes swollen and small, weakening sight, and burnt papers; and the hair falls out, or it feels as if a sharp pain is poking, and the patient sneezes, then know from these symptoms that this matter and catarrh do not come from only one vein, but the cure lies in moving the affected part.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And instruct the patient to press their forehead, then make a deep cut across the forehead, and another one quite wide.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And begin from the cut on the left temple to the right temple, making the incision down to the bone; and keep your hand away from the nerve of the temples that move when you blink. When the bone is exposed, wipe all blood with a sponge, then pull apart the two edges of the cut and place old cotton in between, and cover it with cloth. Then wrap moistened cloths soaked in wine and oil over it, and protect from further infection. Once the bone heals, rub the bone gently until it feels warm, then apply astringent substances to prevent further issues.
En teil maniere: pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this manner: take two parts of wheatflower and three parts of colophony, and make an ointment; apply it to these wounds to soothe them throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	ear discharge
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	Anything that causes discharge from the ears is one of four things: grains, animals, mineral stones, or similar objects; seeds such as beans, peas, or other legumes; or fluid-like substances like water and air and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	If discharge from the ear is a stone or any other object that does not adjust itself to the ear or grow in the ear, then place the ear in the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see a stone, and it distills any little drop of purple oil or oil of myrrh, then prepare for extraction; and it will cause coughing from the condition, and it stops up the nostrils when coughing occurs, and place pieces of cloth or wool in the ear; and pull the ear towards the top.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Often, this treatment brings fever; and if it does not bring fever, then prepare for extraction with very fine tweezers, whose shape is as follows:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it jumps out with the tweezers, that's good; if not, prepare for extraction with an extremely thin wire of small gauge; and if it still does not jump out, make a hook of iron and press the top of the hook into the hole in the ear firmly, and stop up what is around the hook with soft wax so that the air current cannot enter with the hook. Then treat it properly, because often this brings fever as we have said; and if it does not come out in this way, then take a great deal of care in choosing the instruments, and place some cotton in it, and press the lump onto the stone or something similar, and extract it.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if she does not do all these things that we have said, act swiftly to split the ear just as the abscess hardens and the pain subsides; and take care in making the incision so that you first soothe the patient from the cephalics, and extract the blood according to its strength, then place the patient between your hands and straighten the ear above, and make a small incision at the base of the ear where the fat or tissue is attached; let the incision be as wide as a moon until you reach the stone, then remove it with your skill, and suck it into your mouth; and continue the cure until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if there are grains present and they swell, then perform an extraction; and if it cannot be extracted, then use a thin spatula according to this form.
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and make no further incision in that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not be hasty to judge if the grain is moist due to earwax, having made many attempts; then extract it with fine tweezers and suction, as we have said, so that the extraction is gentle.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In the case where something has entered the ear, it is advisable for the patient to use a gentle sneeze and cover the ear with fine cotton wool.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And lie still on that same ear, whether there is wax or water.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If she jumps through fire, it is good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	If the fire is no longer hot, take many small stones along your thumb and forefinger, warm them slightly over the fire, and insert one into the ear canal and try from another side to push it through. Make a cut on another stone with another stone until all moisture is gone, and then jump through fire; if you see that the eardrum has split, take a thin wire, and pull one of the edges inside the ear, and the other edge around the fire until the thinner part is burned; then make several more cuts with different stones until all moisture disappears.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	During the removal of the beast, if it is small like a flea or similar, treat it as we have said in the previous section; but if it is large enough to be felt, use pincers for its extraction; and it is the easiest thing to remove from the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	When treating earworms (vers enjanrez) as we have discussed in the previous section and mentioned distills, if the cure is not effective, it is necessary to examine the ear in sunlight. If there are no visible worms, use fine pincers to remove them; if they remain unseen, take note of their shape.
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And it should be tight from below and wide from above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	And then, more subtly, turn the bottle into the ear according to the amount of suffering of the patient, then suck gently along the entire chain; do this often until all the pain disappears.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if they do not want to come out, plug the chain with cotton as I have said in the previous section; and if they do not emerge easily as we mentioned, administer distillations that the ancients tried in the treatment of worms, and you will find them or learn about distillations elsewhere. And distil your oils and medications into the ear using these tools, forming them as you see fit.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And take a piece of silver or gold wire cut into small pieces, and put them over the small openings to distill; and to press inside the distillation with a well-made iron instrument for this purpose, and if you see a blade, wrap it around the tip carefully; then pour your oil or juice, and whatever you wish from your medicines in the kettle, and let the kettle be in the ear; then put the blade into all the cotton within the kettle, and press your hand firmly until the oil is distilled or the ear is slightly warmed, as one distills it into the ear; and let it not be too cold, for the medicine would not be so good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	From ear inflammation
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born with any perforation in the ears; and the same thing happens to adults due to a wound or a foreign object entering the ear, and this obstruction never completely closes in the ear unless one can see it; and sometimes the hole becomes slightly larger, but no one sees it.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	When the obstruction completely closes, if one cannot see it, it is due to poor healing in various dispositions, and in such cases, one should place the patient's ear towards the sun; and look inside: if you see the swelling apparent, this indicates the extent of the form.
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And make cuts and incisions all around and behind, so that the ear is not damaged; if the pain is from a bone or cartilage in the ear, then hold it with subtle pincers and gently remove it, until all the bone is extracted.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the incisions are perfectly done in the ear, take a very fine and sharp razor, heat it slightly over the fire, then apply it to the cartilage of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you feel the patient groaning from the operation on their ear, make a slight perforation, and be careful not to injure the nerves of the ear; then insert into the ear a plug according to the width of the opening, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Make sure the wound is clean, or take a cloth and dampen it in rosewater, and sprinkle it with vitriol powder; if you see an ear swelling, it is necessary to remove the tent and apply another moistened cloth made of rosin oil and wax, until the swelling subsides; then treat it as long as it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if an infection occurs, immerse a sponge and cloth in cold water, place it on the ear, and use other remedies that remove the infection's swelling, which are treated with distillations.
de la char des papieres	from the work of papers
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	Collect all the papers that come from joints when they are moist and dry, it is necessary to extend them with pincers and forceps, and cut off the top of a spatula at its roots; then put it in a crucible and grind it.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if, after removing the skin, the lenticular cautery is made gently, and the cauterizer makes incisions afterward, it is often repaired, as nothing remains of its roots; and when they are cauterized with fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	(referring to the previous line) of the scar tissue
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Many times come to paper certain things that appear twisted in their form and hardness, and for this reason, this disease is called "grandine," which is a gathering of great moisture on the paper above and below; the work is as follows: take care if the grandine becomes silent from one side to the other, and it is a light thing to know; do then with a wide cut, then scrape gently from each part, then take hold of it with pincers and cut.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If you cannot cover it without piercing the paper slightly, it causes no harm to the patient; and if the split is large, with a seam, treat it until it is healthy; and if it is small, do not use much force, as the moisture will soon restore it and cause infection.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if there is a great pain descending inside the ear towards the top part, turn the paper against it, and the pain will be in claws, and the hammering and pressing from both sides; and if the paper is removed by incision, it causes no harm; and when the pain is cut away, rinse with salt water and cure the wound as long as the patient remains healthy.
de la graisse des eulz	from the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Xerophthalmia is a fat that becomes stuck on the surface of the eyes, and this occurs more frequently in children than in adults, causing great pain to their eyes, leading to cataracts in the mornings, and they cannot bear the light of the sun because tears rush to their eyes. Due to this, they close their eyes repeatedly, sleep on them, and their eyelids become moist below the surface, showing signs of inflammation that open up in the eye.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the joint with your fingers and feel the extraction between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the method of the procedure is that the patient places his head in a healthy position; then he takes a linen cloth and prepares a tent-like shape according to the quantity of the extraction from each part, and places it there; and presses with his fingers on both sides so that the extraction is gathered within the circle; then, using a sharp spatula, they make a groove not wider than the wound made in the vein, and make it completely across the extraction; and continue shaping the skin until they reach the extraction; and in various arrangements, the extraction comes out of the groove in the shape of a white fat piece.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Take then a whole piece of cloth between your fingers over the fire, and move your hand to the right and left as long as it is spread; and be careful not to press into the fissure, do not reach all the way to the oil, do not blow on it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the fissure does not open at the beginning, gently widen it a little bit if it appears to be closed; then take it out as we have said, and moisten cloth with oil and water, and apply it to the wound, and straighten it.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And for such men who grind and apply it to corrupt the moisture that remains.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat him as long as he is sane.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it comes to the place of the hot abscess, treat it with external cooling as long as he is sane.
des poilz des papieres	hairs of paper
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc IIII manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When hairs grow in papers (i.e., abnormally) and become inflamed, they cause great harm as if they were foreign bodies, leading to conditions like cracking, softening, and albugine (a skin condition), all of which are caused by the destruction of the natural hairs; the cure is through four methods: cauterization with fire, medication with astringents according to what is mentioned in the chapter on cauterization, or through incision and stitching, or using ligatures, as I will explain.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	You should place the patient's head in a healthy position, then take the paper from the oil with your left hand; if it turns, that is good; if not, insert an needle along all the thread above; and this should be done near the margin of the paper where the hairs grow, along all the paper, and turn it towards the razor. Then cut the paper in the part beneath the hairs, close to where they are attached, from the great tear to the small one; then extract the thread, and place beneath the paper a thin piece of cotton and cloth, and sign on the paper with an image of a cross, as if from myrrh, but it should be according to the amount that you see the paper raise, which is measured at all points.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if at that part where the skill is to cut, they take a great quantity of paper according to how soft it is; then make a cut along all two lines you have marked, and begin with a large tear from the corner to a small one; and let it be a crack near the natural hair in the thickness of a root, then turn the knife in one of the two angles towards the heart, and scrape off all the flesh. Then bring together the two edges with a single stitch of fine wool thread, and wipe away the blood, allowing the excess threads to hang on both sides without anything sticky; if you do so. If not, leave the stitch and threads for three or four days, then treat the wound without stitching with things that dry and constrict, because the paper revives at the healing of the wound and its gathering together, but the stitch moves (as the ancients say), and this is harmful; and if in another way: it is that you mark the paper with a shape like the leaf of mirth, as we have told, at three points according to the form below:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then take hold of what overcomes the small forces equally according to the shape that is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.
