And if you cannot hold the pincers, and the matter is not equal, take a needle where there is thread, and wrap it around the figure; then take another thread through the large wound, and the second thread through the small one, and gather them equally between your fingers; then gently lower your hand equally, and lift all the skin you have marked, as we have said; then sew together the two edges of the wound with stitches, and cure it until it is healed; and if an abscess forms at your incision, soothe it with ointment or similar soothing applications; and sometimes the hair on the paper becomes altered: it is necessary to use what we have said about the incision; but the stitching in one place and another is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The treatment for broken bones is as follows: take paper and make it inside according to what I have said, then create two bones by art, and two fine bindings just as long as the paper and wide enough with a spatule; as for the parts where you hold the bones, join them together delicately on top of the paper from oil, and pull the two bones from the two joined parts; leave it like this for several days, and the bone that is tightly bound will heal and strengthen and grow.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it delays and the wound has strength, then treat it while it is healthy; and when the wound is sealed and if you lift the paper and the hairs do not grow back, this is the form of the two bones that you will make according to this figure and this quantity of length and width.
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The work requires such skill that you pierce the skin with a fine needle, and wrap it with soft and fine silk thread; then bring together the edges and tie them subtly, making the length of the threads one palm length; then arrange in the wound another fine silk thread briefly tied, and fasten the edges with this thread; then place the patient's head on your healthy hand; and make it so the sun shines such that the work is declared free, for it is a subtle and small work. Then pull the needle all through the wound at the root of the hair adjusted, and pierce it gently into the paper until you treat it above the natural hair. Then extract the hair up to the wound, and wrap in the wound the hair if there are one or two or three or more; then withdraw your hand when the hairs come out entirely from the wound in the paper with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the hair does not come out with pulling, you must pull the hair root out from its entire length that you have ordered it to be, until the hair comes out completely through the opening and you see it with your eye; then you pull the hair and the thread, close the wound and leave it closed for one or two days, until the new hair grows in its place; and if the hairs are small, accompany them with a long hair from a natural horse, and raise them with that which you leave open, as long as they remain extended and then lift it.
de la porriture de l’oil	of the corruption of the wound
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this illness called "aleacrati" or putrefaction occurs in the body, it happens in two ways: naturally or unnaturally.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it occurs suddenly from wounds, or cuts, or cauterization, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the method of treatment in this case is that you split open the wound, separate the edges, and place linen strips inside, binding them until the wound heals; and it is not appropriate to use drying or constricting substances in the care of such a wound.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do this, the illness returns worse than before; but it works with softening things, like fenugreek; and rosewater of water or elderflower and flaxseed are cooked, and applied to each eye, wrapped in a cloth, and the treatment of these.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the true treasure of your cure is that you must be careful not to adhere to the old form; and these works that we have mentioned are only guidelines for this illness, so that it does not return in the same way as before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the moisture that comes to the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This illness, which is dislocation, is truly called "luxation," and it is both natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	Accidental dislocation comes from wounds and fractures and cauterization and similar things; and the path of this process is such that if you prick with an needle, it creates a double thread, and insert it into the flesh, piercing from the left eye socket to the right, so that the thread passes through both sides of the skull; then the bone moves upwards over the entire needle, and the fracture is wide at the scalp.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the shape of the paper returns as it should be, that is good; but if not, take a razor and insert it into the crack, turn the paper, and make two cuts on one side of the incision you made, so that the edges of these cuts form two angles of the cut, making them resemble the angles of a Greek letter 'I'. Then remove the charred material, according to how much is agape from both sides, from where the paper meets it. Then adjust the two parts back together and sew them with a thread of flax. Finally, apply the curative treatments we have mentioned about softening medicines and bandages until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the disease comes from cutting or stitching or cauterization, it is necessary to make a clean cut under the skin between the hairs, and according to what is said above; then separate the two books of the limb, as I have said; and one must perform the work according to the form of the disease, for it is very diverse in form, and skilled masters devise various instruments to restore the natural shape, and the patients themselves, according to what is appropriate for the operation and tools, vary their methods.
dou soudement de la papiere	The phrase "dou soudement de la papiere" translates directly to "cut suddenly from
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this suture is done in a certain way that the paper above is smooth with white oil, and it cannot move or perform its natural functions, then you must insert the tip of a razor under the paper and lift it gently; hold it like pincers, until you remove what is sharp on the delicate spatula, which should not be too sharp or too blunt, so that the patient does not suffer from the overly sharp spatula; and make your incision lightly, so that the paper regains its natural shape; and all of the gathered paper heals, without ever making the oil bitter or salty, but rather raising it with fresh water and a collar; then place between the paper and the oil a cloth of linen, and on top of the oil, wet wool in abundance; and after the third day use a collar and things that seal until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	from the nail of the finger
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	You know that the nail is according to two manners: it is nervous and resembles a hard, dry substance, and another which is not nervous but appears like white, frozen moisture, that when touched with iron and treated as pincers, one cannot; and both resemble beginning near the great toe, and grow little by little until they cover all sight and all light and the movement of the finger.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	The method of incision is as follows: the patient places his head in a healthy position, then opens the fingers; holds a piece of paper in his hand, then coils the nail like a small pincers, extending it upwards; takes an needle, threads it with a horsehair, or a goat hair, or a cowhair, and a strong thread; doubles the tip of the needle slightly and pierces it through the nail, all the way to the end, and ties the nail with the thread, extending it upwards, and scrapes off all the hair around the nail at its base, leaving only the nail itself, so that no tears come from the usual rubbing; never stretch the nail too much, just use a needle and thread as we have said. Then scrape off all the soft tissue around it, giving it this shape:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be sure that the scalpel does not touch and tear the flesh, and that the knife is not pierced; then, after incising, drop a little bit of broached silk into oil, and make a collar from it with litargyre, and leave it until the next day; then tend to it as needed until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	If the nail is not nerve-related and you cannot insert the needle, often this condition requires medication; as I have described in the previous section, if you see it covered with oil on the patient's body, take a light scalpel as per this form.
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And gently remove the nail from above, and if you see that it weakens little by little and the reason presses, let it drop into your mouth an oil made of lightning and a red collar and finely crushed, and stop the oil until the next day; then repeat the other work according to this same procedure, until it is completely removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing contradicts you about the oil, such as a hot abscess, then apply it, and first treat the hot abscess until it is healed, then continue with the work as before, until it is completely healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh causes harm in the eye by great damage, holding it at the onset and cutting off a part but not all, so that no tears come; then it secretes into the eye a red collyre made of litargir.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	from the flesh that is born on the iris
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	Some people are born without any red flesh on the iris, covering it and restraining it under the eyelids, and making it look like a rose of balm; and the difficulty is that the patient must place their head in your hands, then open the eyes and pull out all the flesh as skillfully as possible, maintaining its strength; then cut off the first piece, shaving everything down to the end, taking care not to irritate the eye during the procedure; and use a spatula for incisions, as we mentioned regarding nail incisions and small forces with which one removes the sebum—as this figure after this chapter demonstrates. And when the incision is complete and all the flesh has been removed, apply silk oil or distill collyre red and similar corrosive medicines, and place cotton over it with an egg white to ensure it stays hot from the abscess; and if nothing remains and you suspect a hot abscess, leave the oil and treat the abscess with soothing remedies for a hot abscess. Then return to your procedure as long as it is healthy, and thus make all other incisions in the eye using this method.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But nevertheless, it is necessary that you take care of each weak part of the body naturally; and from the accidental path, in the work of iron; and do not push your hand into any of these works until you see that this member suffers from this work.
des voines des eulz	veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	These are red veins that are covered over the eye, they steal from the sight their work and weaken the eye every day.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	Skill is therefore in the first place that you look at the eye, as it is, strong, and there is no other disease outside of the redness; then take them in this way: instruct the patient to put his head on your healthy hand, then suspend these veins all around gently according to your wisdom, and make the incisions delicate and double according to this form.
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And there should be two incisions by degrees in the body according to this form.
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then, gently coiling the veins, wipe off the blood hour after hour until you see the veins disappear from the flesh; be careful not to pierce the oil with the points of the spatulas, and perform this work at noon in front of the sun, being very diligent in your task so that you do not stop until the veins are gone; and when you have done this, distil green and red collyre into the oil to corrupt what remains from the blood.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you cannot collect all of them in that hour, make a poultice over the wound with soothing things to ease the pain of the joints, and leave it for no more than a day until the pain is eased and the hot abscess is assured, then resume according to this manner as before until it is healed; and this is the form of the veins:
de la fistule de l’oil	from the fistula of the oil
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	He calls these fistulas "arissati": When you treat them with cautery and hot medicine as I have previously mentioned, and they remain unhealthy, there is something within that you must open at the abscess, where he (the patient) is destined to die, and remove all the moisture until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is exposed and you see the corruption and blackness, take all the instruments mentioned here and shape them; it is called a "sharp chisel", and it should be made from fire-hardened steel in the form shown.
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place the corrupt bone back in its socket, then twist it between your fingers, and press your hand slightly until you know that corruption is gone; do this several times, then return the joint to its medicinal remedies.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the joints are fused and it seems to be born that way, and the bowels' course is also fused and remains so for forty days, and it does not heal or become abscessed, and no other adverse incidents occur, then you know it is healthy; if not, there is another tool to reopen the fistula through incision in a specific way: take a second look at the bone with iron, and by using aqua (medicinal water), and when the bone is exposed as shown here, make sure the iron tip has three angles, and thin it out towards the top as you can see.
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	then place it on the lost bone of the arm, and move your hand away from the point, then continue with the entire treatment until it pierces through the bone and the patient feels pain because he has to hold his hand against it; and afterward return to using dry medicines, as I have taught you, and when the skin hardens on the bone, see what happens to the limb; if it becomes lighter for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	from the opening of the vein
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the veins are completely opened and do not cause any disturbance to the lung or any impairment, it is necessary that you hold the patient; then apply a healthy poultice, then place cups or leeches without causing harm in order to draw out the blood, then apply oil made from aloes, frankincense, and sarcocolla, and then strain the oil, and paste it on with bandages and cloth; and the manner of the cloth should be such that you make each layer thin and double them up in four's, and place one upon another according to the need of the vein; then strain it from above a hard board, and renew the cups for sucking without causing harm; then remove the cups and leave the poultice applied day and night until it becomes relaxed, if necessary to draw it tightly; then remove the poultice after day and night, and if you see the blood repairing itself, it is good; otherwise, renew the paste, cloth, poultice, and cups until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	loss of thread integrity
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When there is a disruption in the thread (or yarn), it opens and becomes like small grains of resin, which is encouraging to see; then, if you notice this happening, the work required is such that you push an needle into the root of the part below, and another needle where the thread forms a double strand near the tear; pierce through and leave the first needle according to its position; then cut the thread with the double strand and tie a portion of the yarn around it tightly, and pull out the needle, applying fresh moist lint in abundance; leave it until the thread absorbs the moisture, then treat the wound with comforting remedies until the injury is healed; and at no time should the wound be restrained by the yarn in any part of a circular bandage, until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the joint appears well-formed, pierce it with a fine spatula that comes from oil, remove the white moisture and relax the joint, then insert it again immediately; then extract it as much as it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	of the vein (or duct) of oil
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease called "alcunnati" is not only a vein (or duct) that is gathered in the oil, resembling clear water descending, but it is not clear; and the manner of the appearance of the work is such that you make the patient sit up straight, then take the head between both hands, moving it until you see the vein come to the top near your fingers; then insert a needle and do not allow the light to descend or clear, so that the patient sees things as he usually does; and if the discharge from the vein does not decrease, know that it is acute, and the clearing of the vein must be done as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you make the patient rest in your hands, then take the delicate spatula and make incisions on the thin membrane between the cornea and the conjunctiva along with the cornea and the iris, until the bowel is released; and when it is released, it drips into the clear hot oil mixed with honey, or boiling water with fennel seed and honey, then apply another cure as long as it is healthy.
des aigues de l’oil	Des aigues de l'oil" translates directly to "water from oil" in
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have similar waters in the division, and what is necessary to pierce, if done according to health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	You should place the patient between your crossed hands away from direct sunlight and tie a healthy cloth tightly around them; then place the paper of the oil in your left hand if the nails are on the left side, or in your right hand if the nails are on the right side. Then take the instrument called "almagda" in your right hand if the nails are on the left, or in your left hand if the nails are on the right; then place the tip of the instrument against the crown through the thickness of a single strand at the bluer part of the oil, and press the instrument called "almagda" firmly, and twist your hand as it pierces the bluer part of the oil, and feel that the almagda reaches the empty space. And it is necessary that the measure of the almagda be exactly equal to the measurement of the space from the prunele to the end of the darkness; and this is the crown of the oil; you will see the bone on the paper due to the clarity of the horny skin, and then place the instrument up to where the water is, and press it through one passage after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If he feels the patient sinking now, see if he can spot the sick person before him and the instrument in his hand.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After a brief rest, then the second path must be raised, applying force with the instrument, and when it is deeply inserted and does not move up, extract gently by turning your hand back and forth; then place again in the acute position a little bit of precious oil, and remove from this the blood within.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then apply with heat the hot oil or any other moistened in rose oil and plenty of fat, and wrap it with healthy oil.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	We, and those of our time, place a warm compress with much heat.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the oil cannot enter the eye due to its hardness, as there are many people with very hard eyelids, it is necessary that you press the instrument called "alberit", which has this shape:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And then pierce only the conjunctive tissue, without going too deep, but make it subtle, then insert the warm compress, as we have said; and after completing the work, prepare the patient for sleep, lying on his back in a dark place; and let him be free from all movements, and feed him with light foods, and do not move his head to the right or left, and keep him bound according to his condition for three days. Then release him in the same dark room, and test his vision, and make him see nothing, and then put the bandage back on for seven more days; and it is not appropriate that you perform this at the time of treatment or after incision, but rather lightening it is necessary, because sharp pain rises suddenly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	When an abscess forms, you should loosen the skin in front of the seventh day and apply the remedies that soothe the abscess; and once it is soothed, loosen the bandage and place a small piece of cloth on its face to cover it for some time, and then return it to that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	Then leave the house little by little and return to your own life; and know that no disciples should interfere in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us from Iran, who told us that in their peaceful land they make a tool that sucks out water, but I never saw anything like it in our land, nor do I recall reading about it in the books of the ancients; perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the appearances of the forms of magic, so that he who does not know them will see them as strange; and they must be of gold properly.
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And let the head be at the greatest subtlety of this same, and the rear in three acute angles.
de la char sor le neis	of the charm on the new-born
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	No newborn should have charms adjusted in various ways, so that there are none that seem like scorpions full of pain; and if there are such with enchanting charms of fine color, or if the charm is soft of good color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	In this case where the wound is hot and not yet healed, you must place the patient between your hands facing the sun; open their nostrils, and pour the ointment onto those parts, and rub them thoroughly; hold what you can bear to sustain in one hand, as long as you know that part is completely healed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains anything that cannot be covered, open it with all the delicate and light instruments so that nothing remains; without hesitating, make the incision as needed; and if it is a malignant abscess, hurry and cauterize it until the wound is completely cleansed and all parts are healed, then apply ice or vinegar.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If he opens his mouth and moisture comes out to the tongue, knowing that it is healthy; and if the moisture does not come out as it should, knowing there is a chip in the upper bone, the instruments cannot cut well: then you must insert a line of linen thread a little thick, and hold it with your hands, leaving between each part a space no greater or less than necessary, and place the patient's toe in his mouth to his power, and pull in an aromatic manner until the moisture comes out through the tongue inside the mouth; and children often do this at school, and it is a light thing for him who wants to do it. Then hold the part coming through the tongue with one hand, and the other part coming through the mouth with the other hand, feeling one after the other as we who are in thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Do as you know, purify the infected wound, treat the son (presumably a child), wipe away the blood, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment, then return it to its place as before; do this for three days or more, until the ointments have healed all that remains of the infection. Then put a bandage around the neck for no more than a day, if it is healthy, and if medicine is needed, use it; this is the form of the instrument used to purge the head, from which oils and medicines are distilled into the neck.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it should be of silver or gold, resembling an open lamp, like a funnel, and use it thus; if you make a closed funnel, fill it with tools to purge the head, and have several at hand to hold the head while heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	Of the pain near the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Often near the nose arises a sickness called "telul," which swells and grows very large, so much so that it is a sight to behold; and for this reason you must quickly cover it at the beginning, strip off all the skin, then apply hot cautery or medicinal fire; and if you delay covering it until it becomes large, be careful if it hardens, takes on a dark color, loses sensation: do not touch it with iron, as it is an abscessed joint, for whenever you cover it, great harm comes to the patient. If the abscess is tender to the touch, neither dark nor hard, and you are able to completely cover it without pain or difficulty, then empty the patient and cover it skillfully; cure the wound with dry, restraining things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the nose is cut and sewn together
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Understand that when the continuance of one of these important cartilages is broken, it benefits no one, except perhaps no one at all.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is therefore necessary to close the wound in no way if it is fresh and filled with blood; then sew the two lips together, and treat it until it heals; and if the lips are already separated on both sides, it is necessary to scrape all parts of their core while they heal, then sew the two lips together again, tighten them, and sprinkle dragon's blood powder and ground incense on them; and apply a piece of strong or other adhesive plaster, leaving it until it falls off by itself, and then treat with ointment until it heals.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The method of stitching is such that you bring the edges together: either with needles, as we have said in sewing the belly; or with thread, as I have made known to you.
des apostemes des levres	abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	At home, the abscesses on the lips appear as hard lumps, some smaller and others larger, so you must turn the lips and cut into each one, using tweezers to remove the pus and applying vitriole (a caustic substance) to the wound until the blood stops; then wash it with clean water and care for the lip until it heals.
de la char des gencives	From the work of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Often, a growth appears on the gums, which the ancients call "albulus"; it is necessary that you hold it with tweezers, and cut it at its root, allowing the bowel or blood to flow; then apply powdered vitriol or other astringent and desiccant powders; and if the growth returns after the incision, and this happens often, especially if the piece is cut again, and cauterized, then it does not return after cauterization; these are the shapes of the tools for cutting.
des sordens	from disorders
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	No teeth are ever aligned at the top of the gums, within the painful and rough ridges; and no teeth are black or yellow or rotten, as long as the corruption reaches the gums, and they stink; it is necessary that you make the patient hold still between your hands, and his teeth should be in your safe keeping, and file away the protruding teeth or ridges until nothing remains; and do this with black and green and yellow and other stains, until they are clean; and if what is on the first surface is removed, it's good; if not, recommence again on the second and third day, until everything is filed; and know that teeth require various types of instruments to file, according to what the work demonstrates, because the tools used to file away from the teeth have different shapes than those used between the teeth; and these shapes and others should be prepared with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	You should take care when treating a toothache and delay drawing it out as little as possible, for no one should do so; for it is a very delicate matter, and there is no excuse for delaying treatment.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Then, when the patient is constrained from having their tooth drawn, it is important that you are certain about the healthy tooth.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Often the patient complains of pain, thinking that a tooth is infected, and has it drawn; however, the pain does not cease because the infection remains, as we have seen with these healthy teeth. When you are certain about the painful tooth, you should cut around it with a sharp instrument to protect the gums from all sides. Then move the pliers gently at the first sign of movement, making sure they are well-placed, and then tighten them. The infected matter should be placed between your knees, holding it firmly so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extracting the tooth correctly without breaking it, if it does not come out, take none of these instruments and push them gently from every side, and move it as you did before.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	If the tooth is broken and chipped, it is necessary to fill the hole left with cloth or bandage, either where it is missing or through the opening; and if you hold it slightly with pliers, do not pull too hard so as not to break it; and it is very important to work carefully around the gums to remove the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	Take good care so as not to break it, and if a part remains, return it to the patient; for the evil of its root will cause greater pain than at first.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And be sure not to act like the ignorant healers who, in their haste and arrogance, break the body's natural balance, and do not heed what we have said; but they often bring on a grave illness due to their foolish talk about the roots of the disease or the broken limbs, as we have often seen. And when there is bleeding, wash the wound with wine or honey and lint; and if this does not stop it, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The instruments used to extract teeth should have long and thick tips that do not bend when pulling the tooth; these are their shapes.
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And let the members be strong so that they do not bend when pulled, and be of iron well-forged, and have teeth to hold fast.
de la racine des dens	from the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains stuck when pulled, it is necessary to place over it moist cotton or butter for a day or two.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	until the eyes are softened, then apply pliers called 'algefri', which make the teeth look like a cure (or a tool for pulling); they should be made inside the same way as a file and this is their shape.
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out of these grips, it is necessary that you uncover the flesh all around the root, and place the instrument called "althali," which is a plier, shaped like this:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And if it is hard and thick so that it does not break, and the root jumps out by itself, that is good. If not, use all the instruments, and the shapes will come as follows:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one uses this instrument with two prongs, the shape is:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other tools that are used in the treatment of teeth, and this instrument that resembles large pliers, whose shape is as follows:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	This instrument should be of such sturdy construction that it cannot break, and you must be aware of many other dental tools; likewise, there are other instruments not mentioned here. The most skilled surgeons create their own tools, according to the needs revealed by their work and the condition of the patient, for there are various diseases for which no instruments were developed in ancient times. If a tool breaks or is unsuitable, and he seeks the appropriate instrument I have described, using gestures to convey its form...
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And they should be large and well-gripping to hold the bone, so that it does not escape but can be held and removed; and then return the limb to suitable medicine, and if there is decay in the bone, even small, use all these instruments.
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not according to the body's natural shape, and its form is ugly, especially in young women, it is necessary that you know if the tooth has grown after the normal teeth, and is not in the right place, and cannot be filed or polished: then extract it. And if it is painful with the tooth, take this instrument whose form resembles a small beak, and made of sharp iron:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And take a little pot and hold it in your hands for the hardness of the tooth, and because you do not move the others, and if it is apparent that it can be filed, then file it from one side as this shape:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and it is also like the file of which they make needles; and file the tooth little by little in your hands gently, so that it does not move until it is whole; then in the end, it should be entirely smooth without any roughness, and if the tooth is too sharp, it bleeds the tongue, so you must file the sharpness level until it is even, so that it does not burn or corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the tooth aches
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the tooth aches fiercely, either from hitting or grinding, and the patient cannot bear pressure on it, then they should be treated with restricting medicines, but that is of no avail. Then, they should have it restrained by a golden thread, for silver wire turns green and rots, but gold never changes; and the thread must be neither too thin nor too thick, according to the amount of space between the teeth. If you align the teeth, take the thread and wrap it double between the two healthy teeth, then place the aching tooth or teeth in-between, as many as there are, until you reach firmly to the healthy tooth on the other side; then continue the wrapping until you reach the part you started from, and pull your hand gently and sharply until it does not move; and make sure your ligature is at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then cut the edges of the wound with pliers, and assemble them, and close it between the healthy teeth, and place it thus so that the tongue does not bleed; and then leave it thus as tight as it can stay, and if it opens, the thread will unravel, as if pulled by another thread. It should remain in this position for all its time, and this is the form of the teeth and the arrangement of the two healthy teeth and the two molars, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth is reset in its place, one should do it fresh by fresh as we have said; and it should not be done by anyone who is not skilled and patient, and they never form a tooth from the bone of an animal, and place it where there is a deficiency, and tighten it as we have said, and keep it in this way for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	To uncover the tongue's ligaments.
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	No matter what, these ligaments that come from beneath the tongue, whether by nature or accident from a deep wound, and the task is to open the mouth of the patient, placing their head in a healthy position, and gently lifting the tongue; then cut the nervous ligament with a sharp knife as widely as possible, so that the tongue is dislocated from its attachment, and if there is any hardness or newness, and it is due to sudden bleeding from a wound, then use an iron hook and cut through that ligament as well; and be careful not to cut too deeply into the fissure, for the artery located below. And after you have done this, raise the affected area with rosewater or ice, then place a cloth made of linen beneath the tongue; and apply it to the patient each night, so that the ligaments do not heal.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if the infection comes from pus, mix it with vitriole; and if the pain subsides, cauterize it with a slow-burning cautery, which is good for this; then apply other remedies until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you see it is red, black, or hard, and the patient does not feel it, as it is a chancre, do not touch it; if it turns pale, and there is moisture, drain it with a fine instrument, and cut it from both sides; and if the pain subsides in your work, mix vitriole until it is stained, then return to your work until you have treated everything thoroughly. Then lift the limb gently and treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	from the abscess of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	No matter how often holes appear in the throat that are called "godath", and we properly call them the II amandres, and when you treat them, as we have said in the previous section, if they are not completely healed, be careful: these are small abscesses of a deep red color, so do not touch them with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if they are red and the root is thick, do not touch them with iron, also to prevent the spread of pus; but leave it until it dies, and then you will remove it, or it would break on its own. And if they are of a white color, and the root is thin, have an instrument prepared to cover it, but first ensure that the abscess is calm and at ease.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Then make the patient stand before the sun, and keep his feet in good condition, open his mouth wide, and press the tongue down with the instrument, which gives its shape; and it should be made of silver or subtle gold, just like a knife.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	You cannot press the tongue down with all of this instrument, and if you see the abscess, take the saw and the hook and pull it upwards as much as possible; do not use any part of the strings, then cut it with the instrument, which gives a shape resembling some forces; nevertheless, the handle is curved in one place and straight in another, and they are very sharp, and it is made of iron or steel.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument at hand, if it is like pincers, then take them to shape it thus:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And make incisions on one side and leave the other; and when you have cut one of the mandibles, cut the other in the same manner, and after the incision, rinse the patient's mouth with hot water, clear water, and some salt, and if any blood comes, rinse the patient's mouth with hot water or pomegranate peels, or mint leaves, and similar things, until the blood is stopped; then treat it while it is still fresh; and no other abscesses are formed in the throat besides the two mandibles, so cut them both as we have described.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman for an abscess that was in her throat, namely a small abscess; and had tightly closed the entire throat, so that the woman could not breathe through the blocked passageway, and could neither eat nor drink, and would have died if she had stayed that way for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so swollen that it had forced two ribs through the two openings in the throat where it originated.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I then quickly inserted a knife into one of the abscesses, and drew it out through another opening in the throat, and extracted a large portion of pus; I then did the same on the other side, opening the mouth and pressing the tongue; after inserting the knife into these abscesses, I extracted some of the pus, and only a little blood came out; and thus was the passageway from the throat to the woman opened, and she began to drink water and then wine, and I continued to drain the abscess for a long time. The abscess grew again, filling the space that I had emptied, becoming very large; then I seared it and cauterized it inside the throat, after which it did not grow any more, and I left these parts, and God alone was responsible for their healing afterwards.
de l’uve	of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When the retina detaches from the eye and it is swollen and distant, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is thin and round, it is called "retina".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is treated as we have discussed in the division, but the cure is not effective, and you notice that the inflammation around the wound has subsided, and it is becoming less severe, it is necessary to apply a poultice; and that which is round and not distant, should be carefully watched. It is bloody or of a dark color, then avoid incising it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger for the ill patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	Therefore, when you see this, according to the manner I have said, take the patient's tongue with your instrument, as we mentioned before, and insert the pin into the hole, pull it out from behind, and cut it with one of the instruments I spoke of for making incisions in the two nuts.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And it is important that you do not cut off more than the surplus beyond the natural limit; for if you do, it causes great pain to speech and movement. After the incision, use what we said regarding incisions in the two nuts, and treat it until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient suffers greatly from pain, it is necessary that you use instruments for cauterization to alleviate the painful sensation.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	The method of cauterization is very sharp.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And the patient should place his head on a healthy surface and then press the tongue with the instrument mentioned in this chapter (cauterization), using a sharp but not too thick or too thin blade; and by employing the movement of this instrument, it takes the form as follows:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let the surgeon have a beard, as it were, to apply the medicine, just as one would use a spoon, and place the instrument holding all of the medicine over the eye; and have the patient lie on his side, so that saliva and mucus from his mouth can be absorbed by the medicine without reaching the throat or causing harm. Then hold your hand over all of the medicine and press it onto the eye for about half an hour until you see it begin to work and the stinging of the medicine is calmed; and if you observe, take cotton and wrap it around a tool, moisten the cotton with the medicine, and then press the instrument into the cotton against the eyeball until the cotton dries on the eye. Repeat this several times until the cauterization is complete, then leave it to dry, and after three or four days, wash it out with cold water and use gargles until it heals.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This treatment is safer than cauterization, for it is through incision that healing occurs; if it is performed by fumigation in this manner, take plenty of calament, ysope, origanum, rue, chamomile, and avronne, or any similar herbs, and combine them all in a pot, adding water to boil; the pot should be well sealed with a tight lid, as described below:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.
