It should be of silver or gold, and one of the joints should be squeezed in the mouth of the patient as the vapor rises to the eye through the nostril, until the eye becomes numb; afterwards, it often recurs, while the eye is drying out, and take care not to perform this at the onset of a hot abscess, as many complications may arise; and only carry out this procedure during the decline of a hot abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not available, take a stick and insert a piece of wool in the mouth of the patient so that it is not too hot; for the wool does not allow the heat to reach the mouth, and it is a good remedy altogether.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times a sore throat is caused by bone or fish spine, or some other object. Therefore, it is necessary that you treat what you can see, and press the tongue against the sun with all the instrument so that you can see the object; and if it does not open and is stuck in the throat, you should make the patient vomit so that the food is cooked in the stomach; perhaps this will dislodge the object. Or the patient might swallow a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a root of lettuce, or a crumb of dry bread, and then you should extract it by pressing the sponge; and when it comes to the surface, it will be dislodged and then you can pull it out. And if it does not come out as we have said, take an instrument made of salt according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instrument be curved towards the throat so that it can enter more easily, and hold the head raised high; and beware not to touch the epiglottis, lest all the food go down, and do not push the bone inside; and allow the patient to press the instrument, because he must move it until the obstruction is removed; if it goes down, pull it out evenly throughout the instrument, as far as possible.
de la sansue de la gorge	regarding the obstruction of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	No treatment with medicine should be given for the obstruction, as I said in the previous discussion, except through medicinal cure; and if that does not help, then look at the throat of the patient in the sunlight, and press his tongue with the instrument I told you about.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the wound, pull it with all the small pins or delicate pliers that are suitable for this.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if this does not work, take a horsehair, insert it into the throat of the patient, then twist or gently pull on the hair, do this repeatedly.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient has a fever every day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take a full glass of cold water, open the mouth, and pour it in, making the patient swallow it repeatedly; and if at once as the wound feels the water, it heals.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it does not break as we have said, and poisons the patient with bad smell from the instrument used in the fumigation of the eye, do this many times, for it will eventually break without resistance.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	The method of fumigation is as follows: you light a pot with burning coals and place a perforated cover over it to contain the smoke. The patient places the tip of a cane in their mouth, sealing their mouth so that the smoke does not escape but rather fills their lungs. The vapor should now take effect; if it does not, repeat the fumigation many times. In the meantime, make the patient thirsty and have them consume salty and bitter substances, without drinking any water. Then, after this treatment, it is necessary for the steam to escape in a specific manner.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the instrument with which one treats the wound, if you can see it, resembles a hooked pliers for entering the throat; and it looks like a eagle's beak, and has the roughness of lime, so that whatever it grasps, it cannot let go; and here is the form:
li chapistres des apostemes	the chapter on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	Many appearances of abscesses are, according to what the memory brings forth in this book, and they vary in size and shape; and there are two manners, one being in its own likeness, and those that retain moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second method is through the joints where they are in the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the abscess on the top of the head is different from that at its base, and the abscess in the fleshy part of the arm is different from that which occurs at the joints, and each has its own judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if, for an abscess, one should not pierce the skin while the bowel is still alive according to its completion; and if for such cases it is necessary to pierce when they are grown, and do not die according to their completion, as with abscesses that occur at the joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when an abscess comes from a damaged joint, and it is left as it is for some time, perhaps the ligaments and nerves around the joint are corrupted, which causes contractions in that member.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	Or if the abscess is in the main member, and you delay making an incision until it is gangrenous, it will harm the principal member; or if it is from the foundation, you must pierce it so that it does not spread further, lest it become gangrenous and fester inside, leading to a fistula, and cannot heal fully.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And you should know the time of the perforation of the abscess, which is mortal according to its completion; and this is when the pain is soothed, and the fever departs, and the intensity of the pain and redness decreases, and with a gentle movement, and sharpening of the head of the abscess, and other signs; and you should make the perforation depend on the moment when the abscess opens, and where it starts moving; and it should be a long perforation through the body, and if the abscess is in the hands or feet, or in the joints and nerves and arteries, and everywhere equally without any swelling.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In these cases, according to that limb.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in a fatty tissue, it is good to let the incision heal completely before moving, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you pierce it too soon after this, the body will be filled with bad blood from it, and it may become infected; and by chance, the lips can harden and it can fester from him.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if at any abscess that is pierced according to the width of the body, as needed by the member.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And it is necessary that you make small incisions in small abscesses, and small openings; and in large abscesses, large openings, and many cuts according to the size of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses where it is necessary to dig deep, and cover; when they have grown as thick as drapes, and become numb, then it is also necessary to treat them like boils: and if there are such that are cut in three angles, or such that are covered as if with the fur of myrtle, like the wounds of an enemy; or where a round or other size cut must be made.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Those who do not have a head, like a superficial and painful abscess, it is necessary that you pierce it deeply; and when the abscess is large and has a great bowel, and you pierce it, it is not necessary to drain all the bowels at once, but only a part; then stop the abscess for another day, and do not touch it again for some time; repeat this many times, gradually, until all the bowels are drained; especially if the patient is of weak vitality, or a pregnant woman, or small children, or old decrepit people.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For often hope jumps at the outcome of the bow, that by chance it kills the patient, and you will not be blamed.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Beware therefore of this chapter with great caution, and when you have felt your abscess, if the wound is clean, and the abscess wound is small; and if it is a large cut, apply linseed or cotton immediately; and if it is a large abscess with many openings, you must put a tent in each one so that they meet; and if you have, within the abscess, a part of hard skin, and you have sealed it around, you must fill it with old cotton or linen cloth without moisture, and bind it for three days; then open it and apply treatment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if blood flow occurs due to an injury, then apply cold water and ice, moisten the cloth, and bandage the affected area repeatedly.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the bleeding persists, apply a compress and treatment, and use the powders mentioned in this book, especially if it's winter and the affected area or abscess is very sensitive. In such cases, it is necessary to place wet blankets and cloth soaked in wine and hot oil; but if the condition improves and the limb is fleshy, then moisten the wraps with water and cold oil, or wine and fresh oil for up to three days, as we have mentioned before; then remove the abscess and clean and dress it appropriately until it heals.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And it is necessary to know universally in the treatment of abscesses: for I have already told you how to proceed with the treatment of abscesses, and here is the chapter.
des soros	from blood
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Often, small abscesses come from impure blood, and they appear like threads, also similar to the pus of a wound, and there are many of these kinds.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	Some are thick and filled with moisture, just like veins; and some are hard and difficult to cut through, but there is no doubt that if the arteries do not contradict, they can be treated.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work on the trunk is such that you should try all instruments called "entromissory", from which the shape comes as follows, something it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	Because if it contains moisture, they make a hole from above down long.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is evacuated, it removes nothing from the skin that contains the moisture, because it returns again when you leave it; then dip cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it is available; if not, use water and string, and apply it to the wound, and leave it until the next day; and this will heal what has been delayed by night.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then begin the bandage again, as before, on the second day, and the third, until you know for certain that it does not stay during the night; then treat the wound with suitable medicine, as long as it is healthy.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if an abscess becomes hard, follow this form: cut it deeply; drain all the pus, and scrape from all sides, and apply all your skill to draw out the pus where it lies; and if the artery protests, do as I have told you.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And also do the same for an abscess that is painful, cutting and dressing it as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And cut the abscess and the moisture first, if it is lighter, because they are filled with little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if none of these abscesses or pits have moisture, and it is one of these hard abscesses that I found on the head of an old woman; and I found the abscess as hard as a stone, sharp and white, and not to be crushed; and if anyone were to try to open it, they would do as much damage as with a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other pits that occur on the head, especially those that come from the top of the children and at the roots of the ears, keep them open for as long as possible depending on their condition to allow the bowels to pass, and treat them as appropriate.
des scrophules	Of scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times this abscess appears in the neck, and it breaks open the veins, and infests them with anger, and never comes to any other part of the body, and it is painful, and badly joined together.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each scrofula is properly within its bone, as we have said, both the nodules and the abscesses from the head, and there are many appearances of these scrofulas.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and some that are malicious and do not want to obey the healthy ones.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	In those that you see with a good disposition for touch, resembling the healthy color of the skin, mute (still) from every side and is not too tight at the neck or in the artery or the duct, and is not too deep; it is necessary that you cut it open from above, and scrape it from every part, and the two lips of the heart remain as they are, if it is needed, as we have said in the chapters about the head; and proceed little by little, and be sure not to cut the nerve or the vein, and do not let the hand slip, and do not look too far ahead, so as not to cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you cut the vein or the artery and it does not allow you to operate, apply vitriole (vitriol) or any powders that stop blood flow, and close the wound; leave it until the pain subsides, and the wound softens, and then begin to heal.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the wound is stained with blood, return to your work until it is completed; then pay attention to your expert indication if there remain no small pus spots, if you clean and dress them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is a large vein in the root of the abscess, it is not advisable to clean the abscess at its root, but tie it with a double thread strong and leave it hanging without harm; then use an old cotton wound soaked in Egyptian ointment and treat the wound.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you clean the entire abscess, it is necessary that you close the two edges of the wound and sew them now, so that there is no delay due to the size of the abscess.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	If it is necessary for you to understand how to treat the root of this, and draw it out forcibly, cut it as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For those scrofulas that have an excess, pierce them where they appear to be closing; and the piercing should be as previously mentioned, depending on it, then apply these treatments with ointment and similar things, so that it does not corrupt what is left from the corruption; and when the wound is well cleaned, continue the healing treatment with care, until it is healed.
de squinance	squinance: weakness or frailty.
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	They old ones spoke and discussed about the cutting of the throat; but I never saw in our land anyone who did it, and it is their scriptural word.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	For those with squintiness, it is necessary that the cut in the throat, called "epiglote," be avoided; and one should not attempt help through this, because all the veins and the source of pain are in those who have a hot abscess in their mouth, or in their throat, or in both.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the tongue, it is necessary to cover the epiglote to avoid the destruction that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	It is necessary, when we want to cut the epiglottis, that we cut it in three circles or four small cuts across, between the two circles or according to the size of the cut, without touching the cartilage; and these cuts are very suitable for cutting through the epiglottis so that there is no debris, and the vessels are long.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is cautious, it is necessary that he extends the skin of the throat to its entire circumference, then cuts the heart until it reaches the sternum; and avoid any blood vessels, as we have said, and then cut through the substance, so demonstrating by the section of the stream of the sternum that it comes out from the broken place, and by the loss of voice; and leave the wound open for a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed and there is doubt about the strangulation, bring together the two edges of the wound with care, and cut it entirely through the cartilage; then administer remedies that induce motion, as long as it remains healthy.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasis says: One should not proceed until the throat is completely blocked, and the patient is judged to be near death, lacking breath.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Then they should cut the epiglottis because the patient cannot breathe, and he breathes through the wound, thus preventing death; and for this reason, the ancients command that the wound remain open until the evil of the illness has passed, which takes three or four days. And then they order the wound to be sewed up and treated, as long as it needs treatment; and I will tell you what I have seen.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw that a damsel was pierced by a knife and it entered her throat, cutting through part of the tongue; and I was called to cure her, but I found her as if dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found the blood that was coming from it; I realized that it had no strength or power to flow, but only went directly to the throat, and the veins were exposed through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I acted quickly, sewed the wound, and cured it until it was healthy; and the damsel regained her voice, returning to her normal state; so I say that in the construction of the epiglottis there is no need to be afraid.
de la grosse gorge	Of the great throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	Cystic abscesses are called "throat hernias", and they are large abscesses in the form of a white mass, most commonly found in women; there are two types: natural and accidental, or without any cause.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accidental is according to two manners: one resembles fat, and the other manner is similar to an abscess that arises from an artery; there is fear, and it is not appropriate to make incisions except in the case of a small one, and test and explore all openings: if you find it similar to fat and cannot be moved in any way, treat it as you would treat a nose, and remove it completely if necessary; wrap it well and cure it appropriately until it is perfectly healed.
des nous	From us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	Many ways are there of which I will speak, showing all their similarities; now it is necessary that I explain the distinction between origin and outcome.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that the outcome is heat and fever as long as the ebullition persists, and it completes the putrefaction; then the fever and heat subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With the new, there is neither heat nor fever nor pain, and it contains satisfaction, which is its own sac and is according to the state of the body, and begins like a grain, and becomes large; and they are according to two appearances, either greasy or moist, and have much color as I said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you approach the treatment of a new condition, that you test and inquire first about all the instrument called "intrusive", according to its form as it appears in this or that chapter.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	The method of inquiring about abscesses is to press more or less moistfully the place you find the abscess, and move your fingers in and out gently until you know the instrument has reached the center; then do this according to the size of the abscess; then extract the intrusive tool, and be careful not to tear it.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If the moisture in a cut is running clear, it has the same color as described for other abscesses; and if the intrusive tool does not bring out moisture after it has been inserted, know that it is hard, so make a cross with it and hold it like pincers, peeling it gently from each side, and take care to remove all the pus. If you cannot do this, cut it into pieces until nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	For if it does not move, the vein returns to its place many times; and if it moves slightly and does not cause great pain, it uses some corrosive powders and poultices on the wound, tightens the bandage, applies hot compresses, and treats it with various remedies until it is healed; and if the vein is large, it cuts both sides of the wound and treats it accordingly.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if the vein is stubborn or resistant and does not respond quickly, use powdered vitriol and leave it for two or three days until the wound pus forms and the inflammation of the blood diminishes; then reapply the bandage when it has subsided.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	See here the shapes of the instruments that enter the wound, and there are three types: large, medium, and small; and there are three quadrants called "albaret", and one called "breb", and they also come in three sizes: large, medium, and small, to surround fistular abscesses; and they are similar to needles with which one sews sorceries, made of bronze, iron, or silver, and those that are yellow work best for surrounding the cores of fistules; and these too come in three sizes: large, medium, and small, according to the extent of the opening.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The shapes of the hooks are much alike, as you can see: large, medium, and small; and some hooks have two barbs in three ways; and others have three barbs, also in three ways; and there are hooks with two barbs, or only one barb, and these too are necessary for their proper use.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The head of these instruments is sharp, and there are some that do not cut deeply enough to sever a vein or nerve; and from such insertions, the alemels are withdrawn in pieces, so that the patient does not lose blood when opening abscesses; and they are of three kinds: large, small, and medium, as you see; and they should never be used on dry flesh, such as legs, arms, breasts, wounds, or similar places; and no other small instrument is made, resembling the cuts of a fistula, according to this form, to stop blood.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it should never be placed in a place that heals the severing of veins, arteries, and never according to this great form.
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Never inflate the breasts of any man when they begin to be corrupted, until they seem like a woman's breasts; they remain ugly and swollen, and anyone who wishes to cure them must do so according to this form from line b to g.
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	Then scrape off the fat and apply medicinal poultices with burning charcoal, then bring together the two edges of the wound with stitches, and treat it until it is healed; if the breast sinks downward, and becomes soft due to its size, as in women, making them appear in two ribs, through two similar openings, so that one holds onto the other at the end of each, so that the larger line encloses the smaller according to this form from line b to g. Then scrape off the skin between the two edges, remove the fat, and apply what we have said about stitching and powders, as well as anything necessary for treatment, until it is healed; if it is not healed, or the incision has not been completely made, because the patient does not want to rest, or due to the discharge of blood, then you must fill the wound with moist cotton in a corrosive dressing; leave it until it absorbs the returning moisture and fat, then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	from the abscesses of armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	Abscesses that come from beneath the armpits are hard scrofulas or have lumps, and if they contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those that contain moisture should be cut according to this form, from line .b. to line .g.
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus in the abscess is drained, apply clean cotton to the wound and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton and continue with appropriate treatment until it heals.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess resembles scrofula, then do as we have said about incising scrofula, and if the wound opens, apply cautery as we have mentioned before.
de la routure de l’artere	from the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When an artery ruptures and the covering tissue (cuir) is sealed over it, many abscesses often form, along with swelling in the vein, abscesses, and other similar symptoms; this situation is very dangerous and one should not attempt to treat these abscesses, especially if they are deep within the joints and muscles and surrounded by anger (inflammation) or other conditions. It is very grave.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	You should seek iron cautery, and he who is in charge should also be vigilant, and on him who has an artery-flushing wound make a cut from above the skin long; then open the artery from its threads as much as it is uncovered; then insert a needle underneath and pierce it through to the other side, and tighten the artery with a double thread in two places, just as I have taught you for pulling out the two arteries found in the temples; then mark the place between the two threads of an instrument until there is no leftover part that can cause further harm, and treat the abscess; then apply the cure as it grows, until the link tightens; then tend to the treatment of any resulting injuries, as long as they are clean; and if the abscess is through cutting a vein, hold your hand over the entire area of the abscess, then insert the needle underneath the place you hold, and pierce it, and make a double thread so that you can pull it from the other side; then bind the abscess as I have told you, or the link to one of the two sides with two threads; and if you doubt that the thread has not gone far enough, insert another needle through all the thread underneath the entire abscess at the incision of the first needle, and tighten the threads in three places; then cut off the surplus part of the abscess until the leftover part is gone, then cut off the excess skin and leave what is attached; then cover it with a moist cloth dipped in wine and oil, and apply bandages and treatments with ointments until it is healed.
des apostemes des ners	from abscesses of nails
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Similarly to how abscesses occur in arteries and veins, nail abscesses also form when they are damaged or subjected to excessive strain, among other things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And these occur more frequently in joints and limbs, causing dislocated joints which appear as abscesses with the color of the skin, and are full of pain, not completely intact, and move abnormally in every direction, neither forward nor backward, neither downward nor upward, and those in the joints should not be covered with iron; for it might cause contraction. And those on the head or forehead cause the skin to contract.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, and it has a claw, pull it out at its base; and if it's large, suspend it with a hook, then peel it off, then cut through the flesh and heal the wound with stitches, and treat it until it is healed.
des grosses boces pendans	Des grosses boces pendans" translates to "large, dangling lips
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	It never appears in the belly alone, but is a disease called "fungus" due to its outward appearance, it has subtle roots, and large droppings; there are both small and very large ones. I have seen people with two or more funguses in their bellies that looked more like fungi than anything else, and there was no difference, they were white, had fine roots, and were constantly moist.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I collected and found in one eighteen ounces weighing, and in the other six Z., and the work of the incision is such that you watch if the patient is moist, and the color of the artery is white and moist and of subtle root; if it cleaves with a wide spatula, then perform fire cautery in your presence.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	For when cutting there often arise great complications of blood, and if it bleeds without stopping, then haste to cauterize; and if you see the patient hoping and fearful of the incision, take a well-made plug of thread, and bind the artery as we have said, and leave it for two days; then tighten it, and do not cease to pull the thread until the artery is cut off, and each time without effort; and if the roots are thick, be afraid especially when cutting near the belly, but you can well plug half of it, then cauterize so that it does not return; then cure the wound, and take care not to plug the vein which is of bad color and poor sensation and milky appearance.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For it is an abscess enlarged, and I will come to the treatment of this ulcer later.
quant li boude ist fuer	When the wound is closed due to crusting
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the appearance of the crusting comes from cauterization of the wound or fissure of the flesh, and it is on the abdomen and not in any of the bowels, as occurs in other openings, or from blood letting or cutting of veins or arteries according to what is before, or from flatulence; and if it is due to the opening through the syphilitic flesh and the emission of the bowel, then the color of the abscess resembles the color of the body, and it is a slight thing without pain, and has various openings.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when it is pressed at its openings, it returns, and sometimes becomes tight, greatly expanding at the entrance of the bath or through hard work.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is due to moisture, it is a light matter and opens easily when pressed in the hand, without constraint; and if it is due to blood, it appears through these signs: a large and hard abscess, fixed according to its quantity; and if it is due to flatulence, it feels soft upon touching, and the strain indicates whether it is the blood of an artery, a vein, or flatulence.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	If it is necessary, let the healing take place.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For in the case of abscesses, as I described in the chapter on veins and arteries, there is often doubt and fear, which can lead to death.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	If the appearance is due to an intestinal or bowel issue, instruct the patient to keep their bowels motionless and stretched out straight. Then, make incisions around the entire abscess; then command them to gently move it back and forth between your hands. Then, wrap the affected area with a strong thread or firm silk cord, ensuring it is securely fastened. Open the other half of the abscess that is stretched over the ligature and insert your finger, exploring the intestine. If you find it caught in the ligature, release it and extract the intestine from outside the abdomen. If it's the bowel, cut it at the oncine (a specific point) and remove the excess. If the artery or vein objects, gently move around them. Then return to your task and use two needles, inserting them through the cruciform opening you made; then pull the abscess in four parts using the needles, and if visible, remove the needles and let the area heal until it has dried out and the dead flesh has fallen away on its own. Finally, cure the wound as necessary and complete the treatment of the abscess as we have said, extracting blood or moisture you find, then treat the wound accordingly and sew up the abscess.
dou chancre	A cancerous ulcer
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have described in the previous section the signs of a cancerous growth, and how it should be treated with medicines, and how to avoid the use of iron in its cure; and we say that cancer will develop in the marris, requiring great caution in its treatment, and [it is] advised by the ancients that when a cancer appears in a place where it can be cut out, such as one found in the breast, or the foot, or similar areas, it should all be removed when it is in the early stage; but for one that is large and old, it is not advisable to approach it, for I have never been able to heal any of them; no one has ever healed any before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And for the work, when a cancer is in a place where it can be removed, as we have said, it is that you never purge the patient of black blood; then make the wound healthier if there is any sign of filling, and cut out the cancer from the good flesh to perform the operation; then pour on your poultices or cancer, and shave all parts, and remove it from all sides, leaving nothing; and let the blood flow out completely, and check the flesh with your hand or anything else, and if any signs of bloodletting occur during the incision of an artery or a vein, cauterize it until the wound is healed; then apply another cure until it is healed.
de ydropisie	From hydropsie (or dropsy)
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	We have previously discussed the signs of hydrops and in what way the accumulation of water occurs, as well as the symptoms of each condition, the treatments using medicine, and those using iron; these are distinct issues. And one should not apply iron to these two conditions: namely, tympanitis and ypoharche, for they are deadly. Therefore, when treating this hydrops condition, called 'eclites' with medicine, if the cure does not benefit the patient, consider if the patient is weak or has another illness in addition to hydrops, such as stomach turmoil or similar; then do not use iron, as there is doubt. And if you see a patient of strong constitution and they only have hydrops without any other illness, and are neither too young nor too old, then proceed thus: place the patient gently on your hands, and ask the assistant to press the abdomen towards the lowest part of the pain, then take the spiny spatula in this shape.
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And make incisions from both parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	Insert the point, but do not push it too far so that it can reach the intestines when pushed in, and do not break it; then observe if there is any droplet formation towards the intestines. You should make a cut three fingers deep directly below the nipple, and if the hydrops is due to liver disease, make the cut on the left side of the nipple; and if it's due to jaundice, it should be on the right, and do not let the patient lie on top of the cut so that the excess does not flow to the weak spot. Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And it resembles a thin silver chain, light of iron or gold, and in the center it has a small opening; on one side, three openings; and on the other, two, and another on the other side; and the part is cut as if a feather, which is the form of the incision that scribes make with their pen.
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	At the top of it, there is a seal, so that when the instrument comes into contact with water, it sinks immediately onto the instrument; then empty half or a third of it, for if you empty more than is necessary at this moment, by chance the patient may die due to the resolution of his spirit from the weapon, or he might lose his palm, or approach death; but empty according to the quantity of its virtue, and according to what the dispositions of the virtue of the patient indicate, and his pulses; then take the instrument and hold back the water, and it is held back now by the stop that covers the opening on the syphac, of which I spoke, so that you pierce in this way; then repeat the instrument on the other side the next day, if you see the patient suffering from it, and draw out a small amount of water; do this every day, and be careful not to let it dry up completely.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	And if you doubt about the patient, and leave much water, either by burial or hot sand, or by much sweating or a bath or in the sun, and become discolored; then cure with drying medicines until it is healed, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after extracting the water, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	from the obstruction of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	No child is born without an obstruction in the penis, or if the obstruction is small, or it is not properly aligned.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it is necessary at any time that he cannot pierce through all the tissue with a very subtle instrument according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	then insert or open the subtle plug from below, and hold it and keep it thus for three days or four, and when he wants to urinate, remove the plug and let him urinate, and then put it back; and sometimes it is not necessary at all, because the force of the urine does not allow it to stay closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	If the opening is small, it is a gentle plug for the urine as we have said, then it will enlarge.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who do not have a perforation in their place are bleary-eyed, for no one is born with a perforation at the top of the shaft, so they cannot urinate until they raise their penis; and they cannot ejaculate because the matter cannot reach the base, and it is a bad illness.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the procedure is as follows: the patient should lie on their back, then the shaft and the head should be straightened and made as thin as a feather, so that the perforation opens up as it should; and be careful of the bleeding that often occurs, and if it does, stop the bleeding with what stops blood, and treat the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	from the pustules of the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	This condition often appears on the penis, and it presents as an ugly stain; it can be either malicious or benign. You must prick them gently with a needle, drain them, and clean and dress them with moist cotton in Egyptian ointment. Then apply the healing ointment diligently until they are healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	If the condition is malicious, with a putrid black color and discharge, it requires cautery treatment.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	Once you have drained it and if the condition is deep in the penis, affecting both the inner and outer parts, you must first remove the pus inside; then treat the external part.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you treat it all together, make sure the base of the bone is not pierced, and blackness and decay appear in the bone and joint; then it is necessary to remove everything that is black and corrupt, then apply a plaster made of honey and flour from grated red apples and times, and continue with other remedies until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if decay from pus occurs, apply the lunar cautery according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	The cautery helps in two ways: that is, for the decay of pus and corruption; and if the base of the bone is corrupt and withdrawn, then it is necessary to insert or drive a cane into the bone, and pass urine through it for the patient; and when the skin is dry at the top of the bone that has not been circumcised, or there is an abscess or a wound, then in this case you must peel it with a sharp instrument until the ligaments are loosened and it is freed from the base of the bone on all sides; and if it is a difficult matter to devise, then you should peel it with a small spatula at the top of the bone and the flesh; then carefully separate them and put a fine cloth moistened in cold water over it so that it does not dry out.
de la circoncision	from circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not a dislocation like other wounds; however, when we perform this operation of our own will, particularly on children, it is essential that we make the best and lightest work for their healing.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not speak of circumcision for their children because they did not practice it in their laws, and we only have what we have acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have seen most of the masters and elders who practiced circumcision around that time, and they did it with force and all new tools; it was risky because there are two layers, and perhaps one could cut off this one and leave that one behind.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or she returns with increased pain, and the point of the affected member is not assured during cleaning, and in the case of fingernail cleaning, the iron may escape and damage the work, and often they heal without requiring further cleaning, which I have seen.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	From the cleaning done with force on all the ligament, I have found the benefit of experience, for the forces cut just as well from above as from below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Because when you press your hand, if the cut is even on both sides; and the thread should be well twisted around the skin; and the manner of the first operation should make the child think that you are only tightening the thread around the stick so gently, then you should relax it in all ways that you can; then stretch it straight between your hands, and place the forces between your hands or beneath your feet so that the infant does not see them, nor any of the instruments; then press your hand against the stick and blow into its heart, and pull it up until the part of the stick is entirely clean; then cleanse it well from the filth that is collected on it, then tie it with a double thread, and bind it to another ligament; and hold it by the second ligature at the index finger and the middle finger, and cut between the two ligaments, then lift the heart gently and pull the chief of the stick; then let the blood flow slowly, for that is how it heals; and apply powder above and below, and wrap it with a gluey membrane from a half-boiled egg mixed with rose water, confit with good rosin oil and fresh herbs, and leave it until the next day, and continue treatment as long as it is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of purification is this: both shoulders should be held still and cut open, and the shoulder blades should also be large and evenly cut.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error in purification occurs when the blood vessels inside are cut; then you should extend your finger to avoid infection; and clean it equally, and if you cannot hold it with your finger, use tweezers, and then clean it again.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if it persists for three days, and the area under the blade is swollen, leave it until the abscess has healed, gently peeling off the skin; clean it as best you can, and protect the part of the blade, which will do no harm.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Treat therefore the wound suddenly caused by a powder, which we have spoken about in our treatment of powders, and if one takes too much care, it will go above, and will not harm; treat it then, as we have said, as long as it is healthy.
dou retenement de l’urine	retention of urine
