Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	The retention of urine is due to a stone, or frozen blood, or bowels, or a deformed urethra, or similar conditions, as we have mentioned in the previous discussion; and if the urine cannot be released, and you notice that the retention is caused by a stone in the bladder or at the neck of the bladder, it is necessary for the patient to be bent over his knees; and pressure should be applied to his lower back, and he should stretch his belly upwards from the area above his back, and constrict the patient as much as possible. At this point, the neck of the bladder is forced to expel the stone located above, allowing the urine to flow; and if it does not come out, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then you should help him by using a syringe, which has the shape of a bird's feather. It should be made of fine, light silver, approximately 3.5 inches long.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And the method of urination is such that you take a double thread, tie one end with wool or cotton at the opening of the urethra, and insert the thread into the syringe; then cut off the excess wool and insert it back up to the top of the syringe, afterward greasing the syringe with oil, butter, and egg white, and placing the patient on a couch. Then gently insert the syringe into the urethra until it reaches the root of it, then fold the urethra over the end of the syringe; next, withdraw the syringe before the bladder, and let the patient feel the urination until it empties, and this is not done correctly unless the direction of the flow is followed; then pull out the thread bit by bit through all the wool, and the urine will follow the thread, then extract it forcefully, and allow the urination to continue. Repeat the syringe process until the bladder is empty, and comfort the patient.
des maladies de la vessie	Of bladder ailments
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When blisters or blood come to the bladder, where putrefaction is gathered, and you see it release water and medications, do so with all the instrument called 'clepsydre', and this is its form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	It is closed, and if it has three openings: two on one side and one on the other, as you see; and the hair of the container by which the medicine is poured out is such that it effectively stops the flow without addition, if one can drain the moisture and push as much as needed; and when you see your medicines settle in the bladder, place the head of the vessel into the moisture and draw out the liquid that is inside. Draw out the moisture until the vessel is empty, then refill it and pour it back in with force; the moisture will enter within and immediately reach the bladder, so that the patient feels it; and this is the form of the subtle enema by which one enemas the bladder: thus:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And it is of silver or gold, and the joint is higher; then open the chest where the ribs separate; take a sheep's bladder and fill it with the moisture you wish to use for enema; tie it between the two breasts with a good double thread, and warm the moisture over fire. Then insert the nozzle of the enema into the anus, and press your hand on the bladder until all the moisture has reached the bladder; and if you do not have a bladder, take a piece of parchment, make a circle of it, and pierce it roundly; then thread a strong string through these holes, assemble the circle as one would a dal, and put inside what you wish to use: oil, moisture, and water. Tie it with the instrument, and do as you did with the bladder, pressing your hand until the moisture reaches the bladder.
de la piere	from the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already discussed the methods for dealing with stones and their extraction, along with various medicinal approaches; I have also explained the distinction between stone formations in joints and other signs, and specified which types of stones require surgical intervention, be it in the bladder or the urethra; I will now describe these matters clearly and concisely.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I assert that kidney stones, which are trapped in the bladder, occur more frequently in children, and this is a sign of acute urinary tract infection, resembling clear urine in its subtlety; it opens the urethra, greatly paining the patient, and often causes frequent urination, leading to difficulty; these infections erode the urinary tract's foundations. The cure for children suffering from such stones is relatively mild until they reach four years of age, but it becomes much more difficult in older individuals, particularly those between youth and old age. The treatment is lighter for patients with larger stones compared to those with smaller ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to treatment, it is necessary first to purify the patient with a purge to draw out all the impurities from the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it often gets stuck when trying to remove the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the patient by the feet and straighten them and move them downwards so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, never rising back up; then place him between your hands with his hands beneath his thighs, so that the bladder is tilted downwards; then tie him and feel inside. If you sense the stone in a certain spot, hurry now to cut into the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if it does not come out by pressing, moisten your index finger with oil from your left hand, and the patient is in pain, or your middle finger, and the patient is young and strong; then press it back into its socket, hold the stone, and when you feel it on your finger, if it is at the base of the bladder; then press down on your finger, and push the stone out from where you saw it cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And instruct the assistant to press the bladder with their hand, and order them to extend their right hand above, and remove the skin from their left hand beneath the bladders where the cut was made; then pull out the stone, which shapes itself as follows:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And they make an incision between what is between the cheeks and the foundation, not in the middle but on the side of the left nipple; and it should be straight on the stone, and your two fingers should be always on the foundation, and the blade should be cut wide outwardly and narrow inwardly, according to the quantity of the stone, not too large; so that the pressure from the finger on the foundation causes it to come out without effort; and know that there is a stone with angles and margins: then it needs to be pulled out; and if it is in a place below, similar to a glans, and round, whose exit is light.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	If there are angles and margins, make the cut larger; and if it does not come out, you need to use pliers that are as sharp as a file at the tip, in order to pull the stone so that it does not escape; or you can insert a delicate curved instrument at the tip; and if you cannot do it this way, open up a little the wound, and if it is covered with skin, pull it out with vitriol; and if there are more than one stones, first pull out the largest one from the neck of the bladder, then cut around it, then pull it out, and the smaller ones after.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, as it should be treated carefully, and make a larger wound.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	For two things can happen to the patient: he dies, or his urine flows again through the wound, because the muscles cannot close it; but nevertheless, make every effort to pull out the splinters with tweezers, as long as you are pulling them piece by piece, and when you have completed your work, apply the wound with incense and aloe and dragon's blood, and bind it tightly, and place over it a moist cloth soaked in oil and wine, or oil and rosewater and cold water, to soothe the hot abscess; then dress the patient's neck and do not loosen the bandage for three days.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you dislocate it, if a lot of warm oil and water arises, then apply curative ointment and basilic ointment until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if abscesses and corrosion appear in the wound, and congelations of blood in the bladder, and it is retarded by urine, which is known to happen without effort with the urine: then press your finger into the wound and extract the blood, for if it remains, it will corrode the bladder and cause putrefaction; then clean the wound with water and herbs, and aid it in every way you know, until it is healed; and remember that whenever you treat it, you should bind both thighs together and apply medicines to the affected area.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the stone is small and it is passed through the urethra, and stuck inside, and urine cannot pass; if you treat this as I say, cutting many times, then one is excused from cutting due to this treatment.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have tested it thusly.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	Take the iron at the forefront according to this form, and insert it into the stone at three angles in one firebrand.
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take a thread and tie it around the urethra beyond the stone, so that it cannot go back into the bladder; then push the iron lightly into the urethra until it reaches the stone; and turn the iron in your hand slowly into the stone, as much as you can, so that you pierce the stone from another side; and soon urine will come out, then press your hand on what is remaining of the stone inside the urethra.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is sometimes broken and jumps out with urine, and rubs the patient; and if you cannot do this for any reason, then insert a thread into the stone from below and above, then make the stick into the stone between the two threads, then pull it out forcefully, and loosen the thread, and clean up the congealed blood in the wound; and treat it until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	of women's stone" 
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It is first that a stone is formed in women, and if it happens at all, the cure is difficult, and it is hindered by three things: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; the second is that it is not possible to find a woman well-versed who uncovers herself for treatment, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	The third reason is that it may be impossible to find a woman well-versed in this art of healing; the fourth reason is that if the stone in the woman is larger and more firm than the man's, then a deeper incision must be made, and great caution is required. If such necessity arises, you should engage a skilled midwife, and if you cannot find one, seek a woman who has some knowledge of this art, or a woman wise in the ways of women; she should be instructed to perform what you command regarding the examination of the stone. You must pay close attention to whether the woman is a virgin. Then she should push her left hand down into the abdomen and press on the bladder. If she finds the stone, she should extract it from under her thumb and recommend that the patient press his left thumb against his bladder.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If she has a stone, it is necessary that she move it gradually from the entrance of the bladder to the inside, until it reaches the root of the thigh; then cut into the stone at the root of the thigh against the middle towards the inside, where it is moved and feels the stone in that part; and do not move your hand over or under the stone, nor make the incision too deep at first; then press the thigh, if you feel the stone so sharp in the wound, as long as the stone can come out, and know that there are many types of stones: namely, small and large and rough and smooth, long and round, and those with ribs.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	knowing these things, to know the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if the wound does not heal, put vitriol powder on it and keep it there for an hour until the wound is cleansed; then return to your work while the stone is still hard, and have the tools I told you for removing stones from humans to assist you in your task; and if the wound does not heal, and it's an artery that's cut, apply powder to the spot and press with cloth and bandages, and do not repeat this, leave the stone and do not try to extract it, unless the patient dies; then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is calmed and the eyes open, return to your work while the stone is still hard.
de hernie carnouse	of hernia flesh
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Moisture is nothing other than a gathering of white or sweet fluid, which comes out from the heart of objects, containing the vital force; and it is called 'white' (or 'sweet'), and never properly part of the vital force itself; and this is the skin of the object between the white (or sweet) fluid that we have spoken of; and there is no harm in this.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this fluid is due to weakness that affects the objects, and this material expands.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And it never comes from impact on the objects, and this moisture has many colors: sometimes it declines to jaundice, or is without color, or black, or clear white; these are signs that this gathering has occurred, because if it is the white (or sweet) fluid we have spoken of, then the abscesses are red, long, resembling a vital force, and do not open the objects, as they are surrounded by moisture.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if there is moisture in the wound, if the abscess is red with part of the flesh, then one thinks it's another flesh; and if the moisture is between the skin and the white tissue, it smells well; then, when you want to know the color of the moisture, test all the depth of the wound, from which its form will be known.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	Accordingly, after testing the wound, judge what is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we treat it with iron, it is necessary that the patient be healed according to his ability and the fullness of his body; then put him on his back, on something slightly raised, and place many sheets under him; then sit him up on his left side, and command the assistant to sit at his right, and extend the stick to one of the two ribs in the heart of the chest; then take the scalpel, and cut the skin of the chest from above to below the knuckles, making a straight incision by drawing the skin of the chest up to the white part, scraping it gently according to its strength; then make a large perforation in the tissue with water at a wide opening, and drain all the water, and then apply the bandages, and pull the tissue upward; and do not touch the heart of the ribs, but only the tissue; cut around him carefully, in pieces as thin as possible, so that if you do not cut it sharply, the water will return; and if the flesh jumps out of your hand, put it back in its place when you have completed the work with the tissue; then sew together the two leaves of the heart ribs with a stitch, and treat it like other wounds until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the heart corrupted by another disease, it is necessary that you hold the vessels that are suspended, in doubt of the flow of blood; then cut off the coagulum from the entire suspension, and extract the blood, and treat it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And if the blood is mixed in two parts, knowing that these are two branches, cut off the other part just as you did with the first, then dry the wound and place it with clean lint moistened in rose oil; and put another layer of lint moistened in wine and oil, and place the two compresses on top of each other, and cover them with double-layered cloth, and bind it tightly to all parts according to this form.
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take two strips of cloth, made of chopped wool according to this form, and sew them together at the throat of the trousers, one strip covering the base up to the back, and the other on the palm side; then another two strips over the two legs, and bring them all together in the loop of the trousers. Never use this cautery with a metal tool of iron size, but rather take a delicate cautery knife, cut through the skin of the coions, and heat it as we have said, until the white substance that holds the water is exposed; if you take the cautery in this way, pierce the syph (white substance) as before, and scorch with this delicate hot cautery.
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And the cup should be used in all ways that you can, as long as you drain everything; and be sure that the fire does not touch the wound; and know that this work is safer; and move carefully to avoid blood let down, and consider the work of surgery; and if anything goes against you, whether it's an abscess or blood let down or another complication, then treat what goes against you, according to what has been said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	If the patient is afraid and does not want to undergo this operation because of its horror, then perform the perforation as I have told you, and make sure that when you are certain through the signs that we have mentioned that the bleeding has stopped, place the patient in a high seat; then incise the abscess from below, in the deepest part, making a wide opening throughout the abscess, and insert the perforation deeply into the flesh; let the discharge of pus flow freely. Then apply cotton on top and bind it, allowing the remaining pus to drain; treat the wound until it heals. If a clean bandage does not prevent the pus from coming out through the wound's opening, you should insert a needle or an instrument used to draw out water from dropsy patients, in the shape as mentioned before; open up the abscess again, and know that the pus will return and gather after six months or so, and when it gathers again as before, then the patient's condition will improve.
de l’aposteme des coions	from the abscess of hairs
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	Knowing that in this branch there are numerous dangers, which is why it seems better to leave it; and I will tell you about the work and the similar conditions of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I therefore say that many abscesses occur where hairs are involved, and most often with hair; and this is in many cases.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	This is to know about the excessive acidity and ague that extends to the hairs, or from impact; and the color of the abscess is according to the color of the flesh; it does not cause pain, and it is a serious abscess; and sometimes there are many dark, pus-filled, and red abscesses, and they do not come from any new artery or swelling of a vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is from an artery, if it is contracted by the heat of an abscess above, when you press it with your fingers; and it is not appropriate that you touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	The one who is made of vein inflammation is contracted by the arrangement at the expression of the touch of the fingers, and can be cut well in this shape, and in other parts; and it is what you take the heart of the clots, then the heat is above, and the pain goes away from all parts of the heat.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the heat is already solid with these inflamed parts, then it is necessary that you drain the heat and cut it; and if it is away from the heat, or in those who are inside the veins, then it is necessary that you free all of this tension, and cut it properly.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the source of pain is behind, it is necessary that you remove it entirely and extract the foreign body, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your work is completed, immediately apply woolen cloth soaked in rose oil and wine to the wound, and then use other remedies until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the testicles
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is an abscess wrapped in a covering similar to a boil, with the testicles swollen and painful; it renders the patient severely ill, almost as much as the one mentioned above. Nevertheless, we will tell you the work of its treatment, according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	You should make the patient lie on an elevated surface, then hang the suspended parts below their arms, extending them fully; next, with a large, sharp spatula, cut across the vessels, as long as they remain uncovered, and peel away from each side, as we said in extracting arteries located in temples. Then insert a needle where there is a double thread, tie it to the first joint where the vein appeared, and then tie it to the other end; straighten the parts correctly, according to the length of the body, and remove the corrupted moisture. Treat the wound like any other, so that none of the vessels leak; for this causes no harm, and all vessels will receive veins, so it is necessary to draw the vessels through all the vessels, so that the oesophagus does not lose its nourishment due to vessel incision, dries up, and cannot help itself.
de la routure dou syfac	From the rupture of the sinew.
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	The symptoms of this condition occur either through the rupture itself or from the extension in the abdomen in the region of the angles, causing the intestines to descend from that rupture into one of the coils; and this rupture is either due to the sinew's section or its stretching, and these two modes of occurrence arise from various causes: impact, a jump, straining, lifting heavy objects, and similar actions; and the signs when it is due to the stretching of the sinew include a gradual occurrence over a long period and not suddenly, and the abscess remains equal towards the entire depth, since the sinew pushes the intestines.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are when it is from the incision that sudden pain occurs, and diverse abscesses appear beneath the skin near, and this is due to the exit of intestines and flesh from the syphilitic fire.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And never remove the stitches with the intestines, which remain stuck and cause great pain to the patient, especially when pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these poor treatments with iron, for which one must be wary.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	And the method of treatment is that you command the patient to move the intestine with their fingers inside the wound, if they can; then carefully lift it onto your hands and gently press on the cuisses; then stretch the skin above, and cut through all the skin from the long side; then pull the intestines towards you; open the wound and ensure nothing is trapped or constricted; next, insert your index finger into what follows the intestine, between the white matter beneath the skin and the flesh of the testicle, and between the second matter, and remove what is behind the testicle, and between the second matter. Then move your right hand inside the scrotum and extend the white matter in your left hand above it; gently pull on the testicle towards the abdomen if any intestine or white matter is trapped. Take a needle with a thick thread of about four threads and insert it into the rear part of the testicle after the skin; then cut off the visible parts of the thread as much as possible. Assemble the remaining threads in a cross pattern, and tie them firmly from both sides; then wrap the testicles with the threads and tie them together so that no foreign bodies can enter the wound. Place the first long tie two hand-breadths away, and after these two ties, leave the skin beneath the testicle free for about the width of a finger; then make another tie at a distance from the first one as indicated by its length. After all this, cut off the excess skin beneath the testicles, as we have said before; then apply moist wool to the wound and dress it with thread, as mentioned previously.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And never should the white skin be cauterized as we have said, after incision, out of fear of blood flow.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For this happens often, and leaves the wound open until it heals on its own; if it takes too long to close, then apply hot water, as we have said, until it heals; then treat the wound with another remedy, until it is completely healed.
de hernie carnouse	hernias
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this illness, never has anyone dared to treat it with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the ancients say that it is made like a root that is assembled with a joint, in such a way that you bind the vessels after cutting them lightly on the inside, then cut through the middle and treat the abscess of him who opens, until the vessels stop bleeding; and cure it as we have said, while it is healthy.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	No rupture should occur from a violent attack, as we have said, and open the vessels; nor should any intestines drop out as if they were severed, and if they do, it is bad, and repair them every hour; however, if it persists too long at this point, one may think there is an abscess or gangrene, until the intestines drop out; and this happens due to the spread of gangrene in the wound, as we have said, for it extends, then softens and swells the vessels and opens them; and its cure is by cauterization, as we have previously said; and never should it be cured with iron in this manner. And so, the patient should lie on his back, then cut the vessel of the rupture deeply according to the quantity of three fingers' width; and then extract the gangrene that lies beneath the usual skin, then take a stick and put it over the visible part of the gangrene; and press it firmly in the abdomen, then cut both the two visible parts of the gangrene on top of the stick, and remove them; then remove the stick, and do not cover the gangrene or extend it or anything else, as I have told you about the cure for intestines; then cure it with the cure for wounds.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you treat the wounds, if they become infected and heal the wound, as long as it is clean.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The remedy is restrictive, and has no appearance in the fracture, but the cauterization moves on this side, and is closer to healing.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the hard skin on the joints
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Often, the skin of the joints becomes soft in no particular man, because the muscles within are relaxed, and it is easy to see. If one wishes to cure it, one must make the patient lie on his back and cut away the softened skin from the natural skin; then bring the two edges together with a stitch or three firmly, depending on how much of the soft skin needs to be removed; then cut between the stitches and treat the wound as one would any other, until it heals, and pull out the thread.
dou chastrement	Dou chastrement (Double castration)
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	You know that castration is condemned in our law, and for this reason I would not like to talk about it in this book; there are only two ways to deal with it: one is that you respond wisely when asked, and show wisdom in the cure; the other is because we often need castration of certain animals to help us, such as goats, sheep, cats, and others.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say therefore that castration is done according to two methods: either by attraction or by incision.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In the method where we use attraction, make the animal sit in hot water until the testicles are softened and relaxed; then grasp them firmly in your hand until they return to their normal state and you no longer feel them.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	From castration by sword: You must tie the animal and press the skin of the testicles with your left hand, then tie the suspensory cord, and cut each one to the root when you have well lacerated them; and leave no seed there, especially the subtle seed on the veins; and this method of castration is superior to that which is done by attraction, because at attraction, by chance, something of the testicles remains, which excites lust in the animal; then treat the wound until it is healthy.
des hermofrodites	of hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	A hermaphrodite is in two manners like men: one is when between the two testicles the opening is also shaped like the figure of a woman, with hair, and he never urinates with a penis.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And another way is for women; it extends from the wrist like a rod and has two joints.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the treatment for hunger and thirst is to release all the blocked channels, and treat them like other wounds; in the second way, for men whose urine comes out through the skin of the testicles, there is no cure.
de la tentigene	of the goiter
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	Goiter is a blocked channel in the natural part, so ugly to see; no woman can move it as much as a hand, and that is its treatment.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	It is necessary that you hold the excess of the tendon in your hand or with hooks, and cut it lightly; do not cut too deeply, so as to avoid complications from bleeding, then apply other remedies until it is healed; and for another condition that arises at the mouth of a wound, and spreads, and perhaps jumps, and resembles a cow, and for this reason the ancients called it "cow disease.
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	It is necessary that you cut it, as we said of the tendon, and treat it until it is healed.
de erratique	erratic
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	Erratic is the nature of a woman if her condition is not properly understood, or if the opening is small; it is either innate by birth, or accidental due to illness that comes upon her; or it is caused by tight clothing, or some subtle or extreme pain, and it occurs in any part: in the stomach, side, or back, or wherever; and it affects conception, childbirth, and perhaps even the flowers (breast milk) to be had; and knowledge of these things comes from observation of the body.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the inflammation is close to the surface, it may be due to your own doing or to some external cause.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is a soft and subtle muscle, close to the bones, if you act quickly, thus: place your two index fingers together, and have the woman lie on her back, spreading her legs; then form both sides of the muscle until the soft tissue is completely healed, and pressure can be applied. Then take wool, moisten it in oil, and apply it to the area, making the woman lie down at home each day so that she cannot move.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the muscle is hard and thick, then it is necessary that you cut it with a scalpel resembling a sheet of myrtle.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the swelling is from heat, suspend it with a splint and bandage; have medicines that stop blood flow, such as horse chestnut, dragon's blood, incense, together with abundant egg whites; then apply a broad poultice so that the wound cannot heal; and thus for a long time, and then apply a dry linen cloth; and continue other treatments until it is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when fever comes from heat, if it is not an abscess, then cover in this way: if it is not a severe case.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For an abscess that is severe during fever, do not attempt to treat with fire.
des emorroides	Of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins that, without usual care, can become severe; and in this division, we have previously discussed the appearances, signs, and I will now describe those that receive treatment.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and their complications, when they are completely in the anus, and they do not appear by touch, can only be cured with heat.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those that are at the opening of the anus can be felt; these are those that can be treated.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	It is necessary that you place the woman in a cold house, then stretch her limbs with tongs, and compress them at their roots, then sprinkle medicinal herbs to stop blood flow, such as oak bark, dragon's blood, incense, and similar things; then bind her feet to the wall for an hour, then immerse her in cold water. And when blood comes out, let it sit in a decoction of sumac, pomegranate peel, gall, and similar things, and then take oats flour, mix it with honey and wax, and make paste to apply on her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it becomes saturated, that is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If no, then make the patient inhale cups on his back and on his breasts without causing harm; then take cloth, and dampen it in the juice of plantain or in the juice of hawthorn with old wine, and apply to the place.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess has healed, continue the treatment with the dressing as long as it remains clean; and that which is called "albathir" is red and resembles a hard lump, so it should be covered as I have said in the previous text; then treat it until it is clean.
des apostemes de la marris	about abscesses of the mare (presumably referring to a female horse)
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many kinds of abscesses occur in the body, such as the chancre, and previous abscesses, and sores, and blisters, and fistulas, and hemorrhoids, and hot abscesses, and many other illnesses that I have mentioned in the section.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	Therefore, in this treatment, we should address the hot abscess that occurs in the body, which is not like other abscesses that are bow-shaped; and if you have experience with making incisions, pay attention to when the abscess begins to form, and it is full of heat and fever, and turns red if you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Then do not hasten to pierce, but make the patient suffer until the pain is eased; then have the afflicted person sit in a comfortable position and rest his/her back, bending the legs slightly away from each other; let the knees be bent, and place the arms beneath the genitals, binding them well with a good bandage. Then insert the blade towards the right side of the wound, and use the instrument to open it, from which this form arises; and you must first stick the point into it, in order to know the depth of the wound, so that what enters through the instrument does not go further than necessary, causing harm to the patient; and if the instrument is too large, then cover the depth of the wound with cloth, so that the instrument does not hurt. And you should place the tip of the instrument above, and keep it lubricated.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscess opens and it is incised with a gentle hand, if it is necessary to cover the wound, use a spatula; and when the bowel is emptied, it is necessary to place moist cotton in rose oil or dry green oil in the wound, all the way to the edge of the wound, and then cover it from outside with a clean, wet cloth, soaked in cooked mullein or alder bark; then treat it after two days of dressing, as long as it heals; and never lift the bandage and the wound with a cleanser of water and honey, and then water or cooked lily roots and alder bark are used. Then return to dressing.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is healed in the bed, it is necessary to be careful not to use fire, but treat it as we have said in the previous section.
de l’enfantement	From childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	Knowledge of childbirth is the first step for understanding the natural form of childbearing, and its signs are when you see a woman in labor, pressing down, and desiring to smell the air: then hasten the baby's exit. Then know that these children are born according to nature, coming out head first, and seconding with them; and when you see these signs, gently press her stomach so that the child comes out quickly; for as it descends onto its head, it seconding with him, and the mother delivers her excesses through good cleansing; and this is how it should be, otherwise it does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For it comes at no time upon his feet, but pierces the body or the bone, or the hands, or comes upon his belly, or back, and turns by chance upon his neck, and in other evil forms; therefore it is necessary for the surgeon to be wise and subtle in these things, and wary of error and deception, and I will show you all the figures how he should help.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the evil comes upon his head through natural causes, and a woman is in labor and her strength is weak, then she should be placed on a bed or held by other women; and take the nature of oil or fennel seeds cooked, and then apply the small spatula between her fingers whose shape is as follows:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	and cut through the second joint, and saw off its finger as much as the moisture that is stuck inside; and press the woman's belly until the child descends, and if it does not descend, then it is necessary to enema the woman with fenumigall of fenugreek mixed with oil of sesame; then make her sneeze and blow her nose for a while, keeping her mouth and nose closed for an hour: now the child will come out.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if both hands are stuck out, it is necessary to gently dislocate them one by one; and if they still cannot enter, put the woman on her back and raise her feet upwards; then remove the support from the ground and make the woman lie down so she does not try to stand up; and if her hands cannot enter, and the child dies inside, cut off the hands at the joint closest to the body, extract the child, and dislocate them in the same way.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	From the birth of the child on its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child is born on its feet, it needs to be pushed up, and then pulled back little by little until it is even; then press on the feet and extend them little by little.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	Have them jump as high as their feet allow if commanded to press, and make them sneeze by the condition; if they jump far, God willing.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it does not happen as we have said, pull it back little by little according to nature.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it becomes slightly better.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it does not come as we have said, take a small amount of musk, oil of rose petals, and gum resin, and grind them all in a mortar; then apply this preparation to the woman's vulva both internally and externally, and let her sit in warm water up to her ribs; when she is moistened, make a collar of myrrh and place it around her, leaving it for an hour. Then have her sit on a seat, and have her sneeze, tighten her mouth and nose, and gently press her abdomen, as the child is now ready to be born.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	From the emergence of the child on its knees.
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes in this form, he should move his hands little by little; then rest on his collarbone, and let the feet hang down, lying on his side; and he bends his hands little by little, then takes hold of the hands on the belly, and removes the cushions from underneath until it is completely uncovered downwards; and if the child does not jump, take hold of the feet and move them, then lift the belly upwards, and turn the hands inside out; and gently deliver the child little by little; and tell the woman to press herself as the child emerges.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	From the birth of the child who comes with a strong hand during
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	I know how to bring the hand back: if it cannot be brought back, then have the woman sit up and try again; if she cannot go, place her on a bed with her legs bent; then apply the muscle relaxant I mentioned; and if she still does not give birth, have her sit on a chair, and study how to bring the hand back; deliver the child according to nature, and make her sneeze, and tell her to push as hard as possible.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	from the birth of the child on its chest, with its hands spread and its face turned away from its mother's back.
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	I want the patient to hold their hand, then twist it little by little and gently; and when it is even, he should apply a light, muscly compress of herbs and oil, as we have said, then instruct him that it moves little by little; and when you have done this, let it rest on a pillow, and command him to press; and make him sneeze.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	in the same way for all the rest
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it comes to handling this in the same way for all parts, if the seconding (presumably a bandage or dressing) is stuck to your fingernail, allow the moisture to drain; and if it becomes fixed to his face or neck, cut it from the corner of the mouth so that it does not hold on, and the child may die. Then, remove the child, ensuring you have placed him as appropriate, and command the woman to press herself at regular intervals. Afterward, gently untie.
de l’issue des gemelz	from the opening of the joints
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	You know that twins are born many times, and never three or four; and this is not a strange thing, and it often happens.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	Twins are strange things and do not live, they have no name; I know that they are multiplied, and their destinies are determined by the will of God who created them, who is bound to the womb; and they never emerge as naturally as any other child, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they are born severely deformed, as we have said, and the treatment is subtle, making slow and gentle movements, it should be done as it deserves for their salvation.
de plusors enfans	from many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	They should never be formed in the marris I or II or III or IV or V or VI or VII, or more than XV, and are entirely shaped like a child according to the measurement of his wise heart, and it is necessary that the experienced doctor knows all this, for sometimes a similar thing may occur; he must act accordingly.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you treat a woman who has lost her child, as I mentioned in the previous section, and there is no movement, and you are forced to act by hand; it is important that you know if the woman is of healthy constitution and has not suffered any ill effects from the loss of her child; she should be placed on her back, with her legs inclined downwards and raised; the physician should apply a poultice of two parts, or keep her in bed so as not to disturb her during the descent of the child.
