Then, moisten the mouth of the womb with oily eye drops mixed with fennel and linseed, and apply this mixture to the midwife's hands. Next, gently press the womb, then remove any foreign bodies that might be blocking the passage, and take care that the baby does not descend onto her head; if it is, pin or tie it to her body, and place the cord between her two fingers of her left hand, gently pressing the womb with her right hand until the object becomes free. The shape of the instrument used for this process is as follows:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Then find another joint, where you need it most, so that the extraction is even; and then equally move it from side to side to get it to come out, and it will be notched for holding, just like this form.
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	If a part remains, apply no oil to its joints, and press it in that part, while pulling the other part; and if nothing remains, place this joint higher up, and do this until it comes out completely.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes forward before the other and cannot return due to tightness, you should wrap it up with a cloth until it comes out completely; then cut at the joint of the plant or the finger, and do the same for the other hand, and hold the feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if the child's foot is large and twisted at birth, and has a sharp point collected, it is necessary that you insert the spiny spatula between your fingers, and make the twist and extract the water; or you can use the instrument called 'almidach', from which the form comes with the instruments of this chapter; and thus do the same for the child who has a large head naturally; and then pull out the bones with pincers, and if the foot jumps out and is constrained by force, it may be split, until the moisture at the worst exit is gone; and if it cannot come out, cut it into pieces as you can; and if it is swollen in the belly or under the ribs, pierce it until the moisture runs.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the fever is on his feet, it is a light attraction, and the direction towards the mouth of the wound is gentle.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if it is twisted in the belly or the bowels, then you must extract it with the hand wrapped in a cloth; and make an incision in the belly or the bowels, as much as the moisture that is there; and if another member is dislocated and the stool remains, he should press his hand from the wound towards the mouth of the wound, and pull strongly; then he should use a knife or hook, and pull it out; and if the mouth of the wound is narrowed by the hot abscess that has come, it is not appropriate to work on it, but rather to apply moist and greasy things; and apply poultices, and immerse in lukewarm water that softens and moistens.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the dislocation is on his side, you can put it back even, as we have said about a living child; and if that is not possible, break it into pieces and leave nothing of the broken part.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, apply what we have said about abscesses that come from the wound; and if bleeding occurs, place it in strong restraint, and apply other remedies.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman whose stomach had been cut open, and another was made over it, and I removed the other wounds.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, there appears an abscess in the cheek, it swells until it opens, and begins to cause great pain.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called upon for treatment, and I thought for a long time, but could not heal the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied a strong poultice, and an bone emerged, and after a few days, others followed.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was very amazed because this belly has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	If I thought this was a bone from a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I examined the wound and found a bone in my hand, as long as the woman's arm was; I left it there for some time until it became a little less painful. And I have never recorded this chapter to be used only when a master encounters something strange and knows how to help.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to bring the wife back to her place.
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	After this comes the form of pressure, with which books are bound; and at its turn to the other side, it goes to the two ends of the strings.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	Nevertheless, the horns should be more subtle in their tightening, and made of ebony or box; and the mouth opening should be two fingers wide, and the margin of the wood one palm and a half long; and between the two sides there should be an adjustment of this same horn, which is firmly attached to both, about halfway through a palm length or slightly more; and this adjustment is inserted into the mare's mouth when turning the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, more subtle and lighter in appearance, should be made of ebony or boxwood, resembling pliers; and it has two adjustments, as you can see, one palm length long and two fingers wide; and when opening the mare with the entire instrument, have the woman lie down on her side, with her legs spread apart, then insert both adjustments into the mare simultaneously, holding the base of the instrument between her thighs; then open your hand over the entire instrument, just as you did with the pliers, according to the amount that opens the mare's mouth, until it reaches its desired position.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	The surgical instruments are all diverse, and they have many similar appearances; and when the expert has arranged them, the work is quicker performed, and requires greater skill from the operators for their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Even if you do not understand the instrument, you should not use it without arranging it properly, as its necessity is no excuse for improper handling.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the secondine (a device used during childbirth) is in place, it is important that you instruct the patient to hold her breath and then exhale slowly while squeezing her hands to her mouth and nose. If she does this, it will be good.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If it is not possible, take I a hot compress or poultice and apply herbs that can open the mouth of the wound, such as calament, rue, anis, chamomile, cassia, and centaury; all these herbs, or any of them, should be cooked or steeped in water over fire. Then place one hot compress over the wound and the other over its opening, and keep it there until the vapors go into the wound; then make the patient sneeze, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the dislocation is severe, proceed with the next step.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	If, after this treatment, the dislocation persists but is not too severe, instruct the patient to moisten their left hand with sesame oil or alum water and then wrap it in a bandage. They should hold the dislocated part gently and stretch it out little by little straightening it, so that the joint does not pop out when they release it; but they must move it slightly to the right and to the left and then treat it. It will come back and realign itself.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the mouth of the wound is too tight, we have said the remedy of sneezing and herb fumigation; and if it does not respond to all that we have said, be careful not to drain it; but he who has a wound in the mouth, should tie it to the woman's thigh, then cleanse it with a four-ingredient ointment; it will heal and return, and go away, but nevertheless, when it opens, there is a bad smell in the stomach and head, and turns blue on the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	Therefore, suitable fumigations should be used: no one among the ancients has tried fumigation with arugula and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The shape of the instrument with which a woman is restrained from bleeding and pain is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it is made of glass similar to a tube, and the narrow end is placed in nature, while the wider part is over the fire; and the steam should be on the coals until they are burned out, then another one begins.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born who have not had their foundation pierced, but it is covered with a thin layer of skin: therefore, the nurse should pierce this layer gently with her finger, and do not use an acute instrument, and hold the wound closed so that she does not touch it; then apply moist linen dipped in wine and oil, and treat the wound with medicine until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it does not return, if you insert or remove a plug from the nose, and leave it for several days, and when the child wants to go to sleep, it becomes dislocated.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And this sudden stop of the wound or abscess should never be left untreated; if it is a sudden closure, then it must be treated as we have said about the plug in the nose.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula from its origin
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistules that originate from beneath the fundament are larger and more significant than those that come from above; in cases of a single or multiple fistula, and when this nodulation is ancient, it opens up again, still moist with white or subtle pus, and these fistulas do not heal; they are recognized by the discharge or air coming out when the patient evacuates, and sometimes they burst spontaneously.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if the ulcers pierce through to the bladder, and half of the penis; and reach up to the hip joint, and even to the calve muscle.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus you recognize the ulcer when it penetrates deeply and is not superficial: and then you insert your index finger into the anus and push a thin needle of iron or steel into the fistula, when there is no curvature.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if it has curvature, and you insert a thin probe or a horsehair, as long as you feel the resistance of the probe or hair with your finger; and if you do not feel anything, and there is no expulsion of pus or wind, as we have said, know that it does not penetrate; be careful in treating it.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula persists up to the bladder or up to the urethra, if it lets go of the urine and cannot be healed with medicine.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it is cut near the joint of the thigh, then the veins are exposed up to the place; if there is no twisting or pain around it, and it remains bent, and medicine nor any bandage helps, then there is no cure for these persistent fistulas other than effort and futility from foolish people who meddle.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In the case where it is not persistent and not ancient, there is hope for healing by fire, as I have experienced, and the patient lies on their back between your hands; then stretch their legs up to their thighs, and bring their knees towards their chest; then insert a thin arrow, or a needle if there is twisting, as long as you know where the fistula is.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels pain in the foundations, it is necessary that you press your index finger there, so that he feels the point pierce; and if you discover any discomfort or pain between your thumb and forefinger, then know that it is persistent; unless it works itself out, it cannot be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	Nevertheless, no one can be completely healed of this, but it happens rarely; and the aid that is done consists in applying a gentle cautery according to the size of the fistula, as has been said above; and burn the entire area inside the fistula until it comes out from the foundation; and do this two or three times, until you know that these charred marks have healed, which resemble an eagle's feather; then apply moist compresses, until the wound is completely healed, then finish with a treatment that promotes healing, drawing and sealing.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If he is in such a state, it is good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If the wound is not clean in this way; and if there is a gap between the edges, and it does not pierce to the bone which is the foundation, place a thick covering of cloth or something similar between your two fingers and the gap, and you will see the fistula following the covering towards the heart; if it reaches the beginning of the fistula, remove it immediately before the covering, and then apply cautery afterwards, as much as it goes to the top of the covering; and the covering will be delivered and healed; then beware of those false signs that resemble a bird's feather, and do not hesitate.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if it causes you pain and cuts between you and the work, cauterize it with fire or medicated salve.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For fire cautery combines two good things: namely, the burning of these prepared parts, and the absorption of blood and the drying of moisture; then treat the wound with moistened butter or crushed herbs, as long as the bowels are soft, and pull out the burned parts from the bowels; then heal the wound with hot compresses and dry medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it becomes healthy and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula appears all the way to the bottom of the foundation, and it is removed from the body, if you press down on its origin or foundation, it will hurt.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the tentation, and between them is the cloth or the bandage or the charred, or it is ready to pierce, if there is no other way of escape and hope, through the administration of one of the three methods: you cauterize it as we have said, or cut it all the way to the bottom, or if you can, remove the tentation and cure it as before; do not go too deep, that you do not cut into the tissue holding the foundation, and the discharges come through the other side against your will; then cure it as we have said. Perhaps it will heal, or you remove that cover and clean it after it has been cut away from the base, either with a tent or another pointed instrument; then disinfect the infected wound, as best you can; try to restore the wound, and keep the fistula at bay in the area beyond the base. If it is a lighter matter for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And never are ulcers formed in this manner: and it is when you push the tent into the ulcer, and it is on the side near the foundation of the skin above, then take a tent-shaped knife at the top according to this form:
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And then insert the thread crookedly in two places, and push the tent all along the ulcer until it reaches the top.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is still stuck at the base of the skin, then pull out the thread from that hole, and insert your finger or the base again; take hold of the thread's end, and bring the two parts together, pressing them against each other, and leave it for one to two days; do not touch it, until the threads have healed and the wound is sealed and clean.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not open, try to pierce it in every way you can, but if it is too closed, it will not open.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For if it is not properly opened and then treated, as we have said, until it is healed, it will not be effective.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The form of the sharp, spiky tissue from which the fistula is made, if it is very thick and on one side only and cuts; on the other side it is neither too deep nor too shallow, as you can see.
des emorroydes	Of hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Hemorrhoids exist in two ways: either they are inside the anus, resembling grains of resin, with small or large ones, causing bleeding, and located near or at the anus; but those that protrude have little moisture, sometimes a bit of citrus or salt water, and appear red. The treatment for hemorrhoids located within the anus is to instruct the patient to lie down in chambers until the anus opens and the roots become visible; then use pliers or your fingernail to grab them, cut them off at their base, and apply a hot powder that acts as a cauterizing agent. If the hemorrhoids cannot be removed this way, give the patient a cleansing enema with harsh water to wash out the anus so they can come out easily. When the patient sits down or if the roots are deep within the anus, treatment is simple; you prye them out with your fingernail or pliers and apply the cure as described above until the hemorrhoids heal and there's no risk of incision with a knife.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary for you to administer the stitch in this manner: take a twisted thread and wrap it around an needle, then draw the thread from above and pierce the needle from the other side, and pass both ends of the thread under the needle, and if it is too wide, tighten the forming thread, then tie the thread, and remove the needle, and do so for all others, leaving one for draining the excess blood; then place a moist cloth or ointment on the wound base, and cover it, and instruct the patient to rest; and then leave it until they heal, and when they fall, apply treatment and other remedies until they are healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	The phrase "dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement" translates to "the gently from the roots or
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there is a drying up of fluids in the intestines, due to nature's constraints, and when the illness is old and no medicine helps.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is necessary that you scrape the skin with a spatula or your fingernail, if it prevents moisture; then treat it as it should be until it is dry; and if it cannot dry, repeat the scraping stronger than before, until it heals and is not cut; then treat it until it is healed.
dou fremit	Dou fremit" translates to "it trem
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Ants are a small, fuzzy appearance before the body, and they move very quickly; when the wound freezes, it feels as if it is dead from trembling, spreading throughout the body, and affecting the hands more than any other part.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure is that you take a thin quill from an ostrich feather or a strong vulture feather, and place this quill on the trembling until it turns red throughout; then turn your hand over the entire quill until it heals completely, and remove the trembling from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see that it is a quill of iron or silver in this shape, be subtle and draw them from below and above.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	I do not feel any pain, so that I can hold the hand firm and press it. And if you see, cauterize the tremor, as it is mentioned in this chapter of cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of a douche
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Never should a enema be made with silver or gold, or melted lead or iron wire; nor should these small and large instruments be used according to those to whom they are prescribed.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those, therefore, that are prescribed for the treatment of infants who are weak and in pain, should be small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	He should seek a warm bath of little depth but wide expanse, binding his abdomen according to this manner.
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and if there is a desire for defecation, as you see, and the excretion is within, then he should have one aperture on one side and the other on the opposite side; and the abdomen should be filled with medicines from a bladder of an animal or parchment, and it should be punctured all around by small openings, with one space between each opening, and then thread through these apertures a strong thread twisted in the shape of X or any pattern, and tighten the abdomen like a bowstring; and when the medicine is inside, he should tie the instrument to a strong thread in front, then perform the enema; and this is the shape of a circle.
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let the medicine be neither too hot nor too cold, and apply a warm compress of oil or lard from a chicken, or something similar, then wrap it lightly; then the minister should massage with both hands together until it is completely relaxed, then remove the compress, and have the patient rest his legs against the wall, and let the medicine escape as much as possible; and if he sleeps soundly for one night, that will be greater aid.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you use the enema for a disease of bloating in the belly, and the medicine quickly escapes, it should be repeated until it is cured.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhoid is at the foundation or abscess, it should be treated with as subtle a cleansing as when a child is involved; and this is the form of the very subtle cleansing where the skin is tightened around it.
des plaies	wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already spoken of the treatment of wounds; now we will tell you about the treatments of hands and medicine, according to accomplishment.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to what they are made of, and according to the place where the wound is made, and from what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things by which wounds are made are by the use of stone, and sword and knife, or lance or spear or arrow, or similar objects; or they are made according to the laws of the body, such as a wound that breaks through the collarbone, or on the head, or the side, or the belly, or the liver, and similar members; and I will tell you the cure for each wound, and begin with simple head wounds, for the memory will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head and the bone is not broken, be careful if it is from a stone or similar objects, and the skin is nevertheless torn and the wound is great, and you doubt an abscess forming: do this as soon as possible to make the wound healthier, especially if there is little blood loss from the wound, and on the contrary, treat the affected part; and let the patient avoid wine and rich meat.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he does not want to heal, let his flesh be reduced, and do not make him drink wine, nor eat any meat; and apply a poultice of rose oil alone or of vin stipticum (astringent wine) to the wound; if there is a hot abscess, apply it to the fresh wound while all its blood is still present, and do not let the air, powder—which I will mention later—touch it, but rather use some ointment while it is still clean.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large, like a sword's width or similar, and the edges cannot be brought together, then bring them together with stitches, as I will describe for wounds of the belly, from the stitching.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed through bone, it bleeds profusely and lasts only for a short time if not treated; then treat the wound with medicine and replace the skin with hard wood, and instruct the patient to eat substantial foods, such as roasted meat, bread, cooked grains, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find putrefaction in flesh or leather that does not reach the bone, it consumes the putridity completely and oozes; then treat it, and if there is an artery in the wound or a vein, from which no blood stops, and medicines cannot arrest the flow, cut through the artery, and if you sever it, bind it with a thread; and if this does not help, cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the cure is light: and it is that you put this powder which sticks so that the fire moves it.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	The method for the powder is as follows: take one part of incense; two parts of dragon's blood; three parts of fresh charcoal, and mix the powder finely, applying it to the wound and tightening it until it spreads well and joins together with all its blood; then bind it tightly and leave it unbound, unless it swells; for the medicine is not removed as long as it remains healthy.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And never should charcoal be used alone, unless one has incense or dragon's blood, but the fire must have moved the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the fire has moved the wound, especially if there is no powder applied; but place some prepared ointments or a paste of oats made with water and honey, until it is soft; then apply other remedies until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if a bone fracture occurs with the wound and it is small, then extract it with delicate pincers; and I will tell you below about fractures of the skull.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the collar (or neck).
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound occurs on the neck and it is simple, with no distinction between this and that from the top, but if there is damage in the neck where the artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is an artery, then there is no other remedy than to let it heal, and do not put anything restrictive, as it hurts the artery and causes it to retract; do not apply any sharp objects to the wound, because the substance of the artery is cold, and its continuation is connected to the brain, which is the highest member. But apply medicine accordingly, such as washed chalk in sweet water, mixed with rose oil, and clean bandages also in sweet water, and other stones in the same way, and moist compresses.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is great, cutting it open with a knife and binding it, then heal it as long as it heals.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and infected, filled with pus, pierce them or cut them lower; if an artery is severed, and blood flows, if you deviate from it, and the proper law and cauterization methods, and if the pain in the throat is cut, or the heart, and its conduct is preserved so that the flesh does not adhere too much to the throat bone, and do not touch the throat but set it back according to its natural form; then apply the best healing treatment for as long as it heals; and if the wound has pressed into the bone, pierce them if necessary; and if there are pieces of bone that you cannot remove completely, leave them until the wound decays, becomes dry, and lightens its issue; and if the wound is fresh, sprinkle on the powder I have mentioned.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there are bones or a fistula in the wound, treat it as I have said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound from a lance or knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a wound from a lance or knife, and deep, then consider the direction of the flow of blood as only the patient can: then know that the wound is mortal; but if it is not deep, and still full of fresh blood, do not apply powder in the first hour, nor bind it to prevent further bleeding that could harm the patient and return to the body; instead, apply a soothing dressing and change it twice a day. And if you have no dressing, place old cotton in the wound to suck out the moisture, and have the patient sleep on the wound for three days, or four, or more; if there is no spasm, no shaking of the body, or any strange feeling, then know that the wound is healing.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Cure the wound with various remedies and others, as long as it is healthy; and if it cannot heal, then know that there is a fistula; so treat it as needed.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	If the wound is from a sword or knife cut, and it is shallow or deep, on the front, back, or side, treat it accordingly; if large, use stitches; if small, apply powder; and if it penetrates into the bone, with fragments, clean the wound thoroughly and treat the foreign bodies if necessary; and if they are not suitable, let the wound heal on its own, lightening the extraction; and for other wounds in other limbs, judge as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	disruption of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The disruption of the belly is great and medium and small; from a large wound, no time does the intestine, or the nerves of the intestines, protrude; and stitching is more difficult, and never worth less the small wound than the great, because one must handle the intestines with more care if they are not stitched together from top to bottom; for the intestines soon swell, causing pain, if they are not handled with care, and due to this, it is better to stitch the smaller wounds first, so that we can then properly handle the intestines as needed. And know that the rupture of the belly occurs in four ways: common stitches have a rupture in the stomach's stitching, and the stitches for other body wounds and other specific stitches are common to other wounds; nevertheless, they are more suitable with the stomach's stitching, and I will describe each one and explain them.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small and nothing of the intestine is affected, and it is a difficult thing to reset, then it is by one of two methods: either because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is swollen due to the injury.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, warm it in this manner: moisten a sponge or a thin cloth with hot water solely, or cook water with squinant (a type of herb), and cypress, and spice, and raise the intestine until the swelling is removed; and never use this wine to constrict, but let it be moved so as to relieve the swelling.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling depart, if the intestine is filled with water or other fluids and the hemorrhoids are cooked, for this lightens the entry into the rectum; and if it cannot enter, then make a slight cut in the wound with the instrument used to treat hemorrhoids; and the first cure is to move the feces, that we should not cut them unless there is great need; and this is the instrument to split: slice inside the hemorrhoid and push it out if it does not come out on its own, and see the shape.
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged and the intestine is pushed out, if you can return it to its natural shape in its proper place, do so if you have the ability, for it is beneficial.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is large and located below the stomach, you should have the patient lie on their back and raise their legs higher than their head; if it's in the lower abdomen, place the head and heels higher than the affected area, and ensure that the injured part of the belly is in one of the two sections, so your focus is on making the sore section higher than the other; thus, you should follow what I've said for both large and small wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	For small wounds, prepare what you will use; take in your hands a gentle and clean medicine that will cover the entire wound, and close the lips; this is the common method of stitching, using one or more needles according to the size of the wound, leaving two spaces at the head of the wound for the needle, and threading a strong thread on it; then pierce the two layers of skin with the two prongs of the scalpel, which are located under the skin, until you have pierced from that part, and join the two prongs of the scalpel together; then wrap the thread around the needle twice, and join the edges of the wound neatly, and continue in this way using as many needles as necessary until all the wound is closed; the needles should be medium between fine and thick, for fine needles capture all the flesh, while very thick ones cannot enter properly; they should therefore be medium; do not push the needles too far from the flesh or skin, otherwise they will tear the wound before stitching; then cut off the ends of the needles, place tent or cloth under them to prevent the patient from feeling discomfort while sleeping, and leave them until the wound is healed; this stitching method with needles is preferable for small wounds, because it only requires one or two stitches, and you join the two layers of skin and the two prongs together with a medium strong thread; when you have finished stitching in one place, return to the beginning, sewing like cloth; leave a space between each stitch about as thick as a finger; this method served a man who had a deep wound on his belly, caused by a knife, which was over a palm in size, and it was more than two palms away from the intestines, and was a large wound.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I brought the intestine back as it had been for twenty-four hours, and the wound healed completely within fifteen days, and it was cured, and it became healthy.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And they marveled that he did not die, and it was a miracle; I did not cure him with any treatment, for I was in a place where none could be found, neither any medicine; and I applied clean cotton to the wound twice a day, and washed it with honey water until it healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Now I will tell you the two proper ways of stitching: take the needle, and hold it at the edge of the wounded part from inside to outside; when it has pierced the tissue directly, tie the thread tightly at the point where the needle emerged, and pierce it again from the inside to the outside, and continue this back-and-forth movement until the stitching is complete. The technique should be similar to how a tanner stitches leather, leaving one end of the thread on one side and taking up the other.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second way of stitching, which Galen properly calls, is like any that joins the two parts together naturally, and applies one end to the other in this manner: take a needle or a pointed instrument near at hand, and pierce only through one side, leaving the two parts of the seam; then turn the needle, and pierce from the opposite part towards these parts, as far as they extend; and after that, pierce both parts from the opposite side inward to the other parts (of the seam); and it is in this manner that the stitching is done, and it is the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galen calls this procedure, and many testify to it—stitching the abdomen with two needles, each having thread attached to it, and one needle should be passed from one side, and the other from the opposite side, in the manner of those who stitch wounds; and know that when the rupture is within the abdomen, the stitching will be more difficult than for other abdominal injuries.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgment of the wound is like the judgment of other wounds: and it is that when you puncture the fresh wound until all its blood flows out, and the fire has moved it, if the interior is disturbed, and the tissue, and the pain; then apply a healing powder mixed with charcoal, and if the fire has moved it, apply any remedy at hand, as long as the wound is open; and bind the thread, and make sure the dressing, and the mirra; then treat the wound like other wounds until it is healed; and if you have no medicines, put a piece of old cotton, and move it twice a day until it heals.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you need no other medicine in addition to these arrangements for simple wounds; and if you doubt that the wound does not affect any principal member, it is necessary that you apply a light linen cloth soaked in hot seasonal oil or rose oil, and place it around the affected area, and under the armpits; and if it feels pain or putrefaction in boils, and this happens many times, they should be enema with black wine, especially if the putrefaction reaches the intestines. Puncture it inside, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small intestine.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The inner part that is called "young" cannot heal when it is weary, and this is due to the weakness of the veins, and the subtlety of all the body, and the nearness of its nature to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	If the pus jumps out of the wound, reset it just as the intestine is reset while it is fresh; and if it has become old and turned yellow or black, you should tie down the black part to prevent further blood let, since there are veins and arteries in it; then cut through what is between them, and place the two edges pendant from the outer side of the wound all the way out to facilitate the extraction when the pus comes out.
de la routure dou boueil	From the rupture of the bowels
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestines are torn and the wound is small, it cannot be restored in any man, as I have seen a nobleman's navel or stomach pierced by a lance; and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, it became infected and fistulous, and there issued evacuation and flatulence; I applied remedies as best I could, and did not cease to apply treatments until he was healed, and the scar healed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw it healed, I doubted that the patient would not suffer pain in his stomach; but he felt no pain, but improved in condition and appetite and drinking; and some experienced physicians said that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it must be treated in this manner: take a large plug, then bring together the edges of the wound, and when the plug opens its mouth, place it between the two lips so that it pulls away from his mouth; then cut off the head of the plug, and let it remain in such a way that he cannot untie it, then insert another plug in the same manner until the wound is completely closed; and then dress the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	If the bowel's chief is entangled in the intestine and causes no harm to the patient, it can be tied with a fine thread cut from an animal's intestine, in this way: take the chief of this intestinal thread, which is much stripped, and tie it to the chief of this thin linen thread twisted, then wind the thread onto the needle and sew up the intestine, and arrange it in the rupture; and this method of stitching is only applicable according to reason and hope. If the wound is large and wide, especially when it's in one of the major intestines, there is no health, only subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	or whether it is a fistula, wherever it may be.
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	You know that any wound or abscess, when it opens, is generally called a "fistula", especially if it has hair and is deeply infected.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	A fistula, according to the truth of its formation, is hard and white, without pain, just like the feathers of a bird; sometimes it opens clearly, other times it becomes thick; sometimes it oozes, and other times it remains thin; and I have already spoken about this in the division of wounds. Every wound that does not heal, and there is no pus, is only due to one of the nine causes: namely, either a small amount of blood or pus; or because of its bad nature; or because there is too much hardness inside, and on the lips, which do not allow any pus to form; or there is excessive bowing; or the muscles are rotten, and the material is of poor quality; or the medicine is not good for curing it; or because the corruption has the manner of a plague; or due to the proprieties in the region, digestion is delayed, health is slow, and recovery is hindered by nature; or there are veins or bones. I have already described all these causes, their signs, and the cures with medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	It is necessary that I make you know the treatment of a fistula which is performed by manual work.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	You know that fistulas can occur in all parts of the body; for there are fistulas that affect large veins, arteries, and nerves, or the small intestine, bladder, or any of the ribs, or the spine, or any joint of the hands or feet, and if it affects the dominant member and its associated parts.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all fistulas of this nature are difficult to heal, and there is no cure but labor and ignorance; if there is a fistula that does not come to the place I mentioned, and you have confidence in the cure and understand it, take a piece of iron or steel, if the fistula is straight; and if it is crooked, seek a subtle plug for it, because the pressure should conform to its curvature; and if the fistula has an opening through which you cannot properly insert plugs, clean it with a catheter from one of the openings, as moisture flows from one opening to another, cleaning it. Then cut it thoroughly in your power, knowing if there is bone or nerve, and if it is fully healed, and ask the patient about the pain he feels when pressing your hand, and the place where he feels it; and once you truly know its location, whether it is far from a joint, nerve, artery, or vein, or in any of the places I mentioned, cut it as I have said, and remove the corruption and foul matter inside; then heal it as much as possible, and apply moistened medicine plasters to it, pressing them close to the fistula until the medicine corrodes the excess that is left at the bottom; and then put fresh, healthy bandages over it while it heals; and if this does not work, cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, cut it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If a vein or nerve does not affect the main member as we have said, and if the bone is exposed and there is corruption and blackening, the king must be treated until the corruption is entirely removed, then cure the ensuing complications as long as it is healthy; and if it remains unhealthy and bowed as before, know that you are not yet free: expose it and keep it clean until you reach the bottom, and remove all the corruption, then restore it to its place; and if it becomes healthy in this way, it is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If this is not the case, know that the corruption is too deep for you to treat it; if there is no other cause but to let nature take its course; and if there is a small corrupted bone that you can extract with tweezers, using an appropriate instrument for it, and if there are many bones, break them one by one, leaving none intact; and if the moisture opposes you, and there is neither error nor fear, bind and moisten it, and cure and free the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them in an hour, put something corruptive on the wound and let it fester around the bones until they become lighter; and if it is a large bone, like that of the leg or thigh, scrape off the corruption as much as possible until all blackness is gone, then dress the wound; and if there is a great part of the corruption extending almost to the bone, cover it completely until the corruption is healed, and then treat it until it is secure. And I will tell you about a fistula that occurred in a man's leg, so that you can take an example from it and provide aid in your work.
