Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	He was a young man around 30 years old who had a pain in his leg due to something coming from inside the body, causing substances to reach the leg and resulting in a large abscess that could not be opened; but because of their foolishness, they pricked the abscess so much that it became infected with many substances, turning into a fistula, and creating numerous openings (pertus) from which pus flowed, causing bowing and moisture in the body. Many tried to cure him for two years without any knowledgeable person in the art of medicine; until I was called upon, and I examined his leg and the medications used to treat it, and what was corroded by the pertus on a large scale; and the young man's skin turned red, with a citrine-like color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I pitched a tent in one of these gaps, and then I searched all the gaps, and I found that some came against each other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I then quickly seized one of the gaps and cut as deep as I discovered a piece of bone, which was rotten and broken off, and the corruption reached right down to the bone; I understood what appeared to be the corrupt bone, and thought that there was no other corruption except for this one that I had removed; and I began to treat the wound with medicines for a long time, but they would not adhere; then I examined it again, and discovered the bone as before, and found the corruption continuing in the bone, so I treated it and then re-set it, and bent myself to secure it in place; but I could not do so until I had cut around one palm's width of the bone, and pulled it out completely, then I treated it with more medicines. It healed soundly and securely, without wanting to start the operation again except for the weakness of the patient who could not bear it, and for the fear of death that I had from him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For in the evacuation of blood, it often becomes entirely healed, and a hard callus forms in its place, of good disposition, causing no harm or opposite effect at all, neither to going nor coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if a bone is broken in any part of the body, it should be treated in this manner: take a thread, and pull the end of the bone that is open, and command no one to extend it upwards; and tie another thicker woolen thread upon the first, and fasten it to the flesh that is beyond the bone, pulling the flesh away from the broken part, so that you expose the flesh beneath where you see the injury, and do not allow the flesh to heal over the broken bone; and place charcoal or a table (or cloth) under the bone to cover the corrupted flesh; and it should be treated as much as one can see and feel the corruption, and in this way again.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if a bone is corrupt and will not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part, then expose all of it; then place hot coals from one side to the other over the corruption, as we have said; and if the corruption is in a joint, cut out the corrupted joint, and remove the bone from the other side; and if the corruption is in the connection between two joints, there is no other way to treat it except by cutting; and if the corruption is in the wrist of the hand or the ankle of the foot, this is very difficult, but you must inquire about the corruption how it opens, and purify it in every way that you can, as long as the vein or nerve do not oppose it; and know that there are many instruments for cutting and binding these bones, according to the position of the bone and its appearance, and its thickness and thinness, and its size and smallness, and its hardness; and for this reason, it is necessary to match each work with the appropriate instrument; and know that the work will show you the instrument that you need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the manners of the diseases; choose therefore the instrument that you need, as it is right.
dou feu	By fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The joint dislocates internally or externally; and when you have treated the inflammation with medicines but they are ineffective, it is necessary to immobilize that limb until the inflammation subsides, so that the patient escapes death or harm from the weakness of the limb, and the signs are that the limb turns black, as if it were burned by fire, and after the blackening, the inflammation spreads from joint to joint throughout the body; therefore act quickly in immobilizing it, and if it is due to the bite of certain venomous creatures, such as a sea scorpion, snake, or similar, immediately treat the dislocation at the top of the limb, and do not give it time to return.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it reaches the hand, strike the joint with the bone so that the corruption does not reach the arm; and if it reaches the arm, strike the cut to the shoulder; and if it passes the shoulder, it is death, and no cure can be found except according to its strength, and thus it acts in every corruption: if it comes at the first joint, strike after the other joint; and if it comes at the foot, strike throughout the foot; and if it ascends to the leg, strike at the knee joint; and if it comes above the knee, there is no other remedy but to leave the patient to die; and the manner of striking or binding the member is that you tie it from above and below, and stretch one assistant with the lower ligament, and another with the upper ligament, and you remove the flesh that is between the two ligaments with a wide spatula, until the bone is exposed; then strike or bind, and place on each side a piece of linen cloth, so that the linen does not touch the healthy part, and causes further injury and abscess to the patient.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And if the flow of blood occurs when you open it, carefully cauterize the wound and do not apply any constricting powders; then return to your medicine until it is complete, bind the affected member with a suitable ligature, and treat it until it is healed; and I will tell you that it happened to a man in great pain: he had a blackening that seemed like a burn from fire, and this corrosion first appeared on his right foot, until it discolored the entire foot. When he saw the corrosion, he covered his foot and was healed; but after a long time, the corrosion returned on his left hand, and he came to me, and I placed things against the foot after purification of the body, and the corrosion would not stop; and he asked me to cut off his hand, and I did not want to do so, as I had hope of causing the material to retract. And I also doubted that if I cut off his hand, he would not die, since the man's strength was weak; and he became completely desperate, returned to his land, covered his hand, and was healed; and I have never heard of such a case except for this, if it is necessary.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	No abscess should form in a fleshy part and remain there so long that it creates great swelling; then it bursts and pierces the flesh, remaining like a vase; and the skin over it is as delicate as fine cloth, not penetrating to the bone or nerve, and such a condition is called "sain" (healthy), not "fistule" (abscess). But if it penetrates all the way to the bone, it is called a fistule; and the skin should be cut away around it entirely, especially when it is delicate like fine cloth, and it will not heal due to its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if the skin ruptures and the corruption is not fully healed, and the flesh around it is hard like fine cloth, treat it with an enema as follows: Check if the swelling is large and if the bowel odour is foul; then prepare an Egyptian medicine by mixing equal parts of asafoetida and oil, heating it over fire until the medicine turns red and thick like honey. Then, take as much as needed and mix it with water and honey, and give this enema to the patient, leaving it for two hours before draining it slowly; repeat this process until the swelling is cured and the corruption is gone. If you do not have Egyptian medicine, prepare a mixture of ashes from vine shoots and water, then strain it and use the liquid for the enema; be sure that the swelling is completely cleansed. If the patient cannot tolerate either the Egyptian medicine or the ash water, give an enema with honey mixed with a little bit of powdered lithargirum (calomer), or with wine, as honey has purifying and cleansing properties while wine helps to expel impurities. After performing these steps, if you are confident that the swelling is cleansed, give an enema with a mixture that causes warmth in the bowels, using rose-scented oil and vinegar; or use any other medicine or ointment mentioned in the section on treatments with herbs. If the rupture in the bowel is very small and the catheter cannot enter, enlarge it slightly with a hot iron, and apply the Egyptian ointment (or basilicon) to make it larger; if the wound is too large for the catheter to pass through, cauterize it from above or below until you can insert the catheter.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	Because when the bowel is in perfect condition, it does not allow gas to form; and if you cannot cover the opening of the bowel as you see fit, arrange it in such a way that the bowel moves down to its lowest point, for when the bowel is perfect, it does not allow gas to form, and if you cannot cover the opening of the bowel as you see fit, arrange it so that the bowel moves gently downwards, leaving no part of the bowel behind; and take consolidating medicines to apply over the wound, and place them under a linen cloth that covers the entire wound; then press with force onto the aperture in the side of the bowel a bit wider than before, as treatment for the wound, and apply soothing medication on another cloth according to the size of the wound, and place it over the aperture in the bowel to ease the strain, and do not remove the large linen cloth outside until after many days; and whoever is over the aperture in the side of the bowel often removes it to release the pressure, and knows what comes from the bowel, whether it be poison or a little bit or enough, or digested or undigested; and be careful if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not, and when you see how your medicine has spread in such a way and observe the nature that appears over the aperture in the side of the bowel, then you know that healing has begun, and bring it closer to health; and then unbind it in the morning, or on the third day, and when you unbind the wound, change the cloth, and renew the treatment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast becomes bowed and indigest after many days, knowing that the breast will not open.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons fester after a long time, do not despair of health, for health is approaching.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	For there are some whose spirits grow weaker over time in their wounds, and others who do the opposite; and if the breast becomes bowed and indigest after many days, knowing that the breast will not open; and if the breast is slow to open, and is distant, then use moist medicines with a subtle action, such as those containing vitriol, which is the last medicine; take the diaphanous ointment and mix it with rose oil and equal parts of old wine in substance; then conserve it and use it; and do the same with honey thickened with cooked grain, when diaphanous ointments are not available; you may take mirra, aloe, and incense, crush them to a powder over honey that has been heated, then spread it on the breast; at no time should you apply allicin or celestial lily roots, which are similar to flour or cornmeal; use simples or compounds: grind them to a powder and mix with the honey I described, and apply; and if the cure is prolonged, and this treatment does not heal, know that corruption has taken hold, pressing on the bones, or the hard members, or the ligaments—just as we said before regarding fistula treatment.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	from the abscess of the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	A gangrene is an abscess that forms under a nail in the hand or foot, or occasionally elsewhere; and when it becomes old and one does not take care, it develops a pus-filled abscess, and swells and leaks until it destroys the root of the nail, and perhaps even the whole nail; and the corrosion extends to the bone, causing intense putrid pain, and the flesh around the finger becomes swollen and discolored.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the previous section, and the treatment is not effective, then you must remove all the dead tissue from under the nail, and then cauterize the wound afterward.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The cautery is very great help if the bone is healthy, and the nail is sound; and if the nail pierces the skin, and begins to point, and becomes blistered, then it is necessary that you place the edge under the nail that has pierced the skin, and press it upwards, and carefully extract the nail, and apply hot and corrosive medicines to remove all; then treat the wound with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if the corruption is in the bone, cut it off and pull it out, for as long as the bone is corrupt, it cannot heal; and if you see both bones corrupt, remove them as mentioned above, then treat it until it is healed; and if it is burnt and blistered, and causes great pain, it must be treated first; then carefully cut the nail with a sharp tool at an angle from above, and ensure that the cutting does not reach the skin beneath the nail, for the patient would feel too much pain; and if necessary, apply something to soothe it.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain pierces through the whole body.
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	He who is born without the hands in anyone's care is usually very fleshy, and perhaps has some bones, but never any nails, and none come out at the root of the joint, where birth should be in no way constrained.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	He who is born without any joints in his hands does not move, and he who is born with joints at the hand may not move; the size of the fleshy one is so small, in a similar way: cut him off at the root with a broad instrument.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	He who is born at the root of the joint is difficult to cure: if you keep him covered.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For he who is born or has an injury to the last, it is necessary that you first cover the wound properly up to the bone, then cover the bone with a suitable thread, and then heal it as long as it is healthy.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The injuries that come together belong to birth, or the adhesion of a wound, or the burn of fire, or similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	If it is necessary to close this wound, so that it must be repaired according to its natural form; then place between two moistened cloth or drapes, made of rose oil, so that they do not adhere; or between two pieces of fine felt, as long as the edges are sewn together, as appropriate.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If the dislocation occurs in any of its joints with the palm, then close this wound as appropriate.
des vils	des vils" is not a complete or
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	These veins are thickly wrapped, full of melancholic excesses, which come upon many members of the body; and they occur more in the legs of those who walk, work, and carry things, than others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It is necessary for you to administer purgative once and then the health of the colon.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The cure of iron is according to two manners: one is with the use of cups and drawing out the black blood; and the other manner is that you open the vein and drain it completely.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The incision is according to this manner: first, raise the afflicted leg with hot water very strongly until the thick blood becomes thin; then extract the lower leg from the thigh up to the knee joint; then cut the vein in one or two or three places with a broad blade, drain and squeeze out the black blood in your hand from one end to the other, as much as the sick person can endure; then bandage it and command that he be fed with food producing black stools; and repeat the evacuation and cleansing when the veins are full, causing harm to the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	They should raise the affected leg and if there are many hairs, then immerse it in a bath, and heat the leg with hot water until it turns red and the veins swell; and if you do not have a bath, heat it over a fire, and then compress the vein from the top of the thigh down to the ankle; then cut the skin at the point where the vein appears, and strip it from both sides until it is exposed; and it will appear red and black, and as if it were a white cord; then stretch it downward from the ankle until it is raised from the skin, and then compress it lightly at the second point; then cut again in another place, if necessary, and raise and compress it, and cut it at the third point, and pull and raise it until all the veins are completely gone, and then cover it; and if you cannot pull and raise it, insert a very sharp needle through the entire thread, and tie and pull it, and stretch it downward, and turn your hand back and forth until it comes out; be careful that it does not cut, for if it does, it cannot be pulled or raised, and this brings harm to the patient; and once all the veins have been pulled out, place a moist woolen cloth soaked in wine and rose oil on the wound and dress it until it heals.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if you see that it is contracted and twisted and wrapped together as one, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must break it crookedly, but do not cover it; treat it as we have mentioned above.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The way to do it is to bend the eye gently so that it does not cut into the vein; it should be of great curvature, because if it were thin, it would pierce the vein, but since it must be thick, as we have said, then this is its form.
de la voinne civile	from the natural vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is located in the legs, in hot parts where no herbs or trees grow, and on land where there is no moisture; and sometimes it appears elsewhere than in the legs, due to putrefaction that arises from below the skin, as it comes from within the body, winding and entwined between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein appear, it is characterized by a very great inflammation in the leg, then the color changes, and the vein begins to protrude strongly, just like a root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the vein opens, it is necessary to wrap a piece of cloth around it, from one and a half to two fingers thick, and leave the cloth on the leg; and at every appearance, if there is no opening, wrap the cloth around the leg and the new growth; and if it is too long, cut off a part and wrap the rest, not cutting it at the base, until it is completely removed; for if you cut it, it will return to the flesh and cause abscesses, putrefaction, or other illnesses. For this reason, it should be treated little by little, up to the root, and nothing should remain in the body; and this vein appears when it has grown five or six palms long, as I have seen myself, and when you cut it, it draws one or two fingers down, and pierces all the way to the bottom, so that everything comes out; and the material inside should be emptied, and medicines applied to the wound to prevent putrefaction for as long as necessary, then treat the abscess.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And never again touch this vein, especially when it opens at the ankle or foot joints, and causes a great deal of bleeding; treat it then as we have said above.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	worms that emerge between leather and flesh.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called "beef disease" in our land because it often affects cattle, and it is a small worm that emerges between leather and flesh, traveling throughout the body, causing pain from one limb to another until it ruptures through the skin where it originated, and moves with great force; and it is caused by putrefaction of certain humors, as do worms, snakes, and lice in the belly; and its evil nature is uncertain, for when it travels through the body, it ascends to the head, reaches the eyes, perhaps retreats, and destroys them. This happens frequently.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see it healing and draining, it cannot be done unless the blood flows: therefore, you must bind the limb above and below with a strong, tight bandage, then cut and drain it deeply, and if it bleeds profusely, cauterize it with fire until it stops; and the greatest harm it causes is when it makes the oil flow, as we have said; and if you see a blister forming near the wound, tighten it from below, then cut and drain it; and it is necessary for the patient to use purification of the body with solvent medicines to remove bad humors, and to wash with putrefying meats.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	The pain that comes from flatulence.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This illness is called "vakirir" in our land, and it is a pain that comes to no specific member, and then moves from one member to another; and I have seen what I have told you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a sick woman, and I examined her arm, and saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm; and after that, I noticed something moving up the shoulder, as quickly as anything, like a live silver thread when it cuts through the skin; the pain left the arm and moved to the shoulder, and then spread throughout the body, until it reached the other arm; then she told me that she felt it moving around inside her body.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marvelled greatly at how she moved each part of her body, for I had never seen this disease in such a way.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	Nevertheless, I had observed many cases where the pain moved from one part to another, but I did not understand how this happened, as I saw it in a woman; and I thought it was because she had dry skin, exposed veins, and that constraint caused this discomfort; and I did not see it according to this reason for those who are suffering, and have moist skin and covered veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see this disease heal and the patient feels this pain, if it opens up as we have said, press on it from above and below gently, then apply a poultice; and cauterize the wound; and if you do not have these remedies at hand, cure it with those that release the constraint of the wind, such as foul-smelling pills, serpentary pills, and others like them.
des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows vary, according to their appearance and the parts of the body from which they originate.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	Their diversity lies in that they have varying points—some large, some small, some serrated, and others smooth; and there are those with double edges, and those with elongated tips, and some have fragments; and they pierce different parts in two ways: either through a principal member, such as the head, body, liver, kidney, intestine, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When it comes out in any part of these limbs, and the sign of death, which I will tell you later, appears: it is necessary that you fight for the extraction of this arrow, because death comes after various preparations; and when this bad sign does not appear and the arrow is not completely extracted, pull it out and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of the brain when the arrow comes out and pierces the bone, and there is a sudden relief on the top of the head, then it turns black, dry, and shrivelled, and there is inflammation and redness in the eyes alone, and spasms and confusion in speech, and vomiting of bile; and perhaps the arrow comes out through the nose or ears; and sometimes it loses the power of speech and voice; and there are pus-filled white wounds that look like boils, and also excessive bleeding; if these signs appear to you, and you are a healer, then extract the arrow immediately.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The sign of an arrow when it breaks or withdraws, is that it is near the left breast, and feels as if it were embedded in hard matter, neither hollow nor empty; and sometimes the arrow itself becomes silent like the pulse, accompanied by black blood, coldness, and cold sweat, and fainting; therefore know without doubt that death approaches.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of an arrow that the proton never swells is that there is no foam or discharge from the wound, the throat swells, the patient's face changes color, he breathes heavily and stops moving.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow breaks in the covering of the pit, it leaves small pieces; it causes great pain and suffering, and the patient breathes heavily and his entire shoulder muscles spasm.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if an arrow pierces through the stomach, perhaps some digesting meat will come out from the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if an arrow pierces through the belly, and there is no healthy tissue from the intestine, there is little hope for recovery or in removing the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if an arrow pierces through the bladder, and urine comes out in spurts and leaks out, and the patient feels intense pain, know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limbs, as they make and feel hot and cold and pain in the throat, shoulder, aid (presumably a term for an affected area or symptom), back, hip, knee, and legs, and appear strangely, are safe according to various dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in a nerve or an artery and it is not poisonous, as I will tell you that happened to me, because you do otherwise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	An incident occurred in my home where an arrow struck the ear or the cheek: I attempted to remove it, and pulled from the other side under the ear fat, and it was completely healed without pain.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And also, by chance, an arrow struck in the fat under the skin and through the paper of the skin, and the arrow was lodged, only the tip towards the wood, and it was a large arrow with a turquoise bow, very light without any harm to the ears; the wound healed, and no ill accidents came.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And pull a dart from the throat of a Christian, which was an Arabic dart with ears: I cut the barbs, and removed it as far as I pulled, and healed the Christian.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And I pulled out a dart from a man's home, which had pierced his stomach, and thought he would die; but after thirty days, he showed no change in condition; so I cut the dart, wrapped it, and pulled it out, without any ill effect.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you see a man with a dart pierced through his back or chest, and the wound is deep; and the dart remains inside him, and he shows no change in his natural condition, nor does he experience any discomfort in his natural functions.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And see another man to whom an arrow has penetrated his face, and the wound was deeply embedded; and he endured great pain without relief; and many others like him.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And I pulled out an arrow from the body of a prince, the king, which had penetrated him in the middle of the night, and was slightly inclined to the right side; and the arrow was completely embedded. I was called to cure him after three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very deep.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I desired it as a subtle probe, and felt nothing; but he felt a sharp pain and discomfort beneath his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was the tip of the arrow. I placed a soothing poultice on the wound because the swelling had not subsided; and I saw the shaft of the arrow.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I left the poultice on for several days, and thereby healed the wound; thus the patient endured long pain until he felt the arrow inside his nose; and it came out.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I applied to the wound a corrosive medicine with good hands until it was open, and I probed it, and felt the tip of the arrow firmly in place; then I adjusted the opening of the wound with that same medicine, until the base of the arrow became visibly apparent; it healed well within four months, and then the wound flared up so much that I used pincers, pulling from both sides, but it wouldn't come out; then I did not cease to try subtle and ingenious instruments, until one day, as the shape of the treatment appeared at the end of this chapter, while I pulled on it, I turned the wound around.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And they say that the nose cartilage cannot be restored; so I straightened it, and the wound healed, and the patient was entirely cured.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Or this has told you the quality of extracting certain arrows, so that you place your care on what I do not say, for books cannot fully encompass everything; but wise masters compare well on small and significant things, and on what is present and defective, they seek a new work and new tools at the descent of strange things that occur in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows do not come from members unless they are fixed in one of two ways: either through the place where they enter, or from another part; and that which comes out by this side, where it enters, is an arrow entering into the flesh, and never comes out again.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not currently come out, let it grow until the wound is healed; and also, if it is stuck in the bone and cannot be pulled out, leave it for several days, and every day move it slightly; and then it will come out, and if it does not, pierce through the entire flesh with a sharp needle until the bones around it are widened, and then pull it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	If the arrow is stuck in the bone so deeply that it reaches one of the ventricles of the brain and none of the treatments mentioned above for the patient are effective: do not pull it out, but let it remain as long as it stays straight without moving for several days; for if the arrow comes close to this point, death follows.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is embedded only in the bone and does not come out satisfactorily, it keeps the patient without any bad outcome for several days, if the skill to pull it out is good.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is deeply embedded and cannot come out, then apply herbs around it, as I have told you; then heal the wound as long as it remains healthy.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is embedded deep in the body and one cannot see it, one should try with all efforts; and if you feel it, pull it with any suitable instrument; and if you cannot because of the tightness of the wound and the depth of the arrow, and there are no bones or nerves or veins nearby, then leave it until the wound becomes large; and pull the arrow as much as you can, and if it has roots by which it is embedded, break off the part that is deeply embedded, so that you can pull the rest of it. Be careful not to break the arrow itself while pulling it.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it at once, so that the limb around it is completely relaxed, then draw it, for the extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the signs of bloodletting work against you, then apply what we have said about treatment in that chapter; and be careful with the incision on the nerve and vein, and use any means you can to safely extract the arrow, either immediately or later, or firmly or gently; and place the patient according to the position it was in when the arrow entered, for this is the greatest help, and if you cannot, then do as the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	He knows the arrow that comes from another direction, where it opens anything within, and the flesh is swollen in that place as one sees or feels apparently: then cut above, as far as the pincers can grasp, and then pull it out: if it still projects outward.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	If it is stuck in the bone, turn your hand round, until it enters the bone, and widen the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot be pulled out, leave it for now and then try to pull it out again until it comes out; and if there is an arrowhead in the wound, let it remain, and then use a tool to press against it, so that the arrowhead enters the channel of the tool; and then push it out, and if the arrow has been removed, press the tool with the pointed end entering together to ease the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is embedded, it is necessary that you clean all the flesh around where the poison is, if you can, and then treat the wound as appropriate.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow comes out in the side or the abdomen or the bladder or the ribcage and it is close to a vein or nerve, and you can reach it, then take care to remove it; avoid touching the vein and nerve, then extract it, and clean the wound as required, and treat it until it heals.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The tool used to remove arrows resembles an eagle's claw, and here is its form:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many ways: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the arrowhead.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of it pointing towards the hair is like the feather of a bird, to push the arrowhead to the tip, as this is the shape:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape of pliers, to push and to grasp if this is the way:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the common veins of the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	From veins from which one draws blood, there are XXXI, of which the chief is XVI: these include the two battens located behind the ears, called "herbech"; and the two arteries appearing in the temples; and the two veins in each arm, called "aspires"; the vein across the forehead; the vein at the top of the head near the nose; the two glands located on the collarbone; the two veins above the lips, called "augeherich"; and the two veins beneath the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins commonly drawn from each arm are five: one is the cephalic vein, located on the left side and called by the common people "vein of the head"; the median is called "fast" and is composed of the cephalic and basilic veins; the basilic is located on the right side and called by the common people "vein of the belly", and it lies beneath the fascia, being the vein that appears most clearly when opening the armpit.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the saving vein is the one between the index and middle fingers, and if it rains; and in the leg, there are three veins: one below the tibia on the left side, and the second is the superficial vein at the ankle on the right side; and the third vein is called 'nere' which is also at the ankle on the other side; and in the other leg, there are three veins below these.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The health of veins that are located behind the ears aids in the healing of old cataracts and migraines; and the quality of the healer, as I have said, is to raise the patient's head and rub the affected area with a rough cloth; then tighten the bandage around the patient's neck until the two veins behind the ears appear in two parts extending from the head: hold them there with your hand, and where you feel the pulse beneath your hand, it signifies progress; then take the lancet and puncture just below the vein, up to the bone, then lift your hand along the entire vein upstream, cut and the skin and flesh, and carefully traverse the vein twice as deep as necessary, and let out the blood until you see; then drain and bind it until it heals; and I have already spoken of incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	He heals the two arteries that are in the temples, using an old and clean, accustomed eye socket, and at the source of hot tears alone; and the quality of the healing is as I say: he pulls the patient's neck until both veins open wide; and feels the pulse beneath his thumb, then signs with a cross on top of the vein above his index finger on his right side, and inserts the lancet beneath, lightens the vein at the top, and the clot, just as you did with the other veins, and makes the blood flow according to your need; then releases the patient, and places his thumb on the vein for an hour, then applies cotton; then forms the wound, and leaves it until it heals; we have already spoken of their mending and extraction, at the beginning of this book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The surgeon of the vein on the forehead is as valuable as the surgeon of the head, for treating old facial diseases, migraines, and redness; and his quality is such that the patient pulls their hair tightly by twisting, until the vein appears. Then take the tool called "disserter," which has this shape:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And place the tip on the vein, and press with your hand or another tool, allowing the blood to flow according to its quantity; then gently pull the hair of the patient away from the vein, tying it tightly until it heals and there is no sign of a wide wound.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, one should not let the flames be too intense; and if the wound is across, since the bone is close, and perhaps breaks the flames when they are thin.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The wound of the two veins that are in the arms is treated with special care, as well as the tongue, and the blush, and the eye in the socket, and facial diseases; and the quality of their wound is such that the patient tightens his collar without straining any ligament, as before. Then, the treatment, it should be neither too thin nor too thick with the flame, for there is no room for error.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flame is subtle, it may break; then apply pressure to the blood, as much as needed, and then bind it with cloth, tightly.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The health of the vein near the nose is valuable for headaches, sudden pain, and facial ailments, such as migraines and redness that appear on the face, especially when it is an old problem. The quality of the health is such that the patient squeezes their collar and pulls their nostril with their left hand, takes a subtle flame, and inserts it between the spaces of the two nostrils, because the vein does not open well enough, and the blood will begin to flow. Don't press too hard, and apply pressure with the sanct according to your need, then bind it for a night, as it is quickly restored; this is the shape of the flame.
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The holy oil of the two guindeges aids in the constriction of an ulcer, and at the onset of illness, and with many diseases, and impetigo, and corrosion, and herpes, and boils; and the quality of the oil is such that it draws the patient's skin away from each other, as we have said, and the master who is on top of the patient's head, and the patient sits in a certain place, then clean the vein with long-drawn blood slightly, then treat with blood tempered with warmth, or as needed; then repeat this in the other vein, then untie the ligature, and tighten the veins moderately so that the patient is not strangled, and leave it until morning, allowing the wound to heal.
de la sainie des leivres	from the cleansing of the veins
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The cleansing of the veins above the lips helps to heal in the mouth, and the corruption of gums, and cracks in the lips, and pain and swelling around it.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the qualities of the cleansing are to have the patient sit before you, holding his collar as I said; then turn the lip, and look at the veins, one on the right lip and the other on the left, which you recognize by their black color and the small black veins around them: so cut both, and if you do not know them and are in doubt, cut the thicker one from each side, and do the same with the two veins above and below, for it is the same method.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	from the cleansing of the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The cleansing of the tongue is most beneficial after the purification of the head, and it helps with conditions in the throat, and diseases of the eye, and ailments of the mouth; the quality of the cleansing is such that the patient should feel a pulling in their hands towards the sun, and they should gently move the tongue, looking for any dark veins beneath each side. Then cleanse one and both, but do not press too hard as there are arteries beneath.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins of the neck that are commonly cleansed are done in two ways: either by gently pressing all along their course with moistened fingers, or using a thin, sharp instrument (called an "anesil") as if cutting incisions, and they are wide or narrow according to the size and tightness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	It forms a bright red spot, very well known, and is broad as you see.
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it is necessary to open the large, flat veins that contain much blood and have a dark color; and this is the form of an olive flame.
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more precisely pointed, and is for healing the fine veins where there is subtle, yellow-colored blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The healing of the basilic vein, which is one of these veins, is very helpful for diseases that are beneath the throat, and the collarbone, and the chest, and the abdomen; and it is important for the healer to heal gently, and to wash the artery below.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if it touches the artery, and blood loss occurs, as it is necessary to stop it, as I have said; and the flame should not be gripping, but cutting like a blade.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the vein does not open clearly, it is necessary that you extract it and choose another one; or if you prefer a better outcome, you can cut the vein in the arm; it will open clearly, and cut it with a blade as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.
