And if you learn to recognize the vein, it is necessary that you extract the arm, touching the vein until you feel the pulse; then sign the place with a mark, and bind the arm, and cut the vein with a blade; and be careful not to hurt the artery when you see it swell, for it is the artery: flee from it.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see a discharge from the top as urine from a child, and the wound is red and tender, know that it is an artery: so hurry up, and place your finger for a long time, then remove your finger when the bleeding has stopped, which often happens; hold the arm still, and leave it thus, and do not move the patient; be afraid, and do not move until it is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the wound does not stop bleeding and it weakens you, and there is no medicine at hand, if the artery opens itself, due to its constriction; stop the bleeding of the wound.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And take a piece of chestnut bark, and cut it, and take one half and bind it tightly to the other side; if it feels comfortable, that's good; if not, cure it with powders that stop blood, for the stoppages are not too grievous in many arrangements due to the small size of the wound, and its strength from the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The treatment of the vein in the middle is very beneficial if it stops blood from the top and from below, because it is composed of basilic and cephalic veins, as we have said; and the healer should wash himself by the nerve that is below, and if he does not clean it thoroughly, and finds the nerve, it swells and the healing is hindered, and perhaps it cannot heal; and this nerve opens many times, and if it does not open in any person due to its subtlety, then it is necessary to use an antiseptic instrument; and be careful with the nerve in your power.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two bones, cut it from end to end.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The treatment for the head is to draw out the blood from the head, which helps the pain and promotes healing; it is beneficial to apply olive or myrtle flame, as this is the safest of all veins, as it does not contain any nerve or artery.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	However, it is advisable to seek the lightest joint, and do not be discouraged if it feels uncomfortable the first time, just try again; sometimes, the joints may swell up for some people when treated for the first time, but this should not cause concern.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the blood depends on your thinking.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you must know about bloodletting is that it should only be done to preserve health and prevent future illnesses; and it should be performed through one of the three veins: the cephalic, femoral, or basilic. One should bleed a patient at the beginning of meals during summer and autumn after eating, when the sign of fullness appears; and it should be done on the first day or third day, after two or three hours.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	Bloodletting to treat illnesses does not have a specific time frame; it should be done as needed, at any hour and in all seasons. It is not advisable to bleed children under 12 years old or pregnant women for four weeks after childbirth until the seventh week.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	One should not consider the old, who have passed sixty years, as fully healed.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when anyone wishes to be healed, in whatever way possible, it is advisable to cleanse the intestines with a light enema if they have retained much feces, so that the veins do not draw out excessive and harmful impurities from the primary limbs; nor should one consider as cured those who are overly salty from meats or too dry, as long as it persists. After dealing with colic, vomiting, abdominal distension, frequent sexual activity, hard work, watching, fasting, and similar things, then carefully balance the humors, if they have accumulated excessively through foods, drinks, and medications; then enter a bath, if nothing prevents you from doing so, to purify the blood, and heal the veins from below towards the third hour, as we have said. And guard yourself that day against work, worry, luxury, and similar things; be relaxed and joyful, and consider yourself healthier than before, and rub your arms twice or three times, then gently press the ligament above its middle, for if it is too tight, it cannot heal itself; then rub the area with your hands until the veins swell and you can feel them. Afterwards, moisten the healing bandage with a little old oil, then place your left hand's finger on the vein below the joint that needs to be healed, so that the vein does not break or cause harm.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	Because there are veins that flow as if they were strings in the body, and if they are of a type that is plagued by pus, when flame is applied, it retreats from the flame, and cannot open the vein, thus one becomes affected; and if the vein is opened, the wound is too narrow, therefore it is necessary for the physician to be knowledgeable about these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens the first time, that is good; but if not, it must be tried again from a slightly different angle, or more gently, if the veins are not inflated.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the veins are inflated and the patient is afraid, let it be for one or two days without compression; perhaps it will form an abscess later. Do not immerse him in water; then resume treatment as it pleases you; and if the perforation is small, cut gently and subtly, lest you doubt that it does not bleed as much as you see, because of the pressure from this same perforation to all the flames straightening; and work a little more gently, so that the vein is inflated; for this happens often when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the vein inflated, do not immediately restart the healing process, but apply a little oil to it, as it lightens the body of blood, and the oil moves in this vein the substance that the oil possesses; and thus administer the oil in each wound that you close veins, to stop the flow of blood; and the same method is effective and beneficial when applied to the shoulder; then the blood thins and spreads when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if a large abscess forms, which often happens, especially when the vein is only slightly opened, act quickly and apply a wet sponge with hot oil or silk for an hour; it is important that you do this after the blood has drained from the vein, and if it remains in place after several days without turning black or green, it will not cause harm; and if you see any signs, apply aloe or myrrh mixed with calament juice, or similar substances.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often there is an abscess and swelling in the holy basil: then place your hand upon it, and if you feel the joint soft under the pressure of your hand, this is a bad sign.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, be careful not to place anything on it that we have mentioned, for it may turn out to be without an artery; but make a dry plaster to harden the joint, then apply another treatment until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each case of pain according to the quantity of its strength and the colour of the pain.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the pain is sharp, let it be felt until it turns red; and if you see it swelling, let it continue to swell until it becomes smaller; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And for one who is strong and robust, and has the skill to extract blood, it is necessary to make a wider wound, with broader incisions; but for one who is weak, do the opposite, making a smaller, deeper wound, which should be healed more frequently and cautiously, cutting across, not into, to avoid damaging nerves, and this method of healing is safer from gangrene and nerve damage, and more effective than long or wide wounds.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And to him whose body is afflicted with sickness, it is necessary to give a moist mixture of pomegranate juice; if he is overheated, he should take three or four incisions and draw out the bad blood. And if he has a cold complexion, before the sickness, he should moisten his mouth with a syrup made from mused (or strained) grapes, or a syrup of aromatic honey with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and dates, and a well-scented syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he suffers from sickness, after the release of much blood, it is necessary that he inhale a mist of bread soup and fragrant syrup, and use other things as we have mentioned in the previous section or chapter on syncope for the evacuation of veins.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wishes to extend his arm and heal it later, as necessary, when it is weakened by much bloodletting, he should apply pressure little by little according to the amount of its ongoing strength.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever wishes to extend their arm after the initial bloodletting and has a strong constriction, should apply pressure for seven hours after the first bloodletting, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wishes to heal from another direction should heal on the second or third day.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For there is much blood inside the body, which has already been heated, and it brings fever; so you must draw out a great quantity of it and widen the wound until it ceases to bleed; then, after fulfilling all the conditions for healing, place your hand on his pulse when he is well, that death may not come in its place, and this happens often when healing is neglected; and you must not, when you see the arm being released and blood coming out again, and the wound is closed, press hard on it; nor if it is curved, should you stretch the arm painfully, for that would be harmful; but leave it until it ceases to bleed a second time; or if there is fire at the tip of the wound, as long as the blood frozen in the vein does not come out, put a little string soaked in water on it and press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is inflated, leave it alone and do not squeeze it until the abscess is calmed.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it becomes necessary to drain the blood again due to the abscess, either in the same place or in another vein or arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the arm is healthier in place of the vein in the head because it is composed differently.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the method of venipuncture is that the patient should hold his hand in hot water until the veins are red, then bind it lightly so that the vein appears well, but not too wide or too long; and the puncture should be near the joint of the hand, and if the blood does not come out, return the hand to hot water and let the blood flow in the water until you have enough; and if this is done, do not pull the hand back into hot water because it is put under more heat than necessary; and this vein is safer of all veins, as there are no arteries or nerves.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The healer of the salvation of the right hand is good for all diseases of the soul, and this is the manner: stretch out the hand, and immerse it in hot water until the vein is filled, if you can see it; and if the wound is across, and you cut it with everything completely, then nothing should disturb you; do not make too much effort, for the nerves are all bare of flesh, and then put the hand back into hot water, if the cold has frozen in the wound, and it cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the blood as best you can, then apply oil and silk to seal the wound tightly, and do so for each person.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The healthy person holds the mouse with their left hand for the benefit of the sore on the right side, and does it just as I told you for the left side.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The sage of the soul holds the body against all diseases that affect the skin, such as marital diseases, retention of flowers, diseases of the kidneys, and old legs and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the quality of his health is that the patient drinks warm water and rubs the vein until it disappears, binding it over the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and goes much towards the toes from above the foot; so, when healthy, one should use a wider bandage or one around the ankle, depending on what is more effective.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you apply this to a sore foot, take care to protect the toes that are exposed, and massage it gently as if you were rubbing; and the pain should lessen.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	If the pain cannot be relieved, immerse the foot in water and let the vein drain completely.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	If the treatment needs to be repeated, do so a little higher each time, because the nerve ends are salty; do not doubt the nerve, as we have said, and follow the same procedure for the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The vein's lion is at the foot's joint, and its pus causes pain in the hip when it is hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the quality of its pus is such that the patient feels pain in the bath, and strains from the foot, three or four times by twisting, because otherwise it does not open the vein; and if it opens, wash it in all ways as well as you can, and pass a hand through; and move it gently, for the lion is safe, and it is much relieved by many hands.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you do not clean it, no rain of pus will open on the back or side of the foot, towards the little toe, and be careful not to hurt; and make sure to clean the pus as well as you can, then loosen the bandage, put cotton on it, and tighten it; now it is healed.
des sainies de ventouse	from the suction cup treatments
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Suction cups are made of horns, or wire, or glass; and the suction is created in two ways: either by pricking and drawing blood, or without pricking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	This non-invasive suction method is performed in two ways: either using heat or without heat; and it involves 12 different locations on the body: on the top of the head, in the middle of the chest, on both sides of the chest, under the jaw, on both shoulders, on both legs, on both ankles, and on both wrists. This type of suction does not involve pricking any blood vessels, only small ones scattered throughout the skin, and it should not be applied to any part of the body that has recently been filled (e.g., with food or drink), as it could weaken the patient, just like with a vein treatment; nor should it be performed with excessive heat or cold, under any condition.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if by necessity of illness or habits, it is necessary to open the veins every hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in between and each time; for there are such who, when they need to open a vein, have a heavy head; and those who experience swelling and redness on their face, and on their head, and on their neck, and darkness as well; and such who experience a drop of blood in their mouth, and have a swollen tongue, and bleed; and there are those who dream, and see red blood and nausea and pain and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially in the middle of the month, we order the vein to be opened after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The physician of the body should aid in the treatment of the pain in the head... that comes from the joints, and it is not appropriate to do so after evacuating all the body; this ventilation is for the health of the brain, and it is not appropriate for those of cold complexion, or who have scrofula, for their condition brings them much harm; therefore the elderly should not use it, nor those with a cold head disease.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who have successfully treated it often become forgetful, and for this reason, a cup should be placed a little lower in doubt of oblivion.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The ventilation of the chest is beneficial for the health of the heart and basilic, and therefore it causes constriction of the pis (probably refers to the urethra or a specific organ) and opening of the channel of the penis, and in general, and repletion (possibly refers to an abdominal condition). It needs to be done carefully, as if it grips too tightly, it can cause harm to the stomach and body.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	Ventilation of the chest between the ribs brings relief from head pain, eye aches, migraines, strangulation, and pain in the roots of the teeth, and is beneficial for the health of the heart and basilic. It is important that you instruct the patient to gently place their hand on the area, avoiding pressure on the artery, to prevent complications such as bleeding.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	The inflammations of the jaw are beneficial for mouth diseases, and the corruption of gums, and similar ailments in the mouth; it is located in the health of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	Inflammations of the shoulders are beneficial for diseases that arise from heat and swelling.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	Inflammations of the veins are just as beneficial as three large veins in the arm, because they attract blood from these thick veins; and instruct the patient not to compress them too tightly, as the vein is bare of flesh, and knows how to drain and contract.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The suction cup that is on the rump is as valuable for drawing blood from the depths and for treating internal ailments, and it should be large and made of iron, so that it can extract effectively; and if it is too thin, it may break and cause great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The suction cups on the legs close tightly as they draw blood from throughout the body, and they are effective against chronic pains in the joints, back, bladder, and kidneys; they remove inflammation, and are located on the two hips, two ankles, but after long use, they weaken the body and cause numbness in various parts.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The method of applying a vacuum is as follows: you should first apply it when it is empty, and suck gently, then place it firmly and move it equally, without ceasing to do so until you see the skin red and swollen, and open the veins; afterwards, remove the cups, and take care with the condition of the skin, for there are those who have very thick and others who have very thin skin: only apply once, make wide incisions, and make them quite deep; suck gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the vein is thick, it is necessary to pierce twice: first to open the path of the thick blood vein.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the pain is very sharp, it is necessary to strike a third time; and when we want to draw out blood little by little, we suffice with only one strike.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we want a lot of blood, we must often strike; and if the pain is sharp, by striking well, we reach the end so that the veins are suddenly pierced; it is suitable for those who have thick and hard skin, and who have hairy pores, to apply oil to the suction cups: if it be violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or oil of pumpkin seeds; and if it be in winter, parsley oil, or lily oil, or chamomile oil, or another similar one.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is thick and cold, take amber oil, or balsam, or donkey oil, and similar things.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if anyone has a skin that is tight and has small pores, it is not necessary to put oil on it, but rather wash it after the application of rosewater, or cold water, or water from the morelle tree, or water from the cucumber, or porcelain water, or any similar water.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those with excessive moisture, let them rise from it using myrrh water, and sumac, and similar substances.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And those who have great superfluities should rise from old wine, or holy water, or a decoction of nettle or chamomile, or others like them; and one should not use a vacuum before the bath or after, but rather an hour or two after the bath; and one should not sleep after the vacuuming, and it is necessary for him to wash himself when he needs to be vacuumed and when he has been vacuumed.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And be careful that those who are being healed have no anger or too much heat; it is necessary for them to apply cold things like pomegranates, endives, lettuce, and similar things; and eat little, and drink chestnut wine, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And he who has a cold complexion, should drink syrup of honey and fragrant wine, which is neither too old nor too new, and eat small amounts, and small birds and pigeons; and on the day that he takes the wind, he must drink more than he eats; and it is appropriate to give any man at any time triacle or musk before or after ventilating, in order to strengthen the principal limbs; but it is not right for those who are hot to consume it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The poultices that are applied without causing harm are those placed on the liver, and the spleen, and podagra, and the belly and the bowels and the kidneys and the hips, for these members do not tolerate being harmed in any way; they are only applied to draw blood from one member to another, as we place poultices on the breasts when a child is born; to remove the viscosity that is in the member, as we apply poultices to the belly and bowels to reduce a swollen member; and it removes pain when there is congestion or a stone, for it may by its attractive virtue draw away the congestion or dislodge the stone from its place; and thus it works when applied to the liver and spleen when there is retained wind, and these poultices are prepared empty to suck up only, and never hot, nor mixed with cold water, as in cases where there are tears of pain, and in such a way one fills the poultice with hot water or water in which suitable herbs have been cooked.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the cup (ventouse) administered by fire is this:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	It should have a width of two and a half palm lengths, and on one side, near the center, it should have a small hole, as large as to fit an needle, and be made of metal, smooth so as not to hurt the patient when placed on the body; and in its middle, there should be a crossbar of metal, either iron or steel, to hold a cloth grip, and their sizes vary according to the illness and age of those who use them; for the cup size for children is different from that for adults, and for thin people it's smaller than for fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And one should thus place this suction cup over the member: take the wax or linen cloth and put it through the hole in the suction cup, so that the clarity is at the bottom of the cup to not burn the patient; then place it over the member, and your fingers should be on the opening we have mentioned, so that when you look, the vapour goes out, and remove the suction cup; and take up the linen cloth as before, and repeat often if needed.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the case of the suction cup used to treat pleurisy, or any acute condition, it has no hole or opening, and is only effective when it is completely full of water, and is placed over the member only then; its shape is as follows:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Without wounds that cannot be treated with poultices due to their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar ones; and in the case of wounds devoid of flesh, like those of a dog or a cat, or others similar; and regarding the condition of the patient, if you find poultices on clean, fresh wounds without putrefaction, take them off; place them in fresh water until they become moist, and then treat with vein and poultice, rubbing the member until it turns red, and apply the poultices again; and when they start to hurt and swell, if it is a wound that can be treated with a poultice, apply one, as this helps greatly.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If the limb does not rise easily from the wound, first soak it well in water and then wring it; and if the wounds are still infected after removing the poultices, moisten a linen cloth in cold water and place it on top, until the swelling subsides; and if the swellings multiply, put on vitriol or gall, or similar substances, until they subside; or you can use the half of peeled beans, leaving them on the wound until they harden, which will also help. If you need more, take other poultices.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the veins do not want to be taken, so rub the fresh blood vein with a needle until the vein opens, and then place them back, and soon as they feel the blood, they will contract; and when you see that they are squeezing, sprinkle some alum and fine silk powder or ash on it, and they will stop.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	This begins the book on fractures.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, for the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know, dear son, that the wise men of this treatise, who have dedicated themselves to it, have discovered things from this chapter that have never been seen in any ancient book, nor read in letters; and for this reason the knowledge has become strange in our land, because I have never found anything good about it, and know nothing of it, except through the study of ancient books, where I have dedicated myself so much that I have treated the science, and by experience, and through the habit of my life; and I have described to you in this chapter what is contained, and abridged it at the end, and clearly shown the forms of the instruments used, as I have done in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore appropriate that we begin this book with a prologue that explains the essence of its teachings and the chapters where the wise apply their understanding, focusing on truth, so that those who study it gain knowledge and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when fracture, dislocation, or torsion comes to any part, it is necessary that you hasten to heal the patient on both sides, if nothing else helps, such as weakness of the body, illness, or old age; or if the temperature is very close, or too cold. Avoid cold things like cold baths, and food from goose and hazelnut, and do not drink wine, nor consume any greasy foods, and do not fill yourself too much with meats that fill the veins, until you have no doubt of an abscess becoming hot, or of material spreading in the member; then the patient returns to his former state as if he had never suffered.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary that the patient be fed foods that do not cause excessive gas or thickness, such as cooked wheat in water, and laughter, and beans, and pressure, and goat's stomach, and offal, and oysters, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For part of the healing process, movement reoccurs and more often the fracture occurs again.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that old and brittle bones cannot heal or fuse together properly according to their nature due to the stiffness of the members, nor can those that are too tender, such as the bones of young children; however, don't worry, hold onto the broken bone with strong grips that connect the member together, as much as it did before, and don't touch its entire length, and for this reason, it is necessary to nourish with substantial foods, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures vary in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	Because the fracture from the top is different from the fracture from the bottom, of the leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all manner of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a fracture that goes to the bone, and another when sharpening, just like the edge of a quill for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a fracture with a wound, and a fracture with a very small split.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And each manner has its own mechanism and proper tool for restoration, according to the memory of the place; and the fracture of the bone is known because the limb is twisted, and it opens well under pressure, and sounds when pressed by the hand; and when there is no twist or crack or slight fracture, but only a curve or split or minor fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If you do not intend to move it with your hand, but instead apply remedies that will follow, and then gently hold it now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that the fracture which goes up in an arc, and are the two disjointed parts, they must now be set evenly, so that abscesses do not appear; and if hot abscesses come, it should not stay for any length of time until the abscess is calmed; then set it evenly with gentle and wise pressure, and know that the restoration of this is lighter than the restorations of where there are broken pieces; then hold it as it should be after this.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if a bone is broken into pieces, and it is dislocated from two parts, whether it is the hand or foot, or some small member, or two tendons, or a tendon and your hand, then place the member according to its natural position; so that when the parts of the broken member are brought together, rearrange all the additions in their proper places as much as you can, and be careful not to cause the patient further injury or pain with your work, and adjust both sides of the bone according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And if you feel that the hand is not well positioned, then carefully adjust it, and do not tighten it too much or press down as those who cause abscesses and contractions in the member with their work have done many times before.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limb is completely numb, be very careful not to move it, neither awake nor asleep, nor when turning, or in any other way; and ensure that the limb is securely held so that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when it feels no pain, it is only completely numb, and you must put it in a position where it feels no pain; and be careful that it is placed correctly, so that no twist comes as it heals; and the quality of the damaged limb will depend on what I have told you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	You should know that the damaged limb can be of different sizes, both small and large, and of various shapes.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	Because it has small members, as arms and legs and similar ones: you need to wrap them in soft and thin linen; and those that are larger, like the thigh or leg: you need to wrap them in a wide and firm ligature, for wide ligatures embrace the entire large member and tighten it equally from all sides so there is no movement; then tie softer bands loosely around it, three turns or four depending on the member, and gently tighten your hand over the ligature, then go above the break and tighten less, allowing the break to slightly pull away; gradually soften the ligature little by little, pressing hard enough into the healthy part until you feel satisfaction, then take another ligature and wrap it around the broken place; return to the other side of the break and tighten it moderately, neither too tight nor too loose, as we have said in the first chapter above; then insert between the compressed bands soft linen or cloth, ensuring they are even, then tie everything above with a bandage, and afterwards place your well-made splints on top, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is an inflammation or abscess, apply a soothing heat to it, which reduces the swelling, and leave it thus for several days; then strain your eyes, and make them half the width of a large needle, sharp, or of wood used for making knives, or of palm leaves, according to this figure.
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	But it is necessary that the thread placed on the break be slightly thicker and wider than the others; and also as long as required for the member, whether small or large; then tighten the threads as you did in the first layer, and tie a thin thread over it, as in the first layer on the break; tighter afterwards, less tight; and the thread should be of medium thickness, neither too thick nor too thin, and made of soft flax; because if the thread is thick, like those who make their bindings from twisted flaxen strings, this is a great error, for the binding cannot be even if it is too fine, and it does not suit that there be less space between each thread.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is annoyed by the joints of the stars after dislocating them into their sockets, he should place soft cloth or other bandage over them so that they do not hurt.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is accompanied by a fracture and the veins are broken, I will describe the treatment below.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not appropriate to dislocate all the stars of the broken members on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the members are large, it is not appropriate to put stars too soon, but after 5 or 7 days, or more according to your judgment of the hot swelling coming; and here is the ancient method of pastes for restoring fractures, dislocations, and torsions: take flour that clings to the walls of the mill, mix it with plenty of egg, and make this paste, neither too clear nor too thick, and use it; this is the common way of the paste that restores fractures in many positions, especially with women and small children, because it is neither too hard nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another way to make a plaster that restores fractures and dislocations and twists: take equal parts of bear's fat, lard, ointment, henna, gum arabic, myrrh, aloe, ales (a type of spice), and powder them; mix with egg albumen. If the patient's constitution is hot, use this plaster, as it is a good composition and restores broken bones effectively, benefiting many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another plaster for twists: take myrrh and calamine, in parts X; mirre (myrrh) and aloe, in parts 9; akebia (a plant) in parts 6; Armenian bole (a mineral pigment), in parts X; grind well and mix with water or egg albumen, then apply.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another way to splint joints and straighten bones out of their place, easing the pain that comes with it, and using bandages on the bone, and splints: take a new cloth, moisten it in hot water and oil, and wrap it around the joint.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Cyst splints do not restore, but they are good for easing hot abscesses and properly removing pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another way to splint broken bones: take dry fig leaves and terrestrial pavon leaves, grind them together, and make a paste.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another method of plastering to restore the broken bone and thus lessen the pain of the wound.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take the root of chamomile, fennel flower, violets, and chickpea flour, each in equal parts; grind them and mix with wine, applying this to the affected member, which should be heated beforehand. Alternatively, mix it with fresh coriander water or water alone and apply it as needed.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another stronger method of plastering when a hard abscess comes to the restoration of the member.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take roots of alder, and flaxseed, and balm, and melilot, and fennel, and violet flowers, and chamomile, from each in equal parts; grind them fine, and prepare a paste with strong salt water, or fresh water, or wine, according to the warmth of the affected part, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates writes in his book that to restore a dislocated member, one should not use anything but a paste made of wax and oil, and nothing else; it should be neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems that Galen states that to restore a dislocated member, one should apply things that are dry but slightly warm, such as myrrh and aloe and incense and similar substances, as we have mentioned.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another method of plastering that is useful for injuries and pain: take moss and sheep's wool, or feathers from an eye, or fur, and cut them equally, and crush them, and make a paste from them and bind it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then, a little later, release it gently and take care that the patient does not feel any pain, nor has the bone moved from its place; if, however, by releasing it, there is pain, or itching, or swelling, then hurry up and remove the plaster immediately, and take a light cloth, and a moist sponge from the sea, and dip it in water, and gently lift the skin until the itching stops and the pain is soothed. Then let the member rest for an hour, and apply a dry cloth, moistened with water or rose oil, and bind it tightly, as you are certain of the hot abscess; and thus relieve the swelling in the affected limb, and the pain will disappear. Then continue the process gently, with less plaster, and do not tighten it so much as before; apply it delicately until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is red, swollen, painful, and filled with pus, and you need to apply a poultice and bind it, then repeat this just as you did at first.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	If the limb shows no improvement after what we have said for three, four, five, or seven days—and never lets it heal for twenty days, as is often seen until the fracture is healed and alignment towards recovery begins—then tighten the bandage more than before and fatten the flesh, as I mentioned earlier. If you notice that drying out the limb is unnecessary, then immediately apply warm water each time you loosen the bandage, every third day, and leave it slightly moist. By this means, slowly heal the limb, and avoid the harmful practices of foolish healers who cause further damage by applying treatments incorrectly. It is bad, and such errors are very dangerous; I see nothing else but to give up and do it right.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Of various methods of fracture
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	There are many methods of fractures, with various shapes and distinct causes; for there are fractures caused by the impact of a sword, where the bone breaks completely through to the other side, as if cut with a hatchet or axe; and because of this, this type of fracture is called "haichure.
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	Or, the sword may cut through the bone without actually piercing it, and this is called a "complete" fracture; and this type of wound can range from severe to minor.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is a shock or compression, or a cut from stone, or from falling on stone, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a recent fracture, which extends just to the skin covering the bone, or it is on the bone itself, and this wound is either large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if the wound that is healed in the bone is as subtle as a hair, and the fracture is small, it is called a capillary fracture; and if the wound is caused by hitting with stone, or falling from a height, or similar, and the bone fragment enters deeply, and the edges of the bone are frayed like the edges of a potter's wheel when they shape pots, then between the bone and the stone.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this occurs more often in those with moist bones in their head, such as a child's head; and it happens in all these ways of fracture that small pieces are dislocated, just as if they were broken; and I will speak of it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all the ways of fractures by pulling on them, and inquiry at their joints, and by corrupt flesh above them.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The appearance of the fracture is recognized because when we have discovered the bone and rubbed it thoroughly, the black fracture opens up.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of fractures, be cautious regarding complications with the patient, and if you notice any ill omens, such as vomiting, loss of consciousness, extension or stiffness, pale skin, ague fever, or other similar symptoms appearing in various combinations, then it cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see any alarming complications and hope for a recovery, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the fracture presents itself to you, and it is in winter, then it is necessary to remove the bone before the fourteenth day after the injury.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if this happens, if you hastily remove the bone on the seventh day, so that the wound under the bone is corrupted, then the complications arise as we have said.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the fracture of the bone reaches the tissue that covers the brain, it is necessary to split the fractured part in this way: you must pierce the head of the patient with pain, and expose the bone in all ways possible, and tenderly uncover the wound when the pus has come to light, or an abscess at its base, if there is help for it, and fill the cavity with moist gauze soaked in rose oil; then allow the wound to rest until the abscess has subsided, and be assured of the absence of further pus. Then begin to remove the bone, and this must be done according to two methods: one method is to make a narrow cut directly in front, and this is its form...
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then I choose another treatment even greater than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second method is that you have many different shapes, some with pointed ends and others wide, all made of indestructible iron; and when in use, do not damage the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and dense, it is necessary that you make an incision around it, so that you can insert the correct size of the tool, not allowing the tip to go beyond the soft part of the bone, and there should be a margin or a circle on top of the point to prevent it from piercing through; and you need many different ones, so that each fits perfectly with the thickness of the bone, making them suitable for all bones; and this is the form of the three types of tools:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality to percé the broken bone is that you apply pressure on it, and return to your task as long as you know the bone is pierced; then place the pressure elsewhere a little later, and do this all around, then cut with incisions the space between the gaps of the bone, and do so as delicately as possible, gently, while still holding the bone in your hand or with any tool you have such as pliers or pincers, and be careful not to touch the brain nor the soft tissues.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And once you have pierced and treated the bone, it is necessary that you observe the tension that remains from the bone to all other similar tools like an incisore, but it should be more delicate and subtle than the others; and if it holds onto any small bones or scales, gently remove them with the appropriate instrument; then dress the wound with bandages and ointments as we have said.
