Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And another way of working is that which Galen says, which is safer; it is very strong, and this is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is first necessary that you uncover a part of the bone, either where it is broken open or clearly visible, so when you have uncovered this part, you will place the edge of this curved scalpel beneath it, whose shape is as follows:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut from one side, but the sharp part should be on the opposite side to the bone; then gently tap with a small hammer so that you slightly lift the bone around it, and be very careful of the tissue beneath; if it is separated from the bone, gently lift it, for it can be easily damaged without great harm or pain.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the fracture of the bone does not reach the skin, and the bone is only cut from above, and there are small fragments, then it is necessary to clean that roughness again, and remove the scales with a delicate rasp, of which you must have various quantities, in order to make each one as suitable as possible, according to the severity and shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you encounter great rasps, and then more subtle ones, continue doing this until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other haircuts and subtle fractures, it is necessary to adjust according to their location; and this is something that cannot be fully answered to anyone who has devoted themselves to this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if it pleases him to uncover, you must then press a linen cloth, according to the size of the wound, and moisten it with rose oil, and place it over the wound; then take another cloth, doubled in two or three, and moisten it in wine and rose oil, and place it on top of the first cloth; do this as lightly as possible so as not to harm the wound, and administer another bandage above, without straining it too tightly until it only touches the wound; leave it thus for a day or two, until the abscess is calmed, then remove it, and apply medicines such as lion's root, flour of grain, incense powder, and similar things; make a powder from these, and place it over the wound, and administer foreign remedies without cauterization. And ensure that the wound remains clean, and do not leave any dressing or bowing on it, because when bowing accumulates on the soft flesh, it corrodes and hurts the patient, and brings great harm to him, for when a sharp object is placed over the skin, it causes damage.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take care then, if no bad accident comes to the patient, as we have said, it is doubtful without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if darkness comes not from the medicine that has been put upon it, but to show its virtue, you should press a part of honey and three parts of rose oil mixed with a cloth on the sick; then cure it in a manner befitting the cure, until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	You should know that the two parts of the bone above are never broken, either entirely or only one by one, for they are two bones; and the inner part is cartilage, which does not break, but only bends or twists, and then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, it is necessary that you insert your small finger or index finger through the gap, and place the same fracture in your index finger, and press gently, until the joint returns to its natural position; do this carefully, and be sure that the patient feels no pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the fracture is in the upper part of the joint and the fingers cannot be moved to their normal position, it is necessary that you place a thin stick at the top of the joint.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the fracture is in both parts, do as I have said before, and try to restore it on the first day if you can; if not, after the seventh or fifth day, when the swelling has subsided, then place thin linen strips over the joint, if the fracture is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or turn to another place, if it is broken, and make the splints so thick that they fill the gaps in the neck.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And they say that no restoration is required; the splints must be moistened with butter and changed each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	I do not think this is good, but it is necessary that they be moistened with a mixture of egg and flour powder; then leave the splints, as long as the bones are hard and the cartilage stiff.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And never burn the skin with hot pens or feathers on different parts, and if it stings the wound, holds the break, and blows air into it; or do as you see fit.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if abscesses form at the incision site while you are treating them, apply a poultice or moist cotton in rose oil or in a small vial of dung.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses do not form, apply a paste from spelt flour and incense powder, candied with egg albumen, then place light bandages on top and do not tie the skin; and if the rupture in the skin is small and broken into tiny pieces, extract them with suitable instruments, then clean the wound with hot things like char and cautery, and apply suitable bandages and poultices until it heals.
de la routure de la mandibule	from the dislocation of the mandible
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the mandible is dislocated and there is no external wound, and the fracture is only slightly displaced, not broken into two parts, but only crooked inside, then it can be corrected gently.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	If the fracture is in the right side, you should insert your index finger into the mouth of the patient; and if the fracture is on the left mandible, insert your index finger from your right hand, gently push the fracture inside, and with the other hand pull it outward to make it even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the jaw is severe in two places, you must then administer extension to the second part, as long as it is even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if the movement of the teeth occurs, or rupture, by applying tension with a golden or silver thread or silk, then place cerate on the broken jaw and cover it with a double cloth; put the cloth on a large, equally shaped piece of leather or hide according to the size of the mandible, and secure it with ties as you can, and command the patient to rest and eat light meats.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	And if you notice that the shape changes, after the third day, remove the plaster and then put it back again as it was changed; apply plaster made of finely ground powder or sesame flour after removing the cerate; add a thin layer of the plaster, and if the plaster hardens, and the patient's condition does not change, leave it until it heals; it often heals in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if an abscess appears, it is necessary to do as we have often said.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is both a fracture and a wound together, the treatment should not remove any part of the bone that is broken; it is necessary to use suitable instruments for this purpose.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, open it with fire according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And once you have removed all these pieces and nothing remains, if the wound is wide, close it with suitable bandages to prevent infection, until it heals.
de la forcele	from the strength
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The force can break in several ways, directed towards the shoulder, and these breaks occur in three manners: it may be broken and dislocated into two parts, with fragments, and is easiest to restore; or there is a break with an accompanying wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And if the task is when the break occurs without a wound, you will need two assistants: one should hold the limb with the broken strength; the other should stretch the collar towards the affected area; then, equalize the fracture in your hands, so that the shape is as it should be, and there is no visible or palpable deformity.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to further extend it, place a round spear of cloth or wool beneath the shoulder of the patient, as thick as needed; stretch and ease the tension, hold the spear in your hand, and make sure the break is even, as required.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the muscle away from the deep side, because it is attached completely, then the patient should lie on their side with the dislocated shoulder below, and have a helper press the shoulder upwards, until the bone of the muscle is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	Then grab the break with your fingers and if you feel any debris, it is alright to cut; gently pull the pieces apart, and if the bone cannot join together despite your best efforts, place a tool beneath the muscle on one of the incisions you made earlier to achieve the desired effect.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and it looks like a spoon, and is not broken, and is as wide as necessary, according to the size of the bone and the power of the work; and it has two parts, as you see, one wide, and the other narrow, just as the break in the wound that you made when you treated the bones; and when you are certain of a hot abscess, if you cut the wound deeply, or if the break is small, then you doubt a hot abscess, if you cover the wound with bandages and tents, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if abscesses appear, then moisten the bandages with rose oil and wool and wine, and place them on top.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The binding of the bone, when it has wounds or cuts, is to place on the bone a plaster of fine-milled powdery and egg white, and lay light stoppers above, and insert a spike under the armpit if necessary; then take a very wide bandage, one palm length wide, and place the double cloth over the stoppers and plaster; next, take a thin steel rod three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around the bandage, so that the top of the bandage is hanging; place the steel on the fracture, and turn the bandage back over the collarbone, and under the healthy and sick shoulders; rearrange each part, and as often as you see that the plaster holds well on the broken bone, and you clearly see that the steel does not move upon it, reward it each day, and when the bandages loosen, tighten them again; place the patient on his back, and while he sleeps, insert a small pillow under the armpit to raise the dislocated limb; if this lightens the fracture by aligning the shoulder, or you tie the arm to the neck, and no ill accidents happen for twenty days, then reapply the plaster if needed, tighten it, and leave it thus until it is healed; it is healed in no more than 28 days, and less so for no man.
de la brisure de l’espaule	from the dislocation of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	If the shoulder is dislocated, it does not return to its place, and can only be held in place by touch; if you put it back according to the shape of the dislocation and restore it to its natural form in every way possible, then sprinkle a little fine powder on it with plenty of egg yolk and cover it lightly, and then wrap it in a double cloth; then place a wide and thin plate over it, slightly larger than the shoulder, and fasten it firmly so that the plate does not move from its place, and check it every day. Whenever it becomes looser, tighten it again, and if the plate is out of place, put it back gently, and let the patient lie on his side. The shoulder can be restored in 10 or 25 days, and when this time is up, release it carefully, for it is not a bone that returns easily to its place.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone sticks out and does not come out easily, cut it with a knife and do what we have said to soothe the hot abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	from the fracture of the worst abscess
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The fracture never occurs in the middle, but seldom; but it often breaks at the extreme.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is fractured in the middle, it declines and sticks out, causing the patient great pain and injury, without any relief, and sometimes bleeds, opening up the wound in the broken bone, and feels much better.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that the patient lies on their back, and puts a cushion between their shoulders, then presses the shoulders, and brings together the ribs with both hands, and subtly adjusts them in all ways as appropriate, so that the shape of the bone is correct; then apply poultices and compresses over the gentle salt or other light bandage, and wrap it in a cloth, binding it to the broken bone so that it does not move; and tighten the bandage regularly on the back, adjusting it closely, and changing the dressing every hour, and if it becomes soft, tighten it; and if it needs to be loosened due to erosion or itching that occurs at the site, or pain or abscess, act quickly, loosen it, remove the poultice, and address the cause of the problem. Then reapply the poultice and tighten it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	from the fracture of ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	You know that the fracture of ribs only occurs in the upper back and at the top, and they do not bend unless they are broken; and this causes great pain to anyone touching them.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the restoration is such that you set the fracture back in place as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	Then apply the plaster, and bind it with a stick, if necessary.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the fracture of the ribs is declining inward, it causes the patient to feel very great pain, as if from crying, because the bone pierces the flesh; and also weakness in the limbs, and at times, he vomits much blood, which is a sign of grave illness, and the old ones have put much effort into it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And for those who say it is appropriate to administer foods that cause bloating in the stomach to drive out the fracture from within.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not make any effort if hot abscesses do not come, unless they have already appeared.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has come, if the healthy [one].
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And they say none of you should place suction cups over the joint for it forms a vacuum, and this seems reasonable; nevertheless, there is doubt that the suction cup may draw away the superfluities from the joint due to the weakness of the constitution.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they say none of you should cover the joint with moist wool soaked in hot oil, and place tents between the ribs to even out the space around it, then apply treatment for pleurisy, flesh, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot endure through the bone where the wound is, then doubt arises in the patient; it is necessary to cut into the broken rib cage, and place an instrument to stop the bleeding; and then one must cut the bone, pull gently, and sew together the two edges of the wound if it is large, and treat it with poultices until it heals.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses appear, place moistened oil-soaked rags on them and apply heat; treat the affected area while the heat is on the abscess, and lay the patient comfortably on their side where it hurts, until they are healed.
de la brisure dou col	from the fracture of the collarbone
