Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And never should the leg be broken in this way with staples, as is done in the case of the arm; however, this restoration does not benefit the patient.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the leg is restored in 7 days, or slightly less or slightly more, depending on the diversity of dispositions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	from the street of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	You know that in the street of the knee there is little breakage, but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, even if it is only a crack or an opening, it affects every wound, and without a wound, and everyone feels well.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is when you put each part back in its place as much as possible; then apply the plaster, and insert a round stick if necessary, as you need for each fracture, such as an abscess high up or other similar cases; apply to each case what it requires, as long as it heals properly.
de la brisure de la jambe	from the fracture of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	You know that in the leg there are two bones, of which one is called the "tibula" and the other is called the "fibula"; and a fracture occurs in the leg just as it does in the arm, and its restoration is the same as for the arm equally, and all the work involves this. And if both bones are broken together, the leg returns to its original state from every direction.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the small bones are broken, they return to their original position.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the large bone is broken, it causes great pain, and one can see it well; then remove it from the socket.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	Then apply extension, and set it even, and tie the stars equally; but still, it is important to note that the break should be clean, and there should be multiple pieces, so that the extension is less severe and lighter; and align it according to your ability.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your task, take two strips of cloth that cover the leg on both sides, extending from the knee to the socket; then wrap two bandages around it and tie them in the middle as well, so that the leg cannot bend to the right or left, and thus is secure. And no one should administer anything along the length of the leg; it should be made of wood, and the leg wrapped to prevent movement. This is done properly at the site of the fracture, or wherever there is a wound or any other accident; and each day, move the leg to check for signs of abscess or other complications; treat it as long as it heals.
de la brisure des os dou piet	From the fracture of bones in the foot.
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle, there is no fracture, but the bones in the foot can be fractured and the joints can become stiff, and it occurs in various positions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if the bones in the foot are fractured and you see them intertwined with each other, the patient will feel such intense pain in their foot on the ground, as if they wanted to walk, then place your foot on theirs, raising the broken bones, and press gently until they return to their original position; then apply a splint and tape over it, placing a small, flat table under the stomach of the foot, securing the bandage tightly around the foot, and wrapping other things as needed.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And after three days or four have passed, if it loosens the bandage, for you will find the bones even, either broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if none of the bones are broken, but they are dislocated, as we have said about the hand's joints, then place a stick along the length of the bone, and make it slightly wider, and put under the foot that I mentioned, keeping it firmly in place; and if there are two or three, or more, broken bones, put on each bone a stick according to its amount, wrapped in a strip of linen, and fasten the bandage under the foot, keeping it well in place.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And you must not forget the other things I have said about other fractures, as we have mentioned; and treat each case as it should be.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	On the fracture of the bone of the hand.
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When a woman's bone in her hand is fractured and the swelling increases, then lean her body forward, supporting her from behind. Fill the hollow part of the fracture with cotton, as much as possible, and let it be so; then raise the woman up slightly and gently press on her back, bit by bit, until the cotton reaches the entrance to the bone, and the bone returns to its place. When she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and when she has finished, replace it, doing this for seven days or so. In this way, the fracture will be healed, and if you see that the swelling is gone, take a bladder of a goat and tie one end of a cane to the opening, then empty the entire bladder into the fracture; blow on the cane gently until the bladder is completely inflated inside. The nature of the bone will heal itself; then fill it with cotton again, and leave it like this for several days until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the bone of the hand or of the woman is broken, restore it as we have said regarding the bone of the wrist; and these breaks are not hidden from him who applies his study and skill, and heeds my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For these breaks indicate various dispositions for the right way of restoration; understand this therefore.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the staff, when it is broken, take a goose throat and insert it into the staff; then wrap it with cloth, leave it for three days or longer, and it will be healed naturally.
de brisure avec plaie	from fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is important for someone with a fracture and a wound, especially if it is significant, such as the bones of the leg or shoulder or similar, to seek medical attention now, so that the healing process we have described can take place.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, but there is still adhesion from scar tissue, if you have no other remedy, then begin to restore the fracture in the same hour or on the same day as the abscess formed, so it does not worsen.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if the abscess arises again, let it be allowed to heal completely for a new day, as long as the abscess is calm, and do not touch it for even a third or a fourth part of a day, because you might cause an ill effect.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is visible through the heart's opening, it is necessary that you place it gently in your hands, with a slight extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension does not appear suitable to place equally in your hands, take this instrument which is made of iron, with seven or eight parts long, and adjust its width according to the size of the wound; and for this, it is necessary that he immerses three or four times, according to what is needed for each fracture treatment; and be rounded and slightly thick, so that it does not bend under pressure on the member during your work, and be wider at the front, thicker in the middle towards the front, thus:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And it is called "palainche", so the dislocated joint must be placed back on top of the visible bone; and press firmly once, until it returns, and be even one against the other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is subtle, and the instrument cannot properly grasp the bone, then you must hold the head of the bone, until the instrument has a firm grip.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot bring the bone back as we have said, with a suitable instrument such as a chisel or saw, within your power, then remove what is delayed in the bone from harshness and small cuts.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is brought back, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, knowing that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	If you do everything to put it back in its natural place, then moisten the draping with black astringent wine, and arrange it properly; do not put any wax or other substances on the wound that could cause rot and corruption. Then administer stars (possibly medicines) when you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, removing the dressing around it according to the size of the wound, and be very careful not to constrict the wound with the bandaging; often, people have made this mistake and brought death or corrosion to the patient several times, so make the bindings softer and gentler than other injuries.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is bad or great, and you doubt that a worse accident may come, as we have said, and you feel pain in place, if it is not suitable to put on bandages; but wrap around, instead of bandages, hard cloths, and bind them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two days that the wound is becoming worse, then remove everything that you have put on top of it, and apply a healing dressing to the wound, such as a four-ingredient ointment or similar.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you dislocate the member two times a day, in the morning and in the evening, as long as it is swollen and healed.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limb be dislocated in such a way that the bow of the joint moves slightly downward.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if it persists for a long time, and it cannot heal but keeps dislocating, knowing that there are small fragments of bone, then you must open the wound with care, and remove all these loose pieces that cause the pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula forms in its place, or any other type of infection, it is necessary that you treat it, according to what is said in the chapter above.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when a bone is broken and open in the member, as the bone of the ankle or the shoulder, or other similar bones in the large members, do not pull it immediately, for many times death may come from it, but let it be until it decays; perhaps after 20 days or 30, then treat the wound, if you can; and if you cannot, leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	burns that come from the heat
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We often come after the healing of the burn, especially when it is near a joint, and it is a ugly sight to see the shape of the member; and by chance it cannot perform its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take care then, if we must administer astringent medicines such as aloes, incense, myrrh, sarcocolla, acacia, and similar others, either individually or in combination, and preserve them with vinous astringents or with abundance of heat or cold; place them on the wound in compresses, tighten them well, and do not loosen them for several days; then dislocate it and begin again with another until the inflammations are removed; or apply a piece of good plaster, because its property is to draw out all swellings from the limbs; and if the inflammation has already turned into hardness like stone, it must be removed, cutting off the excess above, and making the remainder appear healthy; or scrape it with a razor until it is removed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	The weak member after treatment.
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture of the bone is healed and the weak and delicate member remains, this can occur for many reasons: one is because it was bound too tightly and not properly aligned as it should be; or because there were too many bindings and it cannot assume the normal shape of the member; or due to excessive swelling; or from too great movements, not in their proper time; or because it has little blood in its body, making it weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the patient eat, and stretch the body, until the blood flow multiplies within it; then administer baths, give joy and rest; then apply lead to the member, so that the lead attracts great blood flow, and often rinse it with warm water, until the flow reaches the member; and it returns to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	The dislocated joint must be set straight after its healing.
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When a limb is twisted after healing, and the bones are broken open, and the shape of the limb is ugly, yet it does not lose its natural function: do not believe those who say one must break the member entirely new, and many foolish practices have been done in our land; and such actions are blameworthy, causing great harm, and perhaps death. However, if the sprains and torments are recent, they should be treated with hot water or softened herbs, such as chamomile leaves, roots, licorice, and similar things; and make an empowering plaster, well-prepared, taking the mucilage of chamomile and confiting it with gelatine fat or sesame oil, and applying it over; or take fig fat and crush it with colon powder and other medicines that reduce swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And never should the dislocation be rubbed continuously and for a long time with moist hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And allow the limb to move every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the stiffness is inflamed and hardened, like stone, it also needs to be released with iron, if necessary all the way to the bone, using a delicate incision; and apply compression and study in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book on dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocations come from a joint moving out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation occurs due to no apparent reason, it is necessary to bring the limb back to its normal position as soon as possible.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if one delays, the limb swells, and by chance if it is reset at a later time, it may cause pain in the joint; for this reason, it is not advisable to move it immediately when it is swollen. Often, this leads to inflammation and other pains; however, once the swelling has subsided, make the patient better, then leave it until the abscesses are healed; then apply hot water and oil, gently reset the limb, and treat each member as suitable for its condition.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters on dislocations of the upper limbs from the shoulder down to the hand.
des mandibules	and of the jaws.
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	It is often the case that the jaws become dislocated, and this dislocation occurs in two ways: either they are slightly out of their sockets, somewhat bent, or entirely dislocated, hanging down toward the chin, preventing the patient from closing his mouth, holding saliva, or speaking clearly with his tongue.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is minor, it often returns on its own due to the body's natural movements.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is whole and complete, then you must reset it hastingly, and not delay; and in such a way that the minister places the head with the sick person, and pulls the mirror gently from one of his hands to the root of the dislocation of the jaw inside the mouth, so that the dislocation is on both sides; and the other two hands should be extended equally; and command the patient to soften his jaws and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And he should place the mirror equally, until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it returns to its place, especially if both jaws are together, then apply hot water and oil, gently resetting it; do not delay in returning it, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are returned to their original position, and the mouth of the patient is closed comfortably with a mild dressing of rose oil and wax, then bind it gently with soft linen; and let the patient sleep on his back, with his legs between two pillows, so that he does not move them to either side, nor make any effort to open them wider, but eat light food and drink until the pain is gone and the jaws are healed; and then he can resume eating normally without opening his mouth too widely.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jaws cannot be restored to their proper position within an hour and do not return to their normal state, then there may follow fever and severe pain in the abdomen, and possibly vomiting of clear bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	And when you see this, then know that it is fatal; and many times it kills him who experiences it, within nine days.
de la forcelle	de la forcelle" translates to "of the fork
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The fork cannot stay steady from either side in the continuance of it, and is dislocated both better and worse, and is never healed properly outside, and causes great pain.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And its restoration is that the patient lies on his back and extends his arms; then he presses the joint into your palm, and it returns; then he applies the plaster and bandage, and tightens it; and the dislocation which is towards the shoulder cannot stay out of place; if not, and if it does not come out even once, if it is brought back to its place as we have said, then he applies the plaster and bandage, and tightens it, and commands the patient to rest until he is healed; and in this way, too, the dislocation of the shoulder is restored when it is in the right position.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	On dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	You know that the shoulder is dislocated in three ways: one is when it dislocates at the acromion end; and the second is at the part of the scapula; and sometimes it dislocates above, which is rare; and it does not dislocate behind the shoulder, nor inside towards the nerves; and often it dislocates away from the acromion towards the scapula, especially in those with little muscle, for them it happens severely; but in those with sufficient muscle, it dislocates slightly, and moves back slightly.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And sometimes it happens to certain men that they suffer a blow or fracture, and an abscess forms in the hot shoulder, and they think it is dislocated by that.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	You must therefore test it, until you are certain, and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And the dislocation is recognized when it turns towards the axis, and it distinguishes between the diseased shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find between them a clear difference; and you will find at the top of the shoulder a depression, and by pressing with your finger on the top of the shoulder, as if it were one bone, the patient cannot bring his hand to his side or move any part of it; and also, if it is dislocated upwards, and not concealed, as you can feel it clearly with your finger, this type of dislocation is not easily corrected, especially when it is new or the patient is in pain.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the method is that the healer should take the patient's hand and place it above the dislocated joint, then apply pressure from below, and lift the joint with force towards its proper position; and the healer should release the hand and extend it upwards, and place it beneath; this will bring relief.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	If the dislocation does not come off as we have said with strong hands after a few days, it is necessary that the patient be bathed in hot water; administer gently a soothing and softening treatment such as a decoction of althae and fenugreek and melilot in water, and then treat them. Then, place the patient on their back and put a soft cloth beneath the dislocated joint, neither too loose nor too tight, then position the heel against the cloth and gently lift the head of the shoulder; pull the hand of the patient with the dislocation away from their body, and another assistant should hold the head of the shoulder to prevent it from moving. The shoulder will return immediately, and if you see that it is properly aligned, know that this method has been successful: and it is important that there be a stronger person present who can handle the patient; place them directly against the side with the dislocated joint, and pull the shoulder away from the joint towards the belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, and any heavy thing is laid upon him, the dislocation returns now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And it is also adjusted in another way: take a long stick and insert it into the ground so that the end is as bright as a pistol, neither too thick nor too thin; then place it from beneath the patient, but with soft cloth above, and the patient's arm fully extended on the other side, and the joint will return to its place; and if it does not want to come back for all the reasons we have said, do this treatment: take a stick of two arms' length and four fingers' width that has a bright end, and push it entirely into the joint according to this form.
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then lay the patient flat on his back, so that the affected area is not disturbed, then remove all padding from the affected area; extend one arm above the head, and bind the limb to the affected body part, starting at the wrist of the hand, then place the arm on the wide edge of a board, extending the palm downwards, and leaving the body hanging from the other side: the joint will now be reset.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is set, in any way, it is necessary that you place under the padding a thin piece of wool equal in size, then apply the plaster with the powder from the mill, mixed with incense and egg white, over the entire shoulder and around, then remove the padding carefully, and wrap the bandage around the plaster, and press the hand against the collarbone, and let the hands remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that he move the dislocated part little by little, as long as the limb is comfortable, for it will heal faster; and then move it again after one or two days, and straighten it; and if it remains locked and is not softened, it will be healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is locked due to moisture or any other cause, it is necessary that you apply heat treatments at three openings, as described in the chapter on cautery.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this, and it loosens after seven days, and the joint does not hold, and the patient cannot raise his arm high, then know that the nerve at the top of the shoulder is either cut, stretched, or damaged; and know that the joint will never be fixed in its place again.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation that is towards the worst part, and the joints, or at the rear, if it occurs through a blow, and stretching of the hands, and is attended with great pain, then apply another remedy; and treat until it is healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And after healing comes cracking in the limb, and delays in movement; if the patient uses it many times, as long as this cracking persists, it will become lighter and return to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	on the cost of dislocation
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	You know that the dislocated joint is weakened at times, and then it returns; if it is dislocated from all sides, especially in front and behind, and the dislocation is not fully corrected, as one can see and feel it well; then it heals according to each shape.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the sick part with the healthy, if you can see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	Because the joint is dislocated, and he cannot bend his arm, nor touch his shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is necessary that you reset it in such a way that the abscess closes and it does not reopen, because if the abscess reopens, it will be difficult to reset, especially when it is at the back; then it is worse than other dislocations, and causes greater pain, and may even lead to death.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is, if it can be brought back, that you extend his hand with both of yours; and his arms should be spread out, and the palms facing each other, from side to side, and turn the joint at his fingers together, either towards his palm's root, until he returns to his place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, it returns when he doubles his hand to his palm, and turn the root of the palm's cut that is misaligned.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if it does not want to return to its place, apply strong extension; and have the other assistant extend the arm, and stretch it from both sides, so that it does not move at the extension; then turn each part of the arm, after you have wrapped a double-long and wide cloth; and when you look at the joint, rub it with no oil to soften the joint, then turn the joint firmly, until it returns; and once it is in place, apply dry plaster with egg white, pull the bandage tightly, and leave it for no days, then untie it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firm in its place and you loosen the ligament, leave it; and if you see that the joint does not hold well, repeat the splinting and the ligature, leaving it thus for several days until it is firmly placed, then loosen it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And if the patient feels better after resetting the joint and it becomes motionless, bathe and gently rub it, applying pressure until it is relieved; or place a grease-soaked woolen compress on the joint, leave it for one day and night, then remove it, and immerse it in a bath. And when it is warm, rub the joint appropriately, apply the compress again, and repeat this process twice or three times until it heals; and if you see that it remains healthy, apply fine, moist warmth with butter and press on it; it will return to its former state.
li dislocation de la main	The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The hand joint is misaligned and its return to normal is slight compared to other joints. However, it must be carefully reduced, immediately after dislocation, so that the swelling does not worsen or an abscess forms nearby.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	And when reducing it, place the patient's hand on a table, extend their fingers, and look to ensure they are even, so that the palm rests upon the joint's surface, holding it until it returns to its normal position. However, you must carefully observe if it is in the correct location; then place the patient's hand, with the back facing up, on a table for extension and reduction.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is on the back of the hand, have the patient lay their back on their hand on a table, and look closely at the appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it returns now, then it is indeed a sign. Otherwise, if the strain of soothing plasters on the abscess does not cease, and it leaves him without starting over again.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And if he cannot endure it, and you cannot put it back in place after any number of days, then the joint remains twisted; and it does not cause further harm to the patient as long as the hand is softened, and nothing can be extracted from it: then know that a nerve or an artery is damaged. There is no other device than cautery to extract it from this case, and perhaps there is nothing else of value.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is dislocated, if you place the splint as we have said, then pull it and leave it for a day, then loosen it and leave it so.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	If he cannot move it well and there is no fracture, then apply hot water moisture and rub it until it is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	On the dislocation of the fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	The fingers of the hand should never be dislocated at each joint, neither at the back of the palm or on the palm itself; then hold the finger, and gently pull the dislocation to its proper place, while supporting the base of the finger, and bend it towards the side where it is dislocated. Leave it in that position for a day, and then reset it the same way; do not bind it, but loosen it each day and move it, and then re-bind it; and do this often until it is tight, and also do so if it is dislocated on the palm of the hand, doing as you have done before, until it is healed; and do the same if it is dislocated on the other side.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	dislocation of the spine
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the spine or the column is dislocated, and there are multiple dislocations, if there is no cure, the patient dies quickly.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the signs are that the patient's movements are sudden and involuntary, he cannot hold them, and sometimes a limb becomes weak, or both legs or both arms, or even the spine is affected in three parts; the part that remains mute at the back is called "gibbousness". The cure, if the gibbousness has been present from childhood, is as follows: if there is no cure or treatment for all of it.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And that which comes from falling or impacts or similar things, the old ways of treatment speak in great words, but they do not bring much benefit to anyone; but I have abbreviated it according to my understanding and formed instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in the stiffness that comes to the penis, no one has a cure; and also that which comes straight to the side, and it is not possible to heal outside of that which properly comes to the back, as I say; and it is that the patient should be stretched on his face equally in the first position, and have strain from below, so that he does not bleed; then I insert a stick into the head in the earth-formed shape, and another at the heel, and tie a string around the afflicted parts, and another at the ankles, and at the knees, and at the ankles; and these ministers know the strings, one on the head and the others on the feet, among the two sticks; and they should be well fastened, the stick as we have said, and the observer places his palms on the formed spine until it returns.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if it does not return with this treatment, take a board three feet long, cut a groove in the wall from edge to edge, place the patient on their side, and turn the head of the board away from the wall; then place the center of the board over the spine, and put mirrors under both ends of the board, pressing firmly until it returns to its original position; and if you see it moving, do this with a stick that turns in your hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And take two long splints, one for the patient's head on the affected arm and two others for their feet; between each splint, make an incision from edge to edge, about a palm's length deep; and in each splint, have a hole through which the stick can turn, and let the splints be firmly fastened so they do not move; and between the two turning splints, place two small splints, each a palm's length, to turn the stick; then tie the one end of the stick that is among the bound pieces to the head splint, and the other end to the foot splint at the other turner, and let every minister turn his turner along all the bindings, and the master make the spine even as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	And when it is even, apply a drying plaster with plenty of heat, then the compresses, and then the end of a tablet three fingers long, which should adhere to the area of the stiffness and the healthy part of the spine, then bind it with a strap, as we have said, and use the patient's mild treatment until they are healed; and if any thing happens at the end of their healing, it is necessary to administer softening and soothing medicines, with the method that we have mentioned above; and never should one apply a piece of lead, nor does its appearance occur in the rear spine, and be careful that it is not dislocation; and it is the bone that opens, for which one must not have presumption, because it could bring about death.
des dislocations de la hainche	Of dislocations of the spine
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	You know that the joints of the hip and the joints of the shoulder only cause dislocations, unlike other joints; and the hip joint is misaligned according to four parts: inside and outside, front and back; and more inside, less misaligned in front and back.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the knowledge of its dislocation within is such that when you join the affected leg with the healthy one, the injured knee becomes longer and opens wider than the healthy one, and the patient cannot bend their kneecap; and it is the heat from the abscess that causes the swelling around the joint, because the joint of the thigh comes here.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of him who experiences this at death is such that this event is contrary to what has been said before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of him who experiences this beforehand are that his leg is well according to completion; however, do not bend the knee too much without pain, and if it is desired for him to walk, he cannot do so until later, and retains urine, and the ankle swells, and when he attempts to stand, he does so on the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of him who experiences this after are that he cannot extend or bend his knee, and one leg is more twisted than the other, and the ankle is softened, and the thigh remains in a position opposite to the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	They should reset this appearance of dislocation if it is that the dislocation is old and remains according to its disposition, as there is no cure; and he should have no presumptuousness.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And for the one where the dislocation is fresh, and it's one of the four types of dislocation, you must act swiftly to reset the joint, both internally and externally, and move it to the right and left; perhaps it will return, and no other cure is needed.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	If it does not return in this way, you must then apply a strong force, and firmly fasten the leg with two hands or bind it at the knee; another minister should extend his hand from above in such a manner that he pulls both of the patient's hands towards himself, then tightly grasp the heel with a firm hold; another should hold the head with the same firm grip; and all should simultaneously pull upward and downward until the patient is completely lifted off the ground and remains still.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is common to all four limbs, and if the dislocation returns, as we have said, it is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If the dislocation is in the joint nearest to the healthy side, it is necessary to place the patient on that side, then tie the affected limb at its root, and the opposite limb above the wound, and towards the strength; then ask another assistant to grasp the patient's arms, and embrace the large joint of the affected limb, extending it to a distant form; it will return to its place now; and this method of dislocation is lighter than others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	And if you cannot hold it in the manner we have said, then you should bind together both feet of the patient with a strong, soft ligature on both heels and both knees, and let the diseased leg be extended two fingers more than the others; then hang it from a post, and let it rest two arms' lengths above the ground; and command the assistant to embrace the top of the thigh, and have other assistants hanging with the patient, who embrace the thigh, for the joint will now come back together.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when the dislocation is external, if the patient lies as we have said in the case of a hunchback, then tightly draw the ligature on the diseased leg, both above and below; then place two hot coals, one at the top and one at the bottom, and insert a third between the thighs of the patient, along its shape; and surround it with moist cloths so that it does not harm the patient, and let each assistant extend towards him, and carefully place their hand on the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, that's good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If it does not return, place it on a table and press it as we have said in the previous passage, and lay the patient on his healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, it is necessary to stretch the affected leg forcibly, as I have said; and place the bandage so that the pain is not on the affected side, then press with the other hand, and extend it downwards towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation is in the joint, it does not suit to extend the patient down, nor to raise him up on his feet, but he should remain as if his hip was dislocated at the fire, just as we have said before gently on both hips; and on his face, and stretch the ligament as we have said above, and press on the joint on the table; and it will be correct when the patient extends his legs, and they are even; then adjust the thighs, and apply a splint, and tie a bandage so that the hip does not move; and rest for three or four days, then release, and put the splint back; and if you see that they are even, tighten as before, and leave it for three days; then release, and let him walk slowly, until the limb is comfortable.
de la dislocation dou genoil	From the dislocation of the knee
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The limb is dislocated in three ways: inwardly and outwardly, and also behind; but not forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the signs are that you command the patient to bend his leg at the knee, and if it does not return to its place at the knee, know that it is dislocated; and the restoration of all is that you make the patient sit upright and extend his leg if he can, and place him face down on your hands, and put his foot on yours. Then take the kneecap in your palms and pull between your fingers, then bend both sides of the knee joint; and another helper extends the patient's foot, until the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that it gently returns the leg to the knee slightly; and apply a poultice, and make the leg return to its position at the knee, and fasten it firmly together for three or four days, then release it; and let not the patient move about until the limb is comforted.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limb is not flexible enough, apply firm extension as we have said in the treatment of the spine, until it is healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	On the dislocation of the heel.
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heel is neither fully extended nor flexed, and it is dislocated both internally and externally.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the signs are that the ankle is swollen, and there is tenderness in the area where it is dislocated; the reduction is gentle, and one should lightly extend their hand towards the affected area when it is slightly flexed.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is dislocated slightly, you should make the patient lie straight, and hold the leg with both hands above the ankle; then take the foot in your right hand and pull it towards you twice, then stretch it up high and push the foot up nicely; do this twice more, alternating between pulling and stretching the foot; if it returns, that is good. If not, recommence the procedure, because it will return. And if it cannot be returned in this way, make the patient lie on their back on the ground, and insert a firm stick into the ground between their thighs, and wrap the sheets around them so they do not hurt; then have each assistant hold the healthy leg at its ankle, and another stretch the foot towards its side, while others keep the dislocation in place when it is pulled; then put each mirror over the dislocation in both hands, and a different assistant turn the healthy leg inward at the knee, and the dislocation will return more easily.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when the swelling has subsided, apply a poultice and compress it, stretch the limb, tie it to the leg, and hold the shoes behind the ankle so that the ligature is not too tight; then leave it for two or three days, and if the swelling improves, loosen the bandage on the third day or after a quarter; and he should be able to walk within four days; and if he goes beyond this time, it is not fortunate that he still suffers.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses form, it is necessary to soothe them, as we have said elsewhere, while they are fresh.
des dois	Of two things
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the eyes are dislocated, if they need to be nicely extended without strain, it is a light thing.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in any other part of the back or leg, it is necessary that you place the patient on a firm bed or table completely straight, and put your foot on what opens from these joints, then press with your foot firmly, until it returns; and when it is level and nothing opens, place under the sole of the foot a piece of wood split in two, then stretch strongly, and leave it for three days, then release it; and let it rest until it is healed.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	From wound and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound comes with dislocation and we wish to restore it, often the patient dies if you are not careful in treating it, especially if you are not experienced in the art or have not practiced it for long, and if you lack compassion and mercy and act too quickly; then leave the patient in God's hands, if you see no hope of recovery. But when there is hope, realign the limb immediately so that the abscess becomes hot, and treat the wound as appropriate, using dried herbs; and if the dislocation involves broken bones or small fragments, reduce them as we have said for simple fractures, and do not enter a path of fear, as I have advised, for this will guide you according to your Creator, and because of your knowledge of weapons and your body.
